Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
One Prostration for Multiple Recitations in One Sitting
Explains the ruling and proof for multiple prostration verses in one sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple recitations of a prostration verse in one sitting and explain the proof from the hadith of Jibril and the principle of tadakhul.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one sitting due to tadakhul fi al-sabab.

When a prostration verse is recited multiple times in one sitting, does each recitation require a separate prostration? The Hanafi school answers with a clear no. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, and the deeper legal concept of tadakhul (integration) that distinguishes acts of worship from penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is reciting or hearing the same prostration verse multiple times in one sitting. The Hanafi ruling is that one prostration is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The main proof is the hadith of Jibril, who would descend with revelation and recite the prostration verse to the Prophet, and the Prophet only prostrated once, even after reciting it to his companions.
This hadith is narrated by several Companions and is considered authentic.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's practice directly indicates that multiple recitations in one sitting are treated as one cause for prostration. Additionally, the principle of removing hardship (nafy al-haraj) supports this, especially for teachers and students.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a narration in al-Nawadir that no prostration is required. Al-Zahid al-Sarakhsi reconciles by interpreting the first position (one suffices) as when repetition occurs before breaking the sitting with speech, and the second as after speech.
This reconciliation shows the importance of defining 'sitting' (majlis).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that one prostration suffices. This is the view of the zahir al-riwayah, and it is supported by the hadith and the principle of tadakhul fi al-sabab.
Tadakhul in the cause means multiple occurrences are treated as a single cause.

ما إذا كان قبله ، فلو لم يسجدها في الصلاة حتى سجدها الآن قال في الأصل : أجزأه ههنا وهو محمول على ما إذا أعادها بعد السلام قبل الكلام لأنه لم يخرج عن حرمة الصلاة فكأنه كررها في الصلاة وسجد إذ لا يستقيم بالوحي فيقرأ آية السجدة على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورسول الله كان . يسمع ويتلفن ثم يقرأ على أصحابه وكان لا يسجد إلا مرة واحدة، وهو مروي عن عدة من الصحابة ولأن المجلس جامع المتفرقات ولأن في إيجاب السجدة لكل تلاوة حرجاً خصوصاً للمعلمين والمتعلمين وهو منفي بالنص. قيد بسجدة التلاوة لأن الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بأن سمعه أو ذكره في مجلس واحد مراراً فيها اختلاف، فبعضهم قاسها عليها، وبعضهم منعه وأوجبها لكل مرة لأنه من حقوق العباد ولا تداخل فيها وهو جفاء له كما ورد في الحديث وقدمنا ترجيحه. وأما تشميت من عطس في مجلس واحد مراراً فأوجبه بعضهم كل مرة والصحيح أنه إن زاد على الثلاث لا يشمته لما روي عن عمر رضي الله عنه أنه قال للعاطس في مجلسه بعد الثلاث قم فانتثر فإنك مزكوم. وفي المجتبى ولا خلاف في وجوب تعظيم اسمه تعالى عند ذكره في كل مرة، وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا تلا مراراً ثم سجد وما إذا تلا وسجد ثم تلا بعده مراراً في مجلس واحد وهو تداخل في السبب دون الحكم ومعناه أن يجعل التلاوة المتعددة كتلاوة واحدة تكون الواحدة منها سبباً والباقي تبع لها وهو ألبق بالعبادات إذ السبب متى تحقق لا يجوز ترك حكمه، ولهذا يحكم بوجوبها في موضع الاحتياط حتى تبرأ ذمته بيقين والتداخل في الحكم أليق في العقوبات لأنها شرعت للزجر فهو ينزجر بواحدة فيحصل المقصود فلا حاجة إلى الثانية . والفرق بينهما أن التداخل في السبب ينوب فيه الواحدة عما قبلها وعما بعدها، وفي التداخل في الحكم لا تنوب إلا عما قبلها حتى لو زنا ثم زنا في المجلس يحد ثانياً بخلاف حد القذف إذا أقيم مرة ثم قذفه مراراً لم يحد لأن العار قد اندفع بالأول لظهور كذبه . وقيد بكون الآية واحدة لأن من قرأ القرآن كله في مجلس واحد لزمه أربع عشرة سجدة لأن المجلس لا يجعل الكلمات المختلفة الجنس بمنزلة كلام واحد كمن أقر لإنسان بألف درهم ولآخر بمائه دينار ولعبده بالعتق لا يجعل المجلس الواحد الكل إقراراً واحداً، وكذا الحرج منتف. وأطلق في المجلس فشمل ما إذا طال فإنه لا يتبدل به حتى لو تلاها في الجامع في زاوية ثم تلاها في زاوية أخرى لا يجب عليه إلا سجدة واحدة، وكذلك حكم السماع، وكذلك البيت والمحمل والسفينة في حكم التلاوة والسماع، سواء كانت السفينة واقفة أو جارية، وكذلك لا يختلف بمجرد القيام ولا بخطوة وخطوتين وكلمة أو كلمتين ولا بلقمة أو لقمتين بخلاف ما إذا كان كثيراً وبخلاف ما إذا نام مضطجعاً أو باع ونحوه فإنه يتبدل المجلس، وكذا لو أرضعت صبياً. وكل عمل يعلم أنه قطع للمجلس بخلاف التسبيح ونحوه فإنه ليس بقاطع كالنوم قاعداً. وفي الدوس وتسدية الثوب ورحا الطحن والانتقال من غصن إلى غصن والسبح في نهر أو حوض يتكرر على الأصح، ولو كررها راكباً على الدابة وهي تسير يتكرر إلا إذا كان في الصلاة لأن الصلاة جامعة للأماكن إذ الحكم بصحة الصلاة دليل اتحاد المكان .
He prostrated another, and if he did not prostrate, or it does not suffice him, one [prostration] is sufficient, like one who repeats it in one sitting, not in two sittings, as a legal ruling. It was mentioned in al-Nawadir that it is not required of him. al-Zahid al-Sarakhsi reconciled between them by interpreting the first as when he repeats it after speech, and the second as when it is before it. If he did not prostrate in the prayer until now he prostrated it, he said in al-Asl: it suffices him here, and this is interpreted as when he repeats it after the salam before speech because he has not left the sanctity of prayer, so it is as if he repeated it in prayer and prostrated, because this answer is not valid when he repeats it after speech because the prayer nature has fallen from him by speech. Thus in al-Bada'i', and al-Tawfiq in al-Muhit corrected it. This indicates that the prayer nature is made up after salam before speaking, even if he does not do something that violates its sanctity. So it should be that their statement 'the prayer nature is not made up outside it' is qualified by this, and by 'outside' they mean outside its sanctity. His statement (like one who repeats it in one sitting not in two sittings) means one suffices him in the first but not the second. The basis for this is what was narrated that Jibril عليه السلام used to descend with revelation and recite the verse of prostration to the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم, and the Messenger would listen and recite it to his companions, and he would only prostrate once. This is narrated from several Companions. Also because the sitting gathers the dispersed things, and because making a prostration obligatory for every recitation would be a hardship especially for teachers and students, which is negated by the text. He qualified it by the prostration of recitation because salawat upon the Prophet when one hears or mentions him repeatedly in one sitting there is difference: some analogize it, some forbid and make it obligatory each time because it is from the rights of people and there is no تداخل in it, and it is rudeness to him as mentioned in the hadith and we have presented its preference. As for tasmit of one who sneezes in one sitting repeatedly, some made it obligatory each time, but the correct view is that if it exceeds three, do not tasmit him based on what was narrated from Umar رضي الله عنه that he said to the sneezer after three: 'Stand and blow your nose, for you have a cold.' In al-Mujtaba: there is no dispute about the obligation of venerating His name whenever mentioned. He said it generally, so it includes when he recites repeatedly then prostrates, and when he recites and prostrates then recites after that repeatedly in one sitting. This is تداخل in the cause not in the ruling. Its meaning is that multiple recitations are made like one recitation, one of them is the cause and the rest are followers, which is more fitting for acts of worship because when the cause is realized, its ruling cannot be abandoned. For this reason, it is ruled obligatory in the place of caution so that his liability is discharged with certainty. تداخل in the ruling is more fitting for penalties because they are legislated for deterrence; one instance deters him and achieves the purpose, so there is no need for the second. The difference between them is that in تداخل in the cause, the one substitutes for what came before and after, while in تداخل in the ruling, it only substitutes for what came before, so if he commits zina then commits zina in the same sitting, he is punished a second time, unlike the hadd of qadhf if it is executed once then he commits qadhf repeatedly, he is not punished because the disgrace has been warded off by the first due to the apparent lie. He qualified it by the verse being one because if someone reads the entire Quran in one sitting, he owes fourteen prostrations because the sitting does not make different types of words like one speech, like someone who acknowledges to one a thousand dirhams, to another a hundred dinars, and to his slave emancipation; the single sitting does not make all one acknowledgment. Also hardship is negated. He said generally about the sitting so it includes if it is long, for it does not change thereby, so if he recites it in one corner of the mosque then in another corner, he only owes one prostration. Similarly for hearing. Similarly for the house, the camel litter, and the ship in the ruling of recitation and hearing, whether the ship is stationary or moving. Similarly, it does not differ by mere standing, nor by one or two steps, nor by one or two words, nor by one or two morsels, unlike if it is much, and unlike if he sleeps lying down or sells and the like, for then the sitting changes. Similarly, if she breastfeeds a child. Every action known to break the sitting [changes it], unlike tasbih and the like, for it is not a breaker, like sleeping while sitting. For treading, weaving cloth, grinding, moving from branch to branch, swimming in a river or pool, it is repeated on the correct view. If he repeats it while riding an animal that is walking, it is repeated, except if he is in prayer because prayer unifies places, since the validity of prayer indicates the unity of place.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling on multiple recitations of a prostration verse in one sitting. It is a ruling with proof. The text begins by addressing a scenario: if someone recites a prostration verse multiple times in one sitting, one prostration suffices. However, if the recitations occur in separate sittings, multiple prostrations are required. The author then reconciles conflicting reports: in al-Nawadir it is said that multiple prostrations are not required, but al-Zahid al-Sarakhsi explains that if the repetition occurs after speaking (i.e., after breaking the sitting), then a new prostration is needed; if before speaking, one suffices. The text then discusses the case of not prostrating during prayer. If one recites a prostration verse in prayer and does not prostrate until after salam but before speaking, it suffices because the sanctity of prayer remains. The main proof is the hadith of Jibril, who would recite a prostration verse to the Prophet repeatedly but the Prophet only prostrated once. Also, the principle of removing hardship (حرج) supports this, especially for teachers and students. The passage then distinguishes between تداخل في السبب (integration in cause) versus تداخل في الحكم (integration in ruling). For acts of worship, integration in cause applies: multiple recitations are treated as one cause, so one prostration suffices. For penalties, integration in ruling applies: each offense is punished separately to deter. The text also defines what constitutes a single 'sitting' (مجلس). Actions that break the sitting include sleeping lying down, selling, long distances, etc. Actions like walking a few steps, eating a morsel, or tasbih do not break the sitting. The riding case is special: if the rider is in prayer, the prayer unifies the places, so one prostration suffices; if not in prayer, each recitation requires a prostration because the animal's movement changes the place.

Key Terms
التداخل (al-tadākhul): Integration or overlapping; in this context, whether multiple occurrences of a cause are treated as one for the ruling.
المجلس (al-majlis): A single sitting or gathering; defined by physical continuity and lack of significant interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a person recites the same prostration verse twice in one sitting, how many prostrations are required?
A) Two
B) One
C) No prostration
D) Depends on the number of recitations

Key Takeaway
One prostration suffices for repeated recitations of a prostration verse in one sitting due to tadakhul fi al-sabab.

Repeating Prostration in Two Rak'at: Abu Yusuf's Reversion
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sajdat al-tilawah repetition in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah when a prostration verse is recited in two rak'at, and explain why Abu Yusuf reverted from istihsan to qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for two rak'at by qiyas; each rak'ah requires its own by istihsan — a major Hanafi ikhtilaf.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the repetition of a prostration verse across two rak'at. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two views: Abu Yusuf's final position (qiyas) that one prostration is enough, and his initial position (istihsan), also held by Muhammad, that each recitation demands a separate prostration. We explore the reasoning behind each and the broader phenomenon of Abu Yusuf reverting from istihsan to qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The prosthesis verse is recited in two rak'at of the same prayer. Determine whether the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah is repeated or resolved.
The scenario assumes the person is riding in prayer (salat al-ridaf) with a walking boy; the boy is not in prayer so his obligation repeats.
2
State the qiyas position
According to qiyas, one prostration suffices for two rak'at. This is Abu Yusuf's final view.
The reasoning is that the prayer unifies the separate rak'at, making them one continuous act.
3
State the istihsan position
According to istihsan, each rak'ah requires a separate prostration. This was Abu Yusuf's first view and is also Muhammad's view.
The reasoning is that each rak'ah is a distinct unit of worship; transitioning to a new rak'ah changes the place of recitation.
4
Understand the methodological shift
Abu Yusuf initially followed istihsan but later reverted to qiyas. This is one of three such reversals he made.
The second case involved a pledge (rahn) for mahr al-mithl; the third is not mentioned here but is known in Hanafi sources.
5
Note the practical consequence
If a person follows Muhammad's view, two prostrations are required; if they follow Abu Yusuf's final view, one suffices. The mufta bihi is not fixed in this passage.
Some later Hanafi works adopt the qiyas view as the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : إذا كان معه غلام يمشي وهو في الصلاة راكباً وكررها تكرر الوجوب على الغلام دون الراكب. وهذا إذا كان في ركعة واحدة، وأما إذا كان كررها في ركعتين فالقياس أن تكفيه واحدة وهو قول أبي يوسف الأخير، وفي الاستحسان أن يلزمه لكل تلاوة سجدة وهو قول أبي يوسف الأول وهو قول محمد. وهذه المسائل الثلاث التي رجع فيها أبو يوسف عن الاستحسان إلى القياس : إحداها هذه والثانية أن الرهن بمهر المثل لا يكون رهناً بالمتعة قياساً وهو قول أبي يوسف الأخير، وفي الاستحسان أن يكون رهناً بها وهو قوله الأول وقول محمد.
They said: If he has a boy walking while he is riding in prayer and he repeats it, the obligation is repeated for the boy but not for the rider. This is if it is in one rak'ah. As for if he repeats it in two rak'ahs, the qiyas is that one suffices him, and this is the latter opinion of Abu Yusuf. In istihsan, each recitation requires a prostration, and this is the first opinion of Abu Yusuf and the opinion of Muhammad. These are the three cases in which Abu Yusuf reverted from istihsan to qiyas: one of them is this; the second is that a pledge (rahn) of mahr al-mithl is not a pledge for the mut'ah (dower) by qiyas, and this is the latter opinion of Abu Yusuf; in istihsan, it is a pledge for it, and this is his first opinion and the opinion of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the repetition of a prostration verse in two rak'at (units of prayer). The text begins with a scenario: if a person is riding in prayer (salat al-ridaf) and has a boy walking beside him, and the rider recites a prostration verse multiple times in one rak'ah, the obligation of prostration is repeated for the boy (because he is not in the unifying effect of prayer) but not for the rider (because prayer unifies the place). Then, the key dispute: if the rider repeats the prostration verse in two rak'at (i.e., once in the first rak'ah and once in the second), what is the ruling? According to qiyas (analogy), one prostration suffices; this is the latter opinion of Abu Yusuf. According to istihsan (juristic preference), each recitation requires a separate prostration; this is the first opinion of Abu Yusuf and the opinion of Muhammad al-Shaybani. The text then mentions that this is one of three cases where Abu Yusuf reverted from istihsan to qiyas. The second case is about a woman who is given a pledge (rahn) in place of mahr al-mithl (proper dower) for her mut'ah (temporary marriage). The third case, which is not explicitly mentioned here but implied. The passage highlights a methodological difference: Abu Yusuf initially followed istihsan but later adopted qiyas, while Muhammad maintained istihsan. The commentary in the original work (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) discusses the reasoning: qiyas (one prostration suffices) is based on the idea that sitting is one, but istihsan argues that each rak'ah is a separate act of worship, and the transition to another rak'ah changes the place, so multiple prostrations are needed. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school is the one adopted for fatwa, which is not explicitly stated here but later scholars may have preferred one.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here it is the basis for the ruling that one prostration suffices for two rak'at.
الركعة (al-rak'ah): A unit of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf's final position (the one he reverted to), how many prostrations are required if a prostration verse is recited in two rak'at?
A) One prostration
B) Two prostrations
C) Fourteen prostrations
D) No prostration

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's reversion from istihsan to qiyas in the case of prostration in two rak'at underscores the dynamic nature of Hanafi legal reasoning; both positions remain part of the school's internal discourse.

The Single Majlis for Sajdah Tilawah: Definition and Break Points
Definition of a single majlis for sajdah tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a single majlis for sajdah tilawah and identify the actions that break or preserve the unity of the majlis.

Core Idea
A single majlis unifies repeated recitations of sajdah ayahs unless a severing action occurs.

Sajdah tilawah is wajib upon reciting or hearing an ayah of sajdah. But if you recite the same ayah multiple times, how many sajdahs are due? The answer depends on whether the recitations occurred in a single majlis (sitting). This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of a single majlis, exploring what actions preserve continuity and what actions break it.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
If a sajdah ayah is recited or heard multiple times in a single majlis, only one sajdah is required. Identify this as the baseline ruling.
The passage begins by affirming this rule and then defines the majlis.
2
Define the majlis as a legal concept
The majlis is not defined by time or exact location but by the continuity of place and absence of significant interrupting actions. Even movement within the same building (e.g., mosque) does not break it.
The text gives examples: moving between corners of a mosque, different rooms in a house, or being on a ship.
3
Identify actions that break the majlis
Actions that clearly sever continuity include: sleeping lying down, selling, breastfeeding a child, and excessive movement (e.g., many steps, moving to another room). List these from the text.
Minor actions like standing, a few steps, a few words, or a few bites do NOT break it.
4
Analyze ambiguous cases
Activities like trampling, weaving, grinding, moving between branches, or swimming are considered to repeat the sajdah (i.e., break the majlis) according to the most correct view.
The text labels these as 'يتكرر على الأصح'.
5
Apply the rider and prayer cases
For a rider on a moving animal, recitation repeats unless in prayer, because prayer unifies places. The two-rak'ah case is disputed: qiyas says one sajdah suffices (Abu Yusuf's latter view), istihsan says a sajdah for each rak'ah (Muhammad and Abu Yusuf's earlier view).
The mufta bihi is the qiyas position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يحد لأن العار قد اندفع بالأول لظهور كذبه . وقيد بكون الآية واحدة لأن من قرأ القرآن كله في مجلس واحد لزمه أربع عشرة سجدة لأن المجلس لا يجعل الكلمات المختلفة الجنس بمنزلة كلام واحد كمن أقر لإنسان بألف درهم ولآخر بمائه دينار ولعبده بالعتق لا يجعل المجلس الواحد الكل إقراراً واحداً، وكذا الحرج منتف. وأطلق في المجلس فشمل ما إذا طال فإنه لا يتبدل به حتى لو تلاها في الجامع في زاوية ثم تلاها في زاوية أخرى لا يجب عليه إلا سجدة واحدة، وكذلك حكم السماع، وكذلك البيت والمحمل والسفينة في حكم التلاوة والسماع، سواء كانت السفينة واقفة أو جارية، وكذلك لا يختلف بمجرد القيام ولا بخطوة وخطوتين وكلمة أو كلمتين ولا بلقمة أو لقمتين بخلاف ما إذا كان كثيراً وبخلاف ما إذا نام مضطجعاً أو باع ونحوه فإنه يتبدل المجلس، وكذا لو أرضعت صبياً. وكل عمل يعلم أنه قطع للمجلس بخلاف التسبيح ونحوه فإنه ليس بقاطع كالنوم قاعداً. وفي الدوس وتسدية الثوب ورحا الطحن والانتقال من غصن إلى غصن والسبح في نهر أو حوض يتكرر على الأصح ، ولو كررها راكباً على الدابة وهي تسير يتكرر إلا إذا كان في الصلاة لأن الصلاة جامعة للأماكن إذ الحكم بصحة الصلاة دليل اتحاد المكان . قالوا : إذا كان معه غلام يمشي وهو في الصلاة راكباً وكررها تكرر الوجوب على الغلام دون الراكب. وهذا إذا كان في ركعة واحدة، وأما إذا كان كررها في ركعتين فالقياس أن تكفيه واحدة وهو قول أبي يوسف الأخير، وفي الاستحسان أن يلزمه لكل تلاوة سجدة وهو قول أبي يوسف الأول وهو قول محمد.
It is not defined because the shame has been repelled by the first due to the appearance of his lie. It is restricted to one ayah because whoever recites the entire Quran in one sitting is obligated fourteen sajdahs because the sitting does not make different types of words like one speech, just as if one acknowledges owing one thousand dirhams to a person and one hundred dinars to another and the freedom of his slave, the single sitting does not make all of it one acknowledgment, and similarly there is no difficulty. It is unrestricted regarding the sitting, so it includes when it is long; it does not change by it, so even if he recites it in the mosque in one corner then recites it in another corner, only one sajdah is obligated on him, and similarly the ruling of hearing, and likewise the house, litter, and ship in the ruling of recitation and hearing, whether the ship is stationary or moving. And likewise it does not differ by mere standing, nor by one or two steps, nor one or two words, nor one or two mouthfuls, unlike if it is much, and unlike if he sleeps lying down or sells something and the like, for then the sitting changes, and similarly if she breastfeeds a child. Every action known to interrupt the sitting, unlike glorification and the like, for it is not a discontinuer, like sitting sleep. Regarding trampling, warping the cloth, grinding, moving from branch to branch, and swimming in a river or basin, it repeats according to the most correct. If he repeats it while riding an animal that is walking, it repeats unless he is in prayer, because prayer unifies places since the ruling of the validity of prayer indicates unity of place. They said: If he has a boy walking while he is riding in prayer and he repeats it, the obligation repeats for the boy but not the rider. This is if in one rak'ah. But if he repeats it in two rak'ahs, analogy is that one suffices him, and that is the latter opinion of Abu Yusuf, and by istihsan each recitation requires a sajdah, that is the first opinion of Abu Yusuf and the opinion of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof by analogy regarding the definition of a single majlis (sitting) for sajdah tilawah. The author explains that if a person recites the same ayah of sajdah multiple times within one sitting, only one sajdah is required, because the sitting unifies the recitations. He clarifies that even a long sitting or moving within the same building does not break the majlis. Actions that definitely break the majlis include lying down to sleep, selling, breastfeeding a child, and excessive movement. Minor actions like standing, a few steps, a few words, or a few bites do not break it. For activities like trampling, weaving, grinding, moving between branches, or swimming, the most correct view is that each instance is separate (i.e., multiple sajdahs). The case of a rider: if he recites while riding and the animal is moving, he repeats the sajdah unless he is in prayer, because prayer unifies the place. The text concludes with the intra-madhab difference regarding two rak'ahs: Abu Yusuf later adopted qiyas (one sajdah suffices) while Muhammad and Abu Yusuf's earlier view follow istihsan (sajdah for each recitation).

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The sitting or location in which a person recites or hears an ayah of sajdah; unity of majlis prevents multiple sajdahs for repeated recitations.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A juristic preference that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) due to a stronger reason, here requiring a sajdah for each recitation in two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites a sajdah ayah in one corner of a mosque, then walks to another corner and recites it again, how many sajdahs are required?
A) One sajdah, because the mosque is one place.
B) Two sajdahs, because the location changed.
C) Depends on the distance.
D) None, because the recitation is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A single majlis for sajdah tilawah is defined by continuity of place and absence of significant interrupting actions; minor movements and same-location recitations require only one sajdah.

Abu Yusuf's Retraction from Istihsan to Qiyas in Three Issues
Lists three intra-Hanafi cases where Abu Yusuf changed from istihsan to qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three issues where Abu Yusuf retracted from istihsan to qiyas and state the mufta bihi position for the sajdah tilawah case.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf retracted from istihsan to qiyas in three specific cases; the relied-upon view follows qiyas.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details three famous issues where Imam Abu Yusuf changed his ruling from istihsan (juristic preference) to strict qiyas (analogy). Understanding these examples illuminates how Hanafi imams weighed evidence and how later authority settled on the stronger view. The first issue concerns the number of sajdah tilawah required when one recites an ayah of sajdah in two separate rak'ahs of the same prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three issues
The passage lists: (1) sajdah tilawah in two rak'ahs, (2) a pledge for mahr al-mithl, (3) a slave's crime less than homicide.
2
For each issue, note Abu Yusuf's earlier and later positions
Earlier view used istihsan, later view used qiyas. For issue 1: earlier and Muhammad said two sajdahs, later said one.
3
Understand the reasoning behind the change
The text implies that the later view (qiyas) became the relied-upon one because it aligns with the unity of prayer.
The tarjih mentions al-Hidayah and al-Fath al-Qadir.
4
Apply the tarjih for the first issue
The mufta bihi is: one sajdah suffices for two recitations in the same prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه المسائل الثلاث التي رجع فيها أبو يوسف عن الاستحسان إلى القياس : إحداها هذه والثانية أن الرهن بمهر المثل لا يكون رهناً بالمتعة قياساً وهو قول أبي يوسف الأخير، وفي الاستحسان أن يكون رهناً بها وهو قوله الأول وقول محمد. والثالثة إذا جنى العبد جناية فيما دون النفس واختار المولى الفداء ثم مات المجني عليه، القياس أن يخير المولى ثانياً وهو قوله الأخير وفي الاستحسان لا يخير وهو قوله الأول وقول محمد. بدل الواو أي أن قولهم الصلاتية لا تقضى خارجها، إما أن يقيد بهذه الصورة أي تخصيص منه هذه الصورة وإما أن يراد بخارجها خارج حرمتها قوله : (وكذلك البيت قال في النهر : إلا إذا كان كبيراً كدار السلطان . قوله : (فالحاصل أن اختلاف المجلس حقيقي الخ وكذا اتحاده حقيقي كالبيت ونحوه وحكمي كما لو أكل لقمتين أو مشى خطوتين كما في النهر قوله : (وقد يقال إن الأولى (الخ قال الرملي : المبادرة أولى في العبادة ولا يمنع منه قول البعض لضعفه بالنسبة إلى الظاهر تأمل ا هـ . ومثله في شرح الشيخ إسماعيل وقال : لا سيما إذا كان بعض الحاضرين محتمل الذهاب قبل التمام كما يتفق في الدروس فإنه ربما لا يأتي بها، وقد يتوهم لعدم سجود المعلم عدم الوجوب والاحتياط العمل بأقوى الدليل فالأولى أن يبادر قوله : (فعلى من تلاها مرتين سجدة واحدة الخ قال الرملي أي غير السجدة الصلاتية إذ لا كلام في وجوبها، وقوله وعلى صاحبه سجدتان أي خارج الصلاة كذلك فيكون عليه ثلاث سجدات، وهذه رواية النوادر ، وكلام هذا الشارح يدل على أنه فهم من كلام القنية أنه لا يجب على
These are the three issues in which Abu Yusuf retracted from istihsan to qiyas: the first is this [the sajdah in two rak'ahs]; the second is that a pledge (rahn) for the mahr al-mithl is not a pledge for the mut'ah by qiyas, and it is the latter opinion of Abu Yusuf, and by istihsan it is a pledge for it, which is his first opinion and the opinion of Muhammad. The third: if a slave commits an offense less than homicide and the master chooses ransom, then the victim dies, by qiyas the master is given a second choice, which is his latter opinion, and by istihsan he is not given a choice, which is his first opinion and the opinion of Muhammad. In place of the waw, meaning that their saying 'the prayer-related ones' are not performed outside of it, either it is restricted to this form, i.e., specifying that form, or it is intended by 'outside it' outside its sanctity. His saying: 'and likewise the house,' he said in al-Nahr: unless it is large like the sultan's house. His saying: 'the conclusion is that the difference of the sitting is real and likewise its unity is real like the house and its like, and legal like if he ate two mouthfuls or walked two steps as in al-Nahr.' His saying: 'and it may be said that the first [preference is...]' al-Ramli said: Promptness is better in worship and the saying of some does not prevent it because of its weakness compared to the apparent, reflect. And similarly in the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il and he said: especially if some of the attendees are likely to leave before completion, as occurs in lessons, for perhaps he will not do it, and it may be thought due to the teacher not prostrating that it is not obligatory, and precaution is to act on the strongest evidence, so promptness is better. His saying: 'so on the one who recited it twice, one sajdah...' al-Ramli said: i.e., besides the prayer-related sajdah, for there is no dispute about its obligation, and his saying 'and on his companion two sajdahs' i.e., outside prayer, so that means three sajdahs on him, and this is a narration of al-Nawadir, and the commentary of this sharh indicates that he understood from the Qunyah that it is not obligatory on...
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute detailing the three issues where Imam Abu Yusuf changed his ruling from istihsan (juristic preference) to qiyas (analogy). The first issue is the one just discussed: the obligation of sajdah tilawah when reciting in two rak'ahs. Abu Yusuf's latter view (qiyas) says one sajdah suffices, while his earlier view and Muhammad say each recitation requires its own sajdah (istihsan). The second issue concerns a pledge (rahn): if a woman pledges something for her mahr al-mithl, is it also a pledge for the mut'ah (consolation gift)? By qiyas, it is not; by istihsan, it is. The third issue: if a slave commits a crime less than killing, the master pays ransom, then the victim dies; by qiyas, the master gets a second choice (to pay or surrender the slave); by istihsan, he does not. The text then includes secondary discussions about the definition of majlis and whether to perform sajdah promptly when teaching, with the preferred view being promptness.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning that brings new cases under an existing ruling due to shared cause; Abu Yusuf retracted to qiyas in these three issues.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that abandons qiyas in favor of a stronger evidence or maslaha; here it required multiple sajdahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Sajdah tilawah in two rak'ahs
B) A pledge for mahr al-mithl
C) The sale of a slave
D) A slave's crime less than homicide

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf retracted from istihsan to qiyas in three specific issues, and the later school adopted qiyas as the mufta bihi view for the sajdah tilawah case.

Repetition of Sajda Tilawa Due to Change of Council
Expansion on repetition of sajda tilawa due to change of council

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of ikhtilaf al-majlis to determine when multiple sajda tilawa become obligatory for the reciter and listener.

Core Idea
The obligation of sajda tilawa repeats only when the council changes—real or virtual.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about when the prostration of recitation (sajda tilawa) must be repeated. The key is the concept of 'ikhtilaf al-majlis' (change of council). Understanding this distinction—real vs. virtual change—is essential for correctly applying the rulings in various scenarios, such as reciting or hearing a prostration verse multiple times in one sitting. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the reasoning and settles on Qadikhan's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The issue is whether repeating a prostration verse in one sitting requires multiple prostrations. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the reciter (tali) and listener (sami').
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; all agree on the basic wajib status of sajda tilawa.
2
Define the cause and condition
The cause (sabab) for sajda tilawa is the recitation itself; hearing is merely a condition (shart). Rulings attach to causes, not conditions.
This distinction is critical: multiplicity of hearing does not necessarily create multiplicity of obligation.
3
Apply the concept of ikhtilaf al-majlis
A change of council can be real (moving physically) or virtual (changing action). For the reciter, repeated recitation in one council is treated as a single act virtually, so only one prostration is wajib. For the listener, multiplicity of hearing is considered actual, so obligation repeats if the council changes.
The virtual unity applies only to the reciter, not the listener.
4
Work through the examples
From the text: a rider hearing a verse, then the mount moves and hears again – two prostrations. If he descends and recites another, another is added. Also, the weaver example from Fath al-Qadir illustrates when repetition does not occur.
Each scenario tests the boundaries of 'council change'.
5
Identify the tarjih and reliance
The author presents Qadikhan's fatwa as the relied-upon view: each change of council (real or virtual) triggers a new wajib. However, caution is advised due to scholarly difference.
Qadikhan's view aligns with zahir al-riwaya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا صلى على الأرض وقرأ آية السجدة في ركعتين لو سمعها المصلي الراكب من رجل ثم سارت الدابة ثم سمعها ثانياً عليه سجدتان هو الصحيح لأنها ليست بصلاتية، ولو سارت الدابة ثم نزل فتلاها أخرى يلزمه أخرى. كذا في المحيط . وفي فتح القدير : واعلم أن تكرار الوجوب في التسدية بناء على المعتاد في بلادهم من أنها أن يغرس الحائك خشبات يسوي فيها السدى ذاهباً ،وآيباً أما على ما هي ببلاد الإسكندرية وغيرها بأن يديرها على دائرة عظمى وهو جالس في مكان واحد فلا يتكرر الوجوب أهـ. فالحاصل أن اختلاف المجلس حقيقي باختلاف المكان وحكمي باختلاف الفعل، ولو تبدل مجلس السامع دون التالي تكرر الوجوب على السامع واختلفوا في عكسه والأصح أنه لا يتكرر على السامع لأن السبب في حقه التلاوة والسماع شرط يتكرر الوجوب عليه لأن الحكم يضاف إلى السبب لا الشرط. وإنما تكرر الوجوب عليه في المسألة الأولى مع اتحاد مجلس السبب لأن الشرع أبطل تعدد التلاوة المتكررة في حق التالي حكماً لاتحاد مجلسه لا حقيقة فلم يظهر ذلك في حق السامع فاعتبرت حقيقة التعدد فتكرر الوجوب، فعلى هذا يتكرر على السامع، إما بتبدل مجلسه أو بتبدل مجلس التالي. وفي القنية : تلا آية السجدة ويريد أن يكررها للتعليم في المجلس فالأولى أن يبادر فيسجد ثم يكرر .اهـ. وقد يقال : إن الأولى أن يكررها ثم يسجد آخراً لما أن بعضهم قال : إن التداخل في الحكم لا في السبب حتى لو سجد للأولى ثم أعادها لزمته أخرى كحد الشرب والزنا. نقله في المجتبي. فالاحتياط على هذا التأخير كما لا يخفى . وفي القنية أيضاً : ولو صليا على الدابة فقرأ أحدهما آية السجدة في الصلاة مرة والآخر في صلاته مرتين كلاهما من صاحبه فعلى من تلاها مرتين سجدة واحدة خارج الصلاة وعلى صاحبه سجدتان اهـ. وقد يقال : بل الواجب على من تلاها مرتين سجدتان أيضاً صلاتية بتلاوته وسمع وخارجية بتلاوة صاحبه. ثم رأيته بحمد الله تعالى في فتاوى قاضيخان أن على كل منهما سجدتين صلاتية بتلاوته وخارجية بسماعه من صاحبه وأطال الكلام في بيانه فراجعه .
And upon this difference, if he prayed on the ground and recited a verse of prostration in two rak'ahs, if a praying rider heard it from a man, then the mount walked, then he heard it a second time, two prostrations are obligatory upon him; that is correct because they are not prayer-related. And if the mount walked, then he descended and recited another, another is obligatory upon him. Thus in al-Muhit. And in Fath al-Qadir: Know that repetition of obligation in the arrangement is based on the custom in their land that the weaver erects sticks, going and returning, but according to what is in Alexandria and elsewhere that he rotates it on a large circle while sitting in one place, the obligation is not repeated. End. So the conclusion is that change of council is real by change of place and virtual by change of action. If the council of the listener changes without the reciter, the obligation is repeated upon the listener, and they differed about the opposite, and the most correct is that it is not repeated upon the listener because the cause in his case is the recitation, and hearing is a condition; the obligation is repeated upon him because the ruling is attributed to the cause, not the condition. And the obligation is only repeated upon him in the first case despite the unity of the council of the cause because the Law negated the multiplicity of repeated recitation in the case of the reciter virtually due to the unity of his council, not actually, so that did not appear in the case of the listener, so the actual multiplicity is considered, so the obligation is repeated. So upon this, it is repeated upon the listener, either by change of his council or by change of the reciter's council. And in al-Qunya: He recited a verse of prostration and wants to repeat it for teaching in the council, so it is preferable to hasten to prostrate, then repeat. End. And it may be said: It is preferable to repeat it, then prostrate last, because some said that overlapping is in the ruling, not in the cause, so that if he prostrated for the first and then repeated it, another became obligatory, like the hadd of drinking and adultery. Transmitted in al-Mujtabi. So caution is on this delay, as is not hidden. And in al-Qunya also: If two prayed on a mount, and one recited the verse of prostration in prayer once, and the other in his prayer twice, each from his companion, then the one who recited twice has one prostration outside prayer, and his companion has two prostrations. End. And it may be said: Rather, the obligatory upon the one who recited twice is also two prostrations, prayer-related by his recitation and external by his companion's recitation. Then I saw, by the praise of Allah, in the Fatawa of Qadikhan, that each of them has two prostrations: prayer-related by his recitation and external by his hearing from his companion, and he spoke at length in its explanation, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the conditions under which the obligation of sajdat al-tilawa is repeated. The author presents a chain of reasoning: the key factor is whether the 'council' (majlis) changes, which can be real (by moving to a different place) or virtual (by changing the action, e.g., engaging in a different activity). For the reciter, if he repeats the same verse in one sitting, only one prostration is required due to virtual unity of council. For the listener, however, the situation is different: hearing is a condition, not the cause, so multiplicity of hearing can trigger multiple obligations. The passage then cites al-Qunya and a view from Qadikhan to illustrate the preferred practice. The core of the discussion is a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of repeated recitation and hearing on the obligation to prostrate.

Key Terms
اختلاف المجلس (ikhtilaf al-majlis): Change of the sitting/council; can be real (by physically moving) or virtual (by changing the action, e.g., from reciting to listening or doing something else). This concept affects the obligation of sajdat al-tilawa: if the council changes, the obligation to prostrate is renewed upon repeated recitation or hearing in the new council.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the mount scenario from Qadikhan's fatwa, how many prostrations does each rider perform?
A) The rider who recited twice: 1 prostration; his companion: 2
B) Both riders: 2 prostrations each
C) The rider who recited twice: 2; his companion: 1
D) Both riders: 1 prostration each

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sajda tilawa repeats only when the council changes—real or virtual—and the listener's obligation is triggered by a change in either his own or the reciter's council.

Manner of Sajdat al-Tilawa: Takbirs, Supplications, and Standing
Describes the manner of sajdat al-tilawa with its sunnah acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions in sajdat al-tilawa and explain why tashahhud and taslim are omitted.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawa is performed like a prayer prostration but without tahrimah, tashahhud, or taslim.

The prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa) has a specific manner that differs from the prostration in regular prayer. While its obligation (wujub) is established, the details of how to perform it—such as the number of takbirs, whether to raise hands, and what supplications to recite—are explained in this passage. Understanding these details ensures the prostration is performed in accordance with the sunnah, even though it is not a complete prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions and exception
The prostration requires the conditions of prayer (e.g., purity, facing qibla) except the opening takbir (tahrimah). This is the first key point: the act is not initiated with a tahrimah.
The exception of tahrimah is stated at the beginning.
2
List the two takbirs and their status
Two takbirs are performed: one for lowering to prostration (takbirat al-wad') and one for rising (takbirat al-raf'). Both are sunnah, based on the Prophet's action reported in Sunan Abi Dawud.
Hands are not raised because these takbirs are for bending, not for entering prayer.
3
Explain omission of tashahhud and taslim
No tashahhud or taslim is recited. The reason: taslim is for exiting prayer, which requires a prior tahrimah. Since there is no tahrimah, there is no need for tahlil (dissolution).
This distinguishes it from a full prayer prostration.
4
Describe the recommended supplications
The most correct (asahh) supplication is saying 'Subhana al-A'la' three times, similar to the prostration in prayer. However, if the prostration is part of an obligatory prayer, one says 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la'; if supererogatory, one may say other reported supplications like 'Sajada wajhi...' or the longer du'a including 'Allahumma uktub li...'.
Outside prayer, any transmitted supplication is acceptable.
5
Note the recommendation to stand before prostrating
It is recommended (mustahab) to stand first and then prostrate, because falling down is from a standing position and the Quranic verses mention falling down. This is reported from Aisha. If one prostrates without standing, it is still valid but not preferred.
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj's view that one does not stand if already sitting is contrary to the relied-upon madhhab position.

His statement: 'And its manner is that he prostrates with the conditions of prayer between two takbirs without raising hands, tashahhud, and taslim.' That is, the manner of the prostration, and we have stated that the takbir tahrimah is excepted from the conditions of prayer. The two takbirs mean the takbir for placing and the takbir for raising, and each of them is sunnah, as verified in al-Bada'i from the hadith of Abu Dawud in the Sunan from his action, peace be upon him, in that manner. He does not raise his hands at the takbir because this takbir is done for bending down, not for tahrimah, as in the prostration of prayer, and similarly the takbir for raising as in the prostration of prayer, and that is transmitted from his action, peace be upon him, and Ibn Mas'ud after him. He does not perform tashahhud or taslim because it is for tahlil, and that requires prior tahrimah, which is absent. They differed about what to say in this prostration, and the most correct is that he says 'Subhana al-A'la' three times like the prostration of prayer, and does not reduce from it. It should not be taken as general, because if it were a prostration in prayer, if it is obligatory, he says 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la', or if supererogatory, he says what he wishes of what is reported, like 'Sajada wajhi li alladhi khalaqahu' etc. And his saying: 'Allahumma uktub li biha indaka ajran, wada' anni biha wizran, waj'alha li indaka dhukhran, wa taqabbalha minni kama taqabbalta min abdika Dawud' And if outside prayer, he says all that is transmitted. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. Among the recommended things for its performance is that he stands and prostrates because falling is from standing, and the Quran came with it, and it is narrated from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, and if he does not do so, it does not harm him. What occurred in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that if he is sitting, he does not stand for it, is contrary to the madhhab. In al-Mudmarat: It is recommended to stand and prostrate, and stand after raising the head from the prostration, and not sit. End. And the second is strange. And it is mentioned in al-Qunya that he stands for it even if many, and he wants to prostrate them consecutively, and it is recommended that the reciter go forward and the people line up... [continued with a return to the number issue]
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage details the manner (kayfiyya) of sajdat al-tilawa. The author explains that the prostration is performed with the conditions of prayer except the opening takbir (tahrimah). Two takbirs are performed: one for going down (takbirat al-wad') and one for rising (takbirat al-raf'), both being sunnah. Hands are not raised because these takbirs are for bowing, not to signify the start. No tashahhud or taslim is recited because there is no tahrimah to dissolve. The preferred supplication is 'Subhana al-A'la' three times. The text also notes the recommended act of standing before prostrating, citing the Quranic action of falling down and a narration from Aisha. The later part of the passage includes a digression about the number of prostrations for the listener, returning to the earlier dispute, but the main lesson on the manner is clear.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الوضع و تكبيرة الرفع (takbirat al-wad' wa takbirat al-raf'): The two takbirs in sajdat al-tilawa: one for lowering to prostration and one for rising. They are sunnah and are done without raising hands.
سجود التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): The prostration performed when reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (ayat al-sajda) from the Quran. It is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates prayer and makes previously permissible actions forbidden (haram) until taslim. In sajdat al-tilawa, it is intentionally omitted.

B) Sunnah
C) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawa is performed with the conditions of prayer except tahrimah; two takbirs are sunnah, no tashahhud or taslim, and the recommended supplication is 'Subhana al-A'la' three times.

Manner of Sajdah al-Tilawah
Describes the performance of sajdah al-tilawah and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the manner of performing sajdah al-tilawah according to the Hanafi school and identify its conditions, sunnah acts, and the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is sunnah muakkadah performed between two takbirs with prayer conditions except the opening takbir.

Sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) is a confirmed sunnah upon reciting or hearing a verse of sajdah. The Hanafi school details its performance with specific conditions and sunnah acts, distinguishing it from the prostration within prayer. This lesson unpacks the rulings and proofs as explained in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that sajdah al-tilawah is sunnah muakkadah and must be performed with the conditions of prayer except the opening takbir (tahrima).
The ruling is based on the hadith of the Prophet's action.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof from the Sunnah: the hadith in Abu Dawood of the Prophet performing sajdah between two takbirs.
The dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action demonstrates that the takbirs are part of the prostration and that raising hands is not required since the takbir is for bending, not for entering.
The absence of tashahhud and taslim is because they require a preceding tahrima.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement on what to recite; the most correct view is to say 'Subhana al-A'la' thrice, similar to prayer prostration.
Other supplications are permissible, especially outside prayer.
5
Determine recommended acts
It is sunnah to stand before prostrating, to have the reciter go forward for collective prostration, and to intend the prostration in the heart while saying a specific phrase.
A woman may lead a man in this prostration according to one narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكيفيته أن يسجد بشرائط الصلاة بين تكبيرتين بلا رفع يد وتشهد وتسليم. قوله ( وكيفيته أن يسجد بشرائط الصلاة بين تكبيرتين بلا رفع يد وتشهد وتسلييم) أي وكيفية السجود وقدمنا أنه يستثنى من شرائط الصلاة التحريمة والمراد بالتكبيرتين تكبيرة الوضع وتكبيرة الرفع وكل منهما سنة كما صححه في البدائع الحديث أبي داود في السنن من فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام كذلك. وإنما لا يرفع يديه عند التكبيرة لأن هذا التكبير مفعول لأجل الانحطاط لا للتحريمة كما في سجود الصلاة وكذا التكبير للرفع كما في سجود الصلاة وهو المروي من فعله عليه السلام وابن مسعود من بعده. وإنما لا يتشهد ولا يسلم لأنه للتحليل وهو يستدعي سبق التحريمة وهي معدومة واختلفوا فيما يقوله في هذه السجدة، والأصح أنه يقول سبحان الأعلى ثلاثاً كسجدة الصلاة ولا ينقص منها. وينبغي أن لا يكون ما صحح على عمومه فإن ربي كانت السجدة في الصلاة، فإن كانت فريضة قال سبحان ربي الأعلى أو نفلاً قال ما شاء مما ورد كسجد وجهي للذي خلقه إلى آخره. وقوله «اللهم اكتب لي بها عندك أجراً، وضع عني بها وزراً، واجعلها لي عندك ذخراً، وتقبلها مني كما تقبلتها من عبدك داود» وإن كان خارج الصلاة قال : كلما أثر من ذلك. كذا في فتح القدير. ومما يستحب لأدائها أن يقوم فيسجد لأن الخرور سقوط من القيام والقرآن ورد به وهو مروي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها وإن لم يفعل لم يضره . وما وقع في السراج الوهاج من أنه إذا كان قاعداً لا يقوم لها، فخلاف المذهب. وفي المضمرات : يستحب أن يقوم ويسجد ويقوم بعد رفع الرأس من السجدة ولا يقعد اهـ . والثاني غريب. وأفاد في القنية أنه يقوم لها وإن كانت كثيره وأراد أن يسجدها مترادفة، ومن المستحب أن يتقدم التالي ويصف القوم خلفه فيسجدون، ويستحب أن لا يرفع القوم رؤوسهم قبله وليس هو اقتداء حقيقة لأنه لو فسدت سجد الإمام بسبب لا يتعدى إليهم. وفي المجتبى معزياً إلى شيخ الإسلام : لا يؤمر التالي بالتقديم ولا بالصف ولكنه يسجد ويسجدون معه حيث كانوا وكيف كانوا. وذكر أبو بكر أن المرأة تصلح إماماً للرجل فيها .اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج ثم إذا أراد السجود ينويها بقلبه ويقول بلسانه أسجد لله سجدة التلاوة الله أكبر كما يقول أصلي لله تعالى صلاة كذا .
And its manner is that he prostrates with the conditions of prayer between two takbirs without raising hands, tashahhud, and taslim. His statement (and its manner is that he prostrates with the conditions of prayer between two takbirs without raising hands, tashahhud, and taslim) means the manner of prostration, and we have mentioned that the tahrima is excepted from the conditions of prayer. The intended meaning of the two takbirs is the takbir of placing and the takbir of raising, and each of them is sunnah as corrected in al-Bada'i' by the hadith of Abu Dawood in al-Sunan from his action (peace be upon him) similarly. And he does not raise his hands at the takbir because this takbir is done for bending down, not for tahrima, as in the prostration of prayer. Similarly, the takbir for raising is as in the prostration of prayer. And it is narrated from his action and Ibn Mas'ud after him. And he does not utter tashahhud nor taslim because they are for tahlil, which requires precedence of tahrima, which is absent. They differed regarding what is said in this prostration. The most correct is that he says 'Subhana al-A'la' three times like the prostration of prayer and does not decrease from it. And it should not be taken as general, because if the prostration is in prayer, then if it is an obligatory prayer, he says 'Subhana rabbi al-A'la', or if it is supererogatory, he says whatever is reported such as 'Sajada wajhi li alladhi khalaqahu...' to the end. And his saying 'Allahumma uktub li biha 'indaka ajran, wada' 'anni biha wizran, waj'alha li 'indaka dhukhran, wa taqabbalha minni kama taqabbaltaha min 'abdika Dawud' and if it is outside prayer, he says whatever is reported from that. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And from what is recommended for performing it is that he stands and prostrates because falling is descending from standing, and the Qur'an came with it, narrated from 'Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her). If he does not do it, it does not harm him. What occurred in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that if he is sitting, he does not stand for it, is contrary to the madhhab. In al-Mudmarat: It is recommended that he stands and prostrates, and stands after raising his head from the prostration, and does not sit. The second is strange. And it is stated in al-Qunyah that he stands for it even if they are many and he wants to prostrate them consecutively. And from what is recommended is that the reciter goes forward and arranges the people behind him and they prostrate, and it is recommended that the people do not raise their heads before him. It is not truly following because if the imam's prostration becomes invalid due to a reason, it does not extend to them. In al-Mujtaba, citing Shaykh al-Islam: The reciter is not ordered to go forward nor to form rows, but he prostrates and they prostrate with him wherever they are and however they are. And Abu Bakr mentioned that a woman is suitable as an imam for a man in it. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Then when he wants to prostrate, he intends it in his heart and says with his tongue 'Asjudu lillahi sajdata al-tilawah Allahu akbar' just as he says 'Uṣalli lillahi ta'ala salata kadha'.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the manner of performing sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The author begins by stating that the prostration is done with the conditions of prayer except for the opening takbir (tahrima), between two takbirs: one for going down and one for coming up. Both takbirs are sunnah, as established by the hadith in Abu Dawood. The hands are not raised because the takbir is not for entering the prostration but for bending. Tashahhud and taslim are omitted because they are for concluding the prayer, which requires an opening tahrima that is absent in this prostration. As for what to say, the most correct view is to say 'Subhana al-A'la' thrice, like in the prostration during prayer. If the prostration is part of an obligatory prayer, he says 'Subhana rabbi al-A'la'; if it is supererogatory, he may say the reported supplications. Outside prayer, additional supplications like the one from Dawud are recommended. The passage then discusses recommended acts: standing before prostrating, as it follows the Qur'anic command in Surah al-Qiyama v.18, and the reciter should go forward and arrange followers in rows. It is recommended that followers do not raise their heads before the reciter, though it is not a true following because if the reciter's prostration becomes invalid, the followers are not affected. A woman may lead a man in this prostration according to one narration. Finally, the intention and wording for the prostration are given: intending in the heart and saying 'Asjudu lillahi sajdata al-tilawah Allahu akbar'.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الوضع (takbirat al-wad'): The takbir said when placing the forehead on the ground for prostration.
تكبيرة الرفع (takbirat al-raf'): The takbir said when raising the head from prostration.
تحريمة (tahrima): The opening takbir that commences the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is sunnah
C) It is not done because the takbir is not for tahrima
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah is performed with the conditions of prayer except the opening takbir, between two sunnah takbirs, without tashahhud or taslim, and the most correct recitation is 'Subhana al-A'la' thrice.

Listener's Prostration When Two Recite: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple prostrations for a listener

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the number of prostrations owed by a listener when two people recite, and evaluate Qadikhan's opposing view.

Core Idea
When two recite, the listener owes one prostration — hearing is one act, not multiple.

In Hanafi fiqh, hearing a verse of prostration obligates sajdah al-tilawah. But what if two people recite such verses in your presence? Does the listener owe one prostration or two? This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute between the relied-upon view and the opinion of Qadikhan, as recorded in al-Bahr al-Raiq. We will see how the madhhab weighs evidence and settles on the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
State the mufta bihi position
Identify the operative ruling: the listener owes only one prostration regardless of how many recite.
This is the view from al-Qunyah and al-Zahiriyyah.
2
Identify the opposing view
Qadikhan argues that the listener owes two: one for his own recitation (if he also recites) and one for hearing from the other.
3
Trace the basis of disagreement
The dispute hinges on whether hearing multiple recitations is considered one or multiple causes (asbab) for obligation.
Qadikhan sees each recitation as a separate cause.
4
Apply tarjih
Explain why the mufta bihi (one prostration) is preferred: the listener's location and hearing are considered a single unit, and multiplying obligations without clear evidence is avoided.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq cites the apparent riwayah in support.
5
Note the practical consequence
In practice, the listener performs only one sajdah al-tilawah after hearing all recitations.
This avoids unnecessary repetition and potential invalidation of salah if done inside prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم رأيته بحمد الله تعالى في فتاوى قاضيخان أن على كل منهما سجدتين صلاتية بتلاوته وخارجية بسماعه من صاحبه وأطال الكلام في بيانه فراجعه .
Then I saw, by the praise of Allah Almighty, in the Fatawa of Qadikhan that each of them owes two prostrations: one obligatory due to his recitation, and one external due to hearing from his companion. And he gave a lengthy discussion explaining it, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah for a listener when two people are reciting. Qadikhan holds that the listener owes two prostrations: one 'salatiyyah' (related to his own recitation) and one 'kharijiyyah' (due to hearing from his companion). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq mentions seeing this in Qadikhan's Fatawa. However, earlier in the text (not included in this lesson), it was stated that the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that only one prostration is owed. The implication is that Qadikhan's opinion is not the official position of the madhhab. The student should refer to Qadikhan's lengthy discussion for details. The lesson highlights the complexity of fiqh rulings when multiple reciters are involved.

Key Terms
سجدة صلاتية (sajdah salatiyyah): A prostration that is considered obligatory due to recitation.
سجدة خارجية (sajdah kharijiyyah): An external prostration due to hearing from another person, as distinguished from the prostration due to one's own recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, how many prostrations does a listener owe when he hears two people recite verses of prostration?
A) Two prostrations
B) One prostration
C) None
D) Four prostrations

Key Takeaway
When two people recite sajdah verses before a listener, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that the listener owes only one prostration.

Dislike of Skipping the Verse of Prostration
Ruling on omitting the verse of prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentionally omitting a verse of prostration and explain the reason for the dislike, including the recommended practice of reciting additional verses.

Core Idea
Skipping a prostration verse intentionally is disliked; reciting it alone is not.

When reciting a surah in prayer or elsewhere, one may encounter a verse requiring prostration (ayat as-sajdah). This passage clarifies the ruling if someone intentionally omits that verse or, conversely, recites only the prostration verse. The Hanafi school considers the former disliked due to its resemblance to arrogance, while the latter is acceptable. Understanding this distinction helps maintain the proper reverence for the Qur'an without falling into unnecessary difficulty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being judged: intentionally skipping the verse of prostration from a surah you are reciting. The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked), not haram.
Contrast with the opposite: reciting only the verse of prostration is not disliked.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is Quran 75:18, which commands following the composition of the Qur'an. Omitting a verse breaks that composition, hence the dislike.
The dalil is from the Quran, but its indication is zanni (speculative), placing the ruling at the disliked level rather than forbidden.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'follow its recitation' (follow its composition). Intentionally leaving out a verse violates this command by altering the order. The dislike arises from this breach of proper recitation etiquette.
The similarity to disdain (istinkaf) is an additional rationale, not the primary legal cause.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi guidance on best practice
Imam Muhammad recommends reciting one or two verses before the prostration verse; Qadikhan says reciting one or two verses before or after is more beloved. This avoids any impression of preferring the prostration verses over others.
These are recommendations (mustahabb), not obligations.
5
Understand the nuance about multiple prostration verses
The text resolves an apparent contradiction in al-Bada'i': reciting several prostration verses in one sitting does not break the Qur'anic order, as true change only occurs by omitting words or verses, not by rearranging them. However, if one delays prostration until after reading all verses, it is fine; immediate prostration after each verse may disrupt the composition according to some.
This nuance shows the depth of Hanafi analysis in preserving the integrity of the Qur'an's arrangement.

قوله (وكره أن يقرأ سورة ويدع آية السجدة لا عكسه) لأنه يشبه الاستنكاف عنها عمداً في الأول وفي الثاني مبادراً لها . قال :محمد وأحب إلى أن يقرأ قبلها آية أو آيتين . وذكر قاضيخان إن قرأ معها آية أو آيتين فهو أحب وهذا أعم من الأول لصدقه بما إذا قرأ بعدها آية أو آيتين بخلاف الأول، وعلله بقوله دفعاً لوهم التفضيل أي تفضيل آي السجدة على غيرها إذ الكل من حيث إنه كلام الله تعالى في رتبة وإن كان لبعضها بسبب اشتماله على ذكر صفات الحق جل جلاله زيادة فضيلة باعتبار المذكور لا باعتبار من حيث هو قرآن . وفى الكافي : قيل من قرأ آي السجدة كلها في مجلس واحد وسجد لكل منها كفاه الله ما أهمه. وما ذكر في البدائع في كراهة ترك آية السجدة من سورة يقرأها لأن فيه قطعاً لنظم القرآن وتغييراً لتأليفه واتباع النظم والتأليف مأمور به قال الله تعالى فإذا قرأناه فاتبع قرآنه القيامة : ۱۸] أي تأليفه فكان التغيير مكروهاً يقتضي كراهة ذلك . كذا في فتح القدير . وأقول : وإن كان ذلك مقتضاه لكن صرح بعده في البدائع بخلافه فقال : ولو قرأ آية السجدة من بين سقطاً لأن الذي رأيته في الظهيرية وكذا في التتارخانية معزياً إليها : وإذا رفع رأسه من السجود يقوم ثم يقعد. وكذا قال في شرح المنية وفي الظهيرية أنه يستحب القيام بعد الرفع منها أيضاً قوله : (يقتضي كراهة ذلك) خبر عن ما في قوله وما ذكر في البدائع أي يقتضي الكراهة في قراءة آي السجدة كلها في مجلس قوله : لكن صرح بعده في البدائع بخلافه ظاهره أن كلامه متناقض لأنه يفيد أن ما صرح به بعده فيه تغيير لتأليفه والأحسن ما في شرح المنية حيث قال: وفيه نظر لأن تغيير التأليف إنما يحصل بإسقاط بعض الكلمات أو الآيات من السورة لا بذكر كلمة أو آية منها على ما مر أن قراءة آية من بين الآيات كقراءة سورة من بين السور. فكما لا يكون قراءة سور متفرقة من أثناء القرآن مغيراً للتأليف والنظم لا يكون قراءة آية من كل سورة مغيراً له، نعم يقتضي أنه لو ترك آية السجدة من آخر السورة لا يكره وفيه ما فيه ا هـ . أي فالأولى أن يذكر صاحب البدائع ولا ولأنه لا يرد هذا الأخير. هذا وما نقله الرملي عن المقدسي من أن قراءة تلك الآيات متوالية في مجلس تغيير للنظم وإحداث تأليف جديد بخلاف ما صرح به في البدائع بعد لأن تلك آية مفردة ا هـ . ظاهر فيما لو أخر السجدات لما بعد التلاوة، أما لو سجد عقب كل آية فلا لأن ذلك فاصل للتأليف كما قالوا فيما لو انتقل من آية إلى أخرى من سورة واحدة في ركعتين لا يكره إذا كان بينهما آيتان فأكثر ولو في ركعة كره مطلقاً كما نبه عليه في شرح المنية، وكذا قراءة سورتين فصل بينهما بسورتين يكره في كل ركعة لا ركعتين كما نبه عليه في الفتح تأمل. ولذا والله تعالى أعلم قال الاستنكاف حتى يشبه
His statement (and it is disliked that he recites a surah and omits the verse of prostration, not the opposite) because it resembles deliberate disdain in the first case, and in the second case it is hastening for it. Muhammad said: And it is more beloved to me that he recites before it one or two verses. Qadikhan mentioned that if he recites with it one or two verses, it is more beloved, and this is more general than the first because it applies when he recites after it one or two verses, unlike the first. He explained it by saying: to prevent the assumption of preference, i.e., preference of the verses of prostration over others, since all are equal in that they are words of Allah, although some have additional virtue due to mentioning the attributes of the Truth, but not as being more excellent as Qur'an. In al-Kafi: It is said that whoever recites all the verses of prostration in one sitting and prostrates for each, Allah will suffice him from what troubles him. And what was mentioned in al-Bada'i' regarding the dislike of omitting the verse of prostration from a surah he recites because it involves breaking the order of the Qur'an and changing its composition, and following the order and composition is commanded. Allah said: 'When We recite it, follow its recitation' (al-Qiyama 18), meaning its composition. So change is disliked, necessitating dislike of that. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And I say: Although that is its implication, he explicitly stated otherwise later in al-Bada'i': 'If he reads the verse of prostration from among ...' because what I saw in al-Zahiriyyah and similarly in al-Tatarikhaniyyah citing it: 'When he raises his head from prostration, he stands then sits.' Likewise said in Sharh al-Munyah and in al-Zahiriyyah that standing after raising is also recommended. His statement (necessitates dislike of that) is news about what is in his statement and what was mentioned in al-Bada'i', i.e., it necessitates dislike in reading all the verses of prostration in one sitting. His statement: 'But he explicitly stated otherwise later in al-Bada'i' ' is apparent as a contradiction because it implies that what he stated later involves changing its composition. The best is what is in Sharh al-Munyah, where he said: There is consideration because changing composition only occurs by omitting some words or verses from the surah, not by mentioning a word or verse from it, as previously that reading a verse from among verses is like reading a surah from among surahs. Just as reading scattered surahs from the Qur'an does not change the order and composition, so reading a verse from each surah does not change it. However, it implies that if he omits the verse of prostration from the end of the surah, it is not disliked, but there is something in it. So it is better that the author of al-Bada'i' is mentioned, and because this latter is not refuted. This and what al-Ramli transmitted from al-Maqdisi that reading those verses consecutively in one sitting is a change of order and creating a new composition, unlike what was stated later in al-Bada'i' because that is a single verse. This is apparent if he delays the prostrations after recitation, but if he prostrates immediately after each verse, then it is not because that separates the composition, as they said regarding moving from one verse to another of a single surah in two rak'ahs, it is not disliked if there are two or more verses between them, but if in one rak'ah it is disliked absolutely, as indicated in Sharh al-Munyah. Similarly, reading two surahs separated by two surahs is disliked in one rak'ah but not in two rak'ahs, as indicated in al-Fath. And therefore, Allah knows best, he said: 'the disdain until it resembles'.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage discusses the dislike (karaha) of intentionally skipping the verse of prostration when reciting a surah. The author explains that the dislike is because it resembles disdain for the Qur'an. However, the opposite—i.e., reciting only the verse of prostration without other verses—is not disliked, as it actually shows eagerness. Imam Muhammad suggests reciting one or two verses before the prostration verse, and Qadikhan considers it more beloved to recite one or two verses with it, either before or after, to avoid the impression of preferring the prostration verses over others. The passage then addresses the ruling on reciting multiple verses of prostration in one sitting. According to al-Bada'i', omitting the verse of prostration is disliked because it breaks the order of the Qur'an. However, a later statement in al-Bada'i' seems contradictory, and the commentator resolves this by citing Sharh al-Munyah, which argues that true change of order only occurs by omitting words or verses, not by reciting a verse from its place. Reading multiple prostration verses one after another in one sitting is not a change of order, as it is like reading individual verses. But if he delays the prostrations until after the recitation, it is fine; whereas if he prostrates immediately after each verse, it might disrupt the composition. The passage concludes with a note that reading two surahs separated by two surahs in one rak'ah is disliked, but in two rak'ahs it is not.

Key Terms
الاستنكاف (al-istinkaf): Showing disdain or arrogance by avoiding the prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling if someone intentionally omits the verse of prostration when reciting a surah?
A) The prayer becomes invalid
B) It is forbidden
C) It is disliked
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Intentionally skipping a prostration verse is disliked due to resemblance to disdain; reciting the verse alone is not disliked, and accompanying it with other verses is recommended.

The Dislike of Skipping the Sajdah Ayah: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof from Quran and scholar preferences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on skipping the sajdah ayah, identify the Quranic proof, and explain the preference for adding surrounding ayahs.

Core Idea
Skipping the sajdah ayah while reciting a surah is makruh because it resembles disdain; reciting only the ayah is fine.

In sujud al-tilawa, the manner of recitation carries legal rulings. This lesson focuses on the key rule: it is disliked to skip the verse of prostration when reciting a surah, but not vice versa. We examine the reasoning and the Quranic proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Locate the statement: 'It is disliked to recite a surah and leave out the ayah of sajdah, not the reverse.' Determine the hukm level.
The text uses 'كره' (disliked); due to resemblance to disdain, it is makruh tahrimi.
2
Understand the reasoning
Skipping resembles intentional disdain (استنكاف) for the verse; reciting only the ayah is hastening to it, which is not disliked.
The opposite is not disliked because it shows eagerness to prostrate.
3
Locate the Quranic dalil
Find the verse cited: 'فإذا قرأناه فاتبع قرآنه' (al-Qiyamah 75:18). Understand how it supports the ruling.
The verse commands following the Quranic arrangement; skipping disrupts it.
4
Note the preference by Muhammad and Qadi Khan
Imam Muhammad prefers reciting one or two ayahs before the sajdah ayah; Qadi Khan allows before or after. Both aim to avoid illusion of preference.
This is a recommended practice, not a condition.

كتاب الصلاة باب سجود التلاوة
خلفه فيسجدون، ويستحب أن لا يرفع القوم رؤوسهم قبله وليس هو اقتداء حقيقة لأنه لو فسدت سجد الإمام بسبب لا يتعدى إليهم. وفي المجتبى معزياً إلى شيخ الإسلام : لا يؤمر التالي بالتقديم ولا بالصف ولكنه يسجد ويسجدون معه حيث كانوا وكيف كانوا. وذكر أبو بكر أن المرأة تصلح إماماً للرجل فيها .اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج ثم إذا أراد السجود ينويها بقلبه ويقول بلسانه أسجد لله سجدة التلاوة الله أكبر كما يقول أصلي لله تعالى صلاة كذا .
