قوله (وكره أن يقرأ سورة ويدع آية السجدة لا عكسه) لأنه يشبه الاستنكاف عنها عمداً في الأول وفي الثاني مبادراً لها . قال :محمد وأحب إلى أن يقرأ قبلها آية أو آيتين . وذكر قاضيخان إن قرأ معها آية أو آيتين فهو أحب وهذا أعم من الأول لصدقه بما إذا قرأ بعدها آية أو آيتين بخلاف الأول، وعلله بقوله دفعاً لوهم التفضيل أي تفضيل آي السجدة على غيرها إذ الكل من حيث إنه كلام الله تعالى في رتبة وإن كان لبعضها بسبب اشتماله على ذكر صفات الحق جل جلاله زيادة فضيلة باعتبار المذكور لا باعتبار من حيث هو قرآن . وفى الكافي : قيل من قرأ آي السجدة كلها في مجلس واحد وسجد لكل منها كفاه الله ما أهمه. وما ذكر في البدائع في كراهة ترك آية السجدة من سورة يقرأها لأن فيه قطعاً لنظم القرآن وتغييراً لتأليفه واتباع النظم والتأليف مأمور به قال الله تعالى فإذا قرأناه فاتبع قرآنه القيامة : ۱۸] أي تأليفه فكان التغيير مكروهاً يقتضي كراهة ذلك . كذا في فتح القدير . وأقول : وإن كان ذلك مقتضاه لكن صرح بعده في البدائع بخلافه فقال : ولو قرأ آية السجدة من بين
من
سقطاً [؟] لأن الذي رأيته في الظهيرية وكذا في التتارخانية معزياً إليها : وإذا رفع رأسه من السجود يقوم ثم يقعد. وكذا قال في شرح المنية وفي الظهيرية أنه يستحب القيام بعد الرفع منها أيضاً قوله : (يقتضي كراهة ذلك) خبر عن ما في قوله وما ذكر في البدائع أي يقتضي الكراهة في قراءة آي السجدة كلها في مجلس قوله : لكن صرح بعده في البدائع بخلافه ظاهره أن كلامه متناقض لأنه يفيد أن ما صرح به بعده فيه تغيير لتأليفه والأحسن ما في شرح المنية حيث قال: وفيه نظر لأن تغيير التأليف إنما يحصل بإسقاط بعض الكلمات أو الآيات من السورة لا بذكر كلمة أو آية منها على ما مر أن قراءة آية من بين الآيات كقراءة سورة من بين السور. فكما لا يكون قراءة سور متفرقة من أثناء القرآن مغيراً للتأليف والنظم لا يكون قراءة آية من كل سورة مغيراً له، نعم يقتضي أنه لو ترك آية السجدة من آخر السورة لا يكره وفيه ما فيه ا هـ . أي فالأولى أن يذكر صاحب البدائع ولا ولأنه لا يرد هذا الأخير. هذا وما نقله الرملي عن المقدسي من أن قراءة تلك الآيات متوالية في مجلس تغيير للنظم وإحداث تأليف جديد بخلاف ما صرح به في البدائع بعد لأن تلك آية مفردة ا هـ . ظاهر فيما لو أخر السجدات لما بعد التلاوة، أما لو سجد عقب كل آية فلا لأن ذلك فاصل للتأليف كما قالوا فيما لو انتقل من آية إلى أخرى من سورة واحدة في ركعتين لا يكره إذا كان بينهما آيتان فأكثر ولو في ركعة كره مطلقاً كما نبه عليه في شرح المنية، وكذا قراءة سورتين فصل بينهما بسورتين يكره في كل ركعة لا ركعتين كما نبه عليه في الفتح تأمل. ولذا والله تعالى أعلم قال
الاستنكاف حتى
يشبه

السور لم يضره ذلك لأنها من القرآن وقراءة ما هو من القرآن طاعة كقراءة سورة من بين السور. وقيده قاضيخان بأن يكون في غير الصلاة فظاهر أنه لو كان في الصلاة كره فهو مقيد لقوله لا عكسه. ثم قال في البدائع ولو قرأ آية السجدة وعنده ناس فإن كانوا متوضئين متأهبين للسجدة قرأها جهراً، وإن كانوا غير متأهبين ينبغي أن يخفض قراءته لأنه لو جهر بها لصار موجباً عليهم شيئاً ربما يتكاسلون عن أدائه فيقعون في المعصية اهـ. وذكر الشارح : : ولو قرأ آية السجدة إلا الحرف الذي في آخرها لا يسجد، ولو قرأ الحرف الذي يسجد فيه وحده لا يسجد إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة بحرف السجدة. وفي مختصر البحر : لو قرأ وسجد وسكت ولم يقرأ واقترب تلزمه السجدة .اهـ. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : رجل سمع آية السجدة من قوم من كل واحد منهم حرفاً ليس عليه أن يسجد لأنه لم يسمعها من والله سبحانه أعلم وبعباده أرحم .
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawa: They prostrate behind him, and it is recommended that the people do not raise their heads before him, and it is not really following because if the imam's prostration becomes invalid due to a reason that does not extend to them. In al-Mujtaba, attributed to Shaykh al-Islam: The reciter is not commanded to go ahead nor to form rows, but he prostrates and they prostrate with him wherever and however they are. Abu Bakr mentioned that a woman is suitable as an imam for a man in it. End. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Then when he intends to prostrate, he intends it in his heart and says with his tongue 'I prostrate to Allah for the tilawa prostration, Allahu Akbar' just as he says 'I pray to Allah Almighty such a prayer.' : He said (It is disliked to recite a surah and leave out the ayah of sajdah, not the reverse) because it resembles intentional disdain in the first, and in the second, hastening to it. Muhammad said: I prefer that he recite before it one or two ayahs. Qadi Khan mentioned: If he recites with it one or two ayahs, it is better, and this is more general than the first because it includes if he recites after it one or two ayahs, unlike the first, and he explained it as repelling the illusion of preferring the ayahs of sajdah over others, since all are at the same level insofar as they are the speech of Allah, although some have extra virtue due to mentioning the attributes of the Truth, but not as Quran. In al-Kafi: It is said that whoever recites all the ayahs of sajdah in one gathering and prostrates for each, Allah suffices him for what concerns him. And what was mentioned in al-Bada'i about the dislike of leaving out the ayah of sajdah from a surah he recites, because it involves cutting the arrangement of the Quran and changing its composition, and following the arrangement and composition is commanded. Allah Almighty said: 'So when We have recited it, then follow its recitation' (al-Qiyamah 75:18), i.e., its composition. So changing it is disliked, necessitating that dislike. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And I say: Although that is its implication, he later stated in al-Bada'i contrary to it, saying: If he recites the ayah of sajdah from among the surahs, it does not harm him. This is because he read 'from among the surahs' [؟]... For what I saw in al-Zuhayriyya and also in al-Tatarkhaniyya attributed to it: When he raises his head from prostration, he stands then sits. Likewise stated in Sharh al-Munya and in al-Zuhayriyya that it is recommended to stand after raising from it. His statement (necessitates dislike of that) is a report about what was in his statement 'and what was mentioned in al-Bada'i', i.e., it necessitates dislike in reciting all the ayahs of sajdah in one gathering. His statement: But he later stated in al-Bada'i contrary to it, apparently his speech is contradictory because it indicates that what he stated later involves changing its composition. The best is what is in Sharh al-Munya where he said: There is a problem because changing the composition only occurs by dropping some words or ayahs from the surah, not by mentioning a word or ayah from it, as previously stated that reciting an ayah from among the ayahs is like reciting a surah from among the surahs. So just as reciting scattered surahs from the Quran does not change the composition and arrangement, reciting an ayah from each surah does not change it. Yes, it would imply that if he leaves out the ayah of sajdah from the end of the surah, it is not disliked, but there is something in it. End. That is, it is better to mention the author of al-Bada'i... This and what al-Ramli narrated from al-Maqdisi that reading those ayahs consecutively in a gathering is a change of arrangement and creating a new composition, contrary to what was stated in al-Bada'i later because that is a single ayah. End. It is apparent if he delays the prostrations until after the recitation. But if he prostrates immediately after each ayah, then it is not, because that separates the composition, as they said regarding moving from one ayah to another from the same surah in two rak'ahs, it is not disliked if there are two or more ayahs between them; but in one rak'ah, it is disliked absolutely, as pointed out in Sharh al-Munya. Likewise, reciting two surahs with two surahs separating them is disliked in each rak'ah but not in two rak'ahs, as pointed out in al-Fath. Contemplate. Therefore, and Allah knows best, he said: 'disdain' until 'resembles'. The surahs do not harm him because they are from the Quran, and reciting what is from the Quran is obedience like reciting a surah from among the surahs. Qadi Khan restricted it to being outside of prayer, so it is apparent that if it is during prayer, it is disliked, so it is a restriction of his statement 'not the reverse'. Then he said in al-Bada'i: If he recites an ayah of sajdah and there are people present, if they are in wudu and prepared for prostration, he recites it loudly; if they are not prepared, he should lower his recitation, because if he recites it loudly, he would impose something on them that they might be lazy in performing, thus falling into sin. End. The commentator mentioned: If he recites the ayah of sajdah except the letter at its end, he does not prostrate; if he recites the letter of sajdah alone, he does not prostrate unless he recites most of the ayah of sajdah with the letter of sajdah. In Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If he recites and prostrates and is silent and does not recite and draws near, the prostration becomes obligatory. End. In Fatawa Qadi Khan: A man heard the ayah of sajdah from a group, each one uttering one letter, he is not required to prostrate because he did not hear it from one person. And Allah Almighty knows best, and He is most merciful to His servants.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on sujud al-tilawa rulings. It covers several points: (1) Following the imam in sujud: The congregation prostrates with the imam, and it is recommended not to raise their heads before him. This is not considered actual following (iqtida') because if the imam's prostration becomes invalid for a reason that does not affect them, their prostration remains valid. (2) The reciter is not required to go forward or stand in a row; he prostrates wherever he is, and others follow. For a woman leading a man in this prostration is permissible according to Abu Bakr. (3) Intention and takbir: The reciter intends in his heart and says 'I prostrate for tilawa prostration' and 'Allahu Akbar'. (4) The main ruling: It is disliked (makruh) to recite a surah and deliberately skip the ayah of sajdah, but not the reverse (i.e., reciting only the sajdah ayah is not disliked). The reasoning: skipping resembles disdain; reciting alone is a sign of haste. Imam Muhammad prefers reciting one or two ayahs before or after to avoid misunderstanding. (5) Reciting all sajdah ayahs in one sitting: Al-Bada'i initially said it is disliked because it breaks the order of the Quran, citing the verse 'follow its recitation'. However, he later contradicted this, saying that reciting an ayah from among surahs does not harm, as it is like reciting one surah from among many. The commentary resolves this by explaining that changing the composition only occurs by omitting part of a surah, not by selecting individual ayahs. (6) If reciting an ayah of sajdah in front of people: if they are prepared to prostrate, recite loudly; if not, lower the voice to avoid causing them sin through laziness. (7) Partial recitation: if one recites the ayah except its last letter, no prostration; if one recites only the verse of sajdah itself, no prostration unless one recites most of the ayah including the sajdah letter. (8) If one hears the ayah from a group each saying a letter, no prostration is required. These rulings are based on specific conditions and aim to preserve the dignity of the Quran and the proper manner of recitation.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawa): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran (ayat as-sajdah).
الاستنكاف (al-istinkaf): Disdain or refusal; used here to describe the act of skipping the sajdah ayah deliberately, which resembles disdain for the verse.
النظم (al-nazm): The composition/arrangement of the Quran in its known order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it disliked to skip the ayah of sajdah when reciting a surah?
A) Because it breaks wudu.
B) Because it resembles disdain for the verse.
C) Because it delays the prayer.
D) Because it is forbidden in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
It is makruh tahrimi to skip the sajdah ayah intentionally; reciting it alone is permissible and not disliked.

Reciting All Sajdah Ayahs: Is It a Change to Quranic Composition?
Intra-Hanafi dispute with resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on reciting all sajdah ayahs in one gathering and apply the resolution based on the principle of preserving Quranic composition.

Core Idea
Reciting all sajdah ayahs in one gathering is not a change to the Quranic composition if each is followed by its prostration immediately.

A debated question: is it permissible to recite multiple verses of prostration consecutively? The Hanafi school debated this, with some considering it a change to the Quran's arrangement. This lesson examines the conflicting positions and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
State the initial position from al-Bada'i
Al-Bada'i initially states that skipping the sajdah ayah is disliked because it cuts the Quranic arrangement. But later he says that reciting the sajdah ayah from among surahs does not harm.
This apparent contradiction requires resolution.
2
Identify the opposing view from the same source
Some scholars (like al-Maqdisi) argue that reciting all sajdah ayahs consecutively creates a new arrangement, thus disliked.
They rely on the same verse 'follow its recitation'.
3
Examine the resolution from Sharh al-Munya
Changing the composition only occurs by omission, not by selecting ayahs. Reciting individual ayahs is like reciting individual surahs; it does not disrupt the arrangement.
The decisive point: immediate prostration after each ayah actually preserves the original order.
4
Apply the principle to the case of immediate prostration
If one prostrates immediately after each sajdah ayah, the composition is separated by the prostration, so no change occurs. If prostrations are delayed, it might be disliked.
The ruling depends on timing.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة باب سجود التلاوة
خلفه فيسجدون، ويستحب أن لا يرفع القوم رؤوسهم قبله وليس هو اقتداء حقيقة لأنه لو فسدت سجد الإمام بسبب لا يتعدى إليهم. وفي المجتبى معزياً إلى شيخ الإسلام : لا يؤمر التالي بالتقديم ولا بالصف ولكنه يسجد ويسجدون معه حيث كانوا وكيف كانوا. وذكر أبو بكر أن المرأة تصلح إماماً للرجل فيها .اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج ثم إذا أراد السجود ينويها بقلبه ويقول بلسانه أسجد لله سجدة التلاوة الله أكبر كما يقول أصلي لله تعالى صلاة كذا .
:
قوله (وكره أن يقرأ سورة ويدع آية السجدة لا عكسه) لأنه يشبه الاستنكاف عنها عمداً في الأول وفي الثاني مبادراً لها . قال :محمد وأحب إلى أن يقرأ قبلها آية أو آيتين . وذكر قاضيخان إن قرأ معها آية أو آيتين فهو أحب وهذا أعم من الأول لصدقه بما إذا قرأ بعدها آية أو آيتين بخلاف الأول، وعلله بقوله دفعاً لوهم التفضيل أي تفضيل آي السجدة على غيرها إذ الكل من حيث إنه كلام الله تعالى في رتبة وإن كان لبعضها بسبب اشتماله على ذكر صفات الحق جل جلاله زيادة فضيلة باعتبار المذكور لا باعتبار من حيث هو قرآن . وفى الكافي : قيل من قرأ آي السجدة كلها في مجلس واحد وسجد لكل منها كفاه الله ما أهمه. وما ذكر في البدائع في كراهة ترك آية السجدة من سورة يقرأها لأن فيه قطعاً لنظم القرآن وتغييراً لتأليفه واتباع النظم والتأليف مأمور به قال الله تعالى فإذا قرأناه فاتبع قرآنه القيامة : ۱۸] أي تأليفه فكان التغيير مكروهاً يقتضي كراهة ذلك . كذا في فتح القدير . وأقول : وإن كان ذلك مقتضاه لكن صرح بعده في البدائع بخلافه فقال : ولو قرأ آية السجدة من بين
من
سقطاً [؟] لأن الذي رأيته في الظهيرية وكذا في التتارخانية معزياً إليها : وإذا رفع رأسه من السجود يقوم ثم يقعد. وكذا قال في شرح المنية وفي الظهيرية أنه يستحب القيام بعد الرفع منها أيضاً قوله : (يقتضي كراهة ذلك) خبر عن ما في قوله وما ذكر في البدائع أي يقتضي الكراهة في قراءة آي السجدة كلها في مجلس قوله : لكن صرح بعده في البدائع بخلافه ظاهره أن كلامه متناقض لأنه يفيد أن ما صرح به بعده فيه تغيير لتأليفه والأحسن ما في شرح المنية حيث قال: وفيه نظر لأن تغيير التأليف إنما يحصل بإسقاط بعض الكلمات أو الآيات من السورة لا بذكر كلمة أو آية منها على ما مر أن قراءة آية من بين الآيات كقراءة سورة من بين السور. فكما لا يكون قراءة سور متفرقة من أثناء القرآن مغيراً للتأليف والنظم لا يكون قراءة آية من كل سورة مغيراً له، نعم يقتضي أنه لو ترك آية السجدة من آخر السورة لا يكره وفيه ما فيه ا هـ . أي فالأولى أن يذكر صاحب البدائع ولا ولأنه لا يرد هذا الأخير. هذا وما نقله الرملي عن المقدسي من أن قراءة تلك الآيات متوالية في مجلس تغيير للنظم وإحداث تأليف جديد بخلاف ما صرح به في البدائع بعد لأن تلك آية مفردة ا هـ . ظاهر فيما لو أخر السجدات لما بعد التلاوة، أما لو سجد عقب كل آية فلا لأن ذلك فاصل للتأليف كما قالوا فيما لو انتقل من آية إلى أخرى من سورة واحدة في ركعتين لا يكره إذا كان بينهما آيتان فأكثر ولو في ركعة كره مطلقاً كما نبه عليه في شرح المنية، وكذا قراءة سورتين فصل بينهما بسورتين يكره في كل ركعة لا ركعتين كما نبه عليه في الفتح تأمل. ولذا والله تعالى أعلم قال
الاستنكاف حتى
يشبه

السور لم يضره ذلك لأنها من القرآن وقراءة ما هو من القرآن طاعة كقراءة سورة من بين السور. وقيده قاضيخان بأن يكون في غير الصلاة فظاهر أنه لو كان في الصلاة كره فهو مقيد لقوله لا عكسه. ثم قال في البدائع ولو قرأ آية السجدة وعنده ناس فإن كانوا متوضئين متأهبين للسجدة قرأها جهراً، وإن كانوا غير متأهبين ينبغي أن يخفض قراءته لأنه لو جهر بها لصار موجباً عليهم شيئاً ربما يتكاسلون عن أدائه فيقعون في المعصية اهـ. وذكر الشارح : : ولو قرأ آية السجدة إلا الحرف الذي في آخرها لا يسجد، ولو قرأ الحرف الذي يسجد فيه وحده لا يسجد إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة بحرف السجدة. وفي مختصر البحر : لو قرأ وسجد وسكت ولم يقرأ واقترب تلزمه السجدة .اهـ. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : رجل سمع آية السجدة من قوم من كل واحد منهم حرفاً ليس عليه أن يسجد لأنه لم يسمعها من والله سبحانه أعلم وبعباده أرحم .
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawa: They prostrate behind him, and it is recommended that the people do not raise their heads before him, and it is not really following because if the imam's prostration becomes invalid due to a reason that does not extend to them. In al-Mujtaba, attributed to Shaykh al-Islam: The reciter is not commanded to go ahead nor to form rows, but he prostrates and they prostrate with him wherever and however they are. Abu Bakr mentioned that a woman is suitable as an imam for a man in it. End. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Then when he intends to prostrate, he intends it in his heart and says with his tongue 'I prostrate to Allah for the tilawa prostration, Allahu Akbar' just as he says 'I pray to Allah Almighty such a prayer.' : He said (It is disliked to recite a surah and leave out the ayah of sajdah, not the reverse) because it resembles intentional disdain in the first, and in the second, hastening to it. Muhammad said: I prefer that he recite before it one or two ayahs. Qadi Khan mentioned: If he recites with it one or two ayahs, it is better, and this is more general than the first because it includes if he recites after it one or two ayahs, unlike the first, and he explained it as repelling the illusion of preferring the ayahs of sajdah over others, since all are at the same level insofar as they are the speech of Allah, although some have extra virtue due to mentioning the attributes of the Truth, but not as Quran. In al-Kafi: It is said that whoever recites all the ayahs of sajdah in one gathering and prostrates for each, Allah suffices him for what concerns him. And what was mentioned in al-Bada'i about the dislike of leaving out the ayah of sajdah from a surah he recites, because it involves cutting the arrangement of the Quran and changing its composition, and following the arrangement and composition is commanded. Allah Almighty said: 'So when We have recited it, then follow its recitation' (al-Qiyamah 75:18), i.e., its composition. So changing it is disliked, necessitating that dislike. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And I say: Although that is its implication, he later stated in al-Bada'i contrary to it, saying: If he recites the ayah of sajdah from among the surahs, it does not harm him. This is because he read 'from among the surahs' [؟]... For what I saw in al-Zuhayriyya and also in al-Tatarkhaniyya attributed to it: When he raises his head from prostration, he stands then sits. Likewise stated in Sharh al-Munya and in al-Zuhayriyya that it is recommended to stand after raising from it. His statement (necessitates dislike of that) is a report about what was in his statement 'and what was mentioned in al-Bada'i', i.e., it necessitates dislike in reciting all the ayahs of sajdah in one gathering. His statement: But he later stated in al-Bada'i contrary to it, apparently his speech is contradictory because it indicates that what he stated later involves changing its composition. The best is what is in Sharh al-Munya where he said: There is a problem because changing the composition only occurs by dropping some words or ayahs from the surah, not by mentioning a word or ayah from it, as previously stated that reciting an ayah from among the ayahs is like reciting a surah from among the surahs. So just as reciting scattered surahs from the Quran does not change the composition and arrangement, reciting an ayah from each surah does not change it. Yes, it would imply that if he leaves out the ayah of sajdah from the end of the surah, it is not disliked, but there is something in it. End. That is, it is better to mention the author of al-Bada'i... This and what al-Ramli narrated from al-Maqdisi that reading those ayahs consecutively in a gathering is a change of arrangement and creating a new composition, contrary to what was stated in al-Bada'i later because that is a single ayah. End. It is apparent if he delays the prostrations until after the recitation. But if he prostrates immediately after each ayah, then it is not, because that separates the composition, as they said regarding moving from one ayah to another from the same surah in two rak'ahs, it is not disliked if there are two or more ayahs between them; but in one rak'ah, it is disliked absolutely, as pointed out in Sharh al-Munya. Likewise, reciting two surahs with two surahs separating them is disliked in each rak'ah but not in two rak'ahs, as pointed out in al-Fath. Contemplate. Therefore, and Allah knows best, he said: 'disdain' until 'resembles'. The surahs do not harm him because they are from the Quran, and reciting what is from the Quran is obedience like reciting a surah from among the surahs. Qadi Khan restricted it to being outside of prayer, so it is apparent that if it is during prayer, it is disliked, so it is a restriction of his statement 'not the reverse'. Then he said in al-Bada'i: If he recites an ayah of sajdah and there are people present, if they are in wudu and prepared for prostration, he recites it loudly; if they are not prepared, he should lower his recitation, because if he recites it loudly, he would impose something on them that they might be lazy in performing, thus falling into sin. End. The commentator mentioned: If he recites the ayah of sajdah except the letter at its end, he does not prostrate; if he recites the letter of sajdah alone, he does not prostrate unless he recites most of the ayah of sajdah with the letter of sajdah. In Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If he recites and prostrates and is silent and does not recite and draws near, the prostration becomes obligatory. End. In Fatawa Qadi Khan: A man heard the ayah of sajdah from a group, each one uttering one letter, he is not required to prostrate because he did not hear it from one person. And Allah Almighty knows best, and He is most merciful to His servants.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on sujud al-tilawa rulings. It covers several points: (1) Following the imam in sujud: The congregation prostrates with the imam, and it is recommended not to raise their heads before him. This is not considered actual following (iqtida') because if the imam's prostration becomes invalid for a reason that does not affect them, their prostration remains valid. (2) The reciter is not required to go forward or stand in a row; he prostrates wherever he is, and others follow. For a woman leading a man in this prostration is permissible according to Abu Bakr. (3) Intention and takbir: The reciter intends in his heart and says 'I prostrate for tilawa prostration' and 'Allahu Akbar'. (4) The main ruling: It is disliked (makruh) to recite a surah and deliberately skip the ayah of sajdah, but not the reverse (i.e., reciting only the sajdah ayah is not disliked). The reasoning: skipping resembles disdain; reciting alone is a sign of haste. Imam Muhammad prefers reciting one or two ayahs before or after to avoid misunderstanding. (5) Reciting all sajdah ayahs in one sitting: Al-Bada'i initially said it is disliked because it breaks the order of the Quran, citing the verse 'follow its recitation'. However, he later contradicted this, saying that reciting an ayah from among surahs does not harm, as it is like reciting one surah from among many. The commentary resolves this by explaining that changing the composition only occurs by omitting part of a surah, not by selecting individual ayahs. (6) If reciting an ayah of sajdah in front of people: if they are prepared to prostrate, recite loudly; if not, lower the voice to avoid causing them sin through laziness. (7) Partial recitation: if one recites the ayah except its last letter, no prostration; if one recites only the verse of sajdah itself, no prostration unless one recites most of the ayah including the sajdah letter. (8) If one hears the ayah from a group each saying a letter, no prostration is required. These rulings are based on specific conditions and aim to preserve the dignity of the Quran and the proper manner of recitation.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawa): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran (ayat as-sajdah).
النظم (al-nazm): The composition/arrangement of the Quran in its known order.
التأليف (al-ta'lif): The composition/structure of the Quran in terms of order of verses and surahs.

According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting all sajdah ayahs in one gathering with immediate prostration after each?
A) Disliked because it changes the Quranic composition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits reciting all sajdah verses in one sitting with immediate prostration; it is not a change to the Quranic composition.

Practical Conditions for Sujud al-Tilawa: Following the Imam, Intention, and Recitation Etiquette
Set of practical rulings with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the practical conditions for sujud al-tilawa regarding following the imam, intention, volume of recitation, and partial recitation.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawa has specific conditions: following the imam is not iqtida', intention is internal, and recitation volume depends on audience readiness.

Beyond the core ruling, sujud al-tilawa involves practical rules for congregation, intention, and voice modulation. This lesson covers the conditions that affect its performance.

Guided Path
1
Rule on following the imam
When the imam prostrates for tilawa, the congregation prostrates with him. It is recommended not to raise heads before the imam. This is not considered formal following (iqtida') because if the imam's prostration becomes invalid due to a reason that does not affect them, their prostration remains valid.
The reciter may be anywhere; no need to form rows.
2
Intention and takbir
The reciter should intend the sujud in the heart and say 'I prostrate to Allah for the tilawa prostration, Allahu Akbar'.
This is like the takbir for prayer.
3
Loud vs quiet recitation
If people are present and are in wudu and prepared to prostrate, recite the sajdah verse loudly. If they are not prepared, lower the voice to avoid causing them sin through laziness.
This is for the reciter's consideration.
4
Partial recitation of the sajdah verse
If one recites the sajdah verse except its last letter, no prostration is required. If one recites only the letter of sajdah (e.g., 'يسجدون' without the full verse), no prostration unless most of the verse is recited with that letter.
The threshold is reciting most of the verse including the sajdah word.
5
Hearing from a group
If a person hears the sajdah verse from a group where each person says a letter, he is not required to prostrate because he did not hear the complete verse from one person.
Prostration is only wajib when the complete verse is heard from one reciter.

Source Text

قوله (وكره أن يقرأ سورة ويدع آية السجدة لا عكسه) لأنه يشبه الاستنكاف عنها عمداً في الأول وفي الثاني مبادراً لها . قال :محمد وأحب إلى أن يقرأ قبلها آية أو آيتين . وذكر قاضيخان إن قرأ معها آية أو آيتين فهو أحب وهذا أعم من الأول لصدقه بما إذا قرأ بعدها آية أو آيتين بخلاف الأول، وعلله بقوله دفعاً لوهم التفضيل أي تفضيل آي السجدة على غيرها إذ الكل من حيث إنه كلام الله تعالى في رتبة وإن كان لبعضها بسبب اشتماله على ذكر صفات الحق جل جلاله زيادة فضيلة باعتبار المذكور لا باعتبار من حيث هو قرآن . وفى الكافي : قيل من قرأ آي السجدة كلها في مجلس واحد وسجد لكل منها كفاه الله ما أهمه. وما ذكر في البدائع في كراهة ترك آية السجدة من سورة يقرأها لأن فيه قطعاً لنظم القرآن وتغييراً لتأليفه واتباع النظم والتأليف مأمور به قال الله تعالى فإذا قرأناه فاتبع قرآنه القيامة : ۱۸] أي تأليفه فكان التغيير مكروهاً يقتضي كراهة ذلك . كذا في فتح القدير . وأقول : وإن كان ذلك مقتضاه لكن صرح بعده في البدائع بخلافه فقال : ولو قرأ آية السجدة من بين
من
سقطاً [؟] لأن الذي رأيته في الظهيرية وكذا في التتارخانية معزياً إليها : وإذا رفع رأسه من السجود يقوم ثم يقعد. وكذا قال في شرح المنية وفي الظهيرية أنه يستحب القيام بعد الرفع منها أيضاً قوله : (يقتضي كراهة ذلك) خبر عن ما في قوله وما ذكر في البدائع أي يقتضي الكراهة في قراءة آي السجدة كلها في مجلس قوله : لكن صرح بعده في البدائع بخلافه ظاهره أن كلامه متناقض لأنه يفيد أن ما صرح به بعده فيه تغيير لتأليفه والأحسن ما في شرح المنية حيث قال: وفيه نظر لأن تغيير التأليف إنما يحصل بإسقاط بعض الكلمات أو الآيات من السورة لا بذكر كلمة أو آية منها على ما مر أن قراءة آية من بين الآيات كقراءة سورة من بين السور. فكما لا يكون قراءة سور متفرقة من أثناء القرآن مغيراً للتأليف والنظم لا يكون قراءة آية من كل سورة مغيراً له، نعم يقتضي أنه لو ترك آية السجدة من آخر السورة لا يكره وفيه ما فيه ا هـ . أي فالأولى أن يذكر صاحب البدائع ولا ولأنه لا يرد هذا الأخير. هذا وما نقله الرملي عن المقدسي من أن قراءة تلك الآيات متوالية في مجلس تغيير للنظم وإحداث تأليف جديد بخلاف ما صرح به في البدائع بعد لأن تلك آية مفردة ا هـ . ظاهر فيما لو أخر السجدات لما بعد التلاوة، أما لو سجد عقب كل آية فلا لأن ذلك فاصل للتأليف كما قالوا فيما لو انتقل من آية إلى أخرى من سورة واحدة في ركعتين لا يكره إذا كان بينهما آيتان فأكثر ولو في ركعة كره مطلقاً كما نبه عليه في شرح المنية، وكذا قراءة سورتين فصل بينهما بسورتين يكره في كل ركعة لا ركعتين كما نبه عليه في الفتح تأمل. ولذا والله تعالى أعلم قال
الاستنكاف حتى
يشبه

السور لم يضره ذلك لأنها من القرآن وقراءة ما هو من القرآن طاعة كقراءة سورة من بين السور. وقيده قاضيخان بأن يكون في غير الصلاة فظاهر أنه لو كان في الصلاة كره فهو مقيد لقوله لا عكسه. ثم قال في البدائع ولو قرأ آية السجدة وعنده ناس فإن كانوا متوضئين متأهبين للسجدة قرأها جهراً، وإن كانوا غير متأهبين ينبغي أن يخفض قراءته لأنه لو جهر بها لصار موجباً عليهم شيئاً ربما يتكاسلون عن أدائه فيقعون في المعصية اهـ. وذكر الشارح : : ولو قرأ آية السجدة إلا الحرف الذي في آخرها لا يسجد، ولو قرأ الحرف الذي يسجد فيه وحده لا يسجد إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة بحرف السجدة. وفي مختصر البحر : لو قرأ وسجد وسكت ولم يقرأ واقترب تلزمه السجدة .اهـ. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : رجل سمع آية السجدة من قوم من كل واحد منهم حرفاً ليس عليه أن يسجد لأنه لم يسمعها من والله سبحانه أعلم وبعباده أرحم .
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawa: They prostrate behind him, and it is recommended that the people do not raise their heads before him, and it is not really following because if the imam's prostration becomes invalid due to a reason that does not extend to them. In al-Mujtaba, attributed to Shaykh al-Islam: The reciter is not commanded to go ahead nor to form rows, but he prostrates and they prostrate with him wherever and however they are. Abu Bakr mentioned that a woman is suitable as an imam for a man in it. End. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Then when he intends to prostrate, he intends it in his heart and says with his tongue 'I prostrate to Allah for the tilawa prostration, Allahu Akbar' just as he says 'I pray to Allah Almighty such a prayer.' : He said (It is disliked to recite a surah and leave out the ayah of sajdah, not the reverse) because it resembles intentional disdain in the first, and in the second, hastening to it. Muhammad said: I prefer that he recite before it one or two ayahs. Qadi Khan mentioned: If he recites with it one or two ayahs, it is better, and this is more general than the first because it includes if he recites after it one or two ayahs, unlike the first, and he explained it as repelling the illusion of preferring the ayahs of sajdah over others, since all are at the same level insofar as they are the speech of Allah, although some have extra virtue due to mentioning the attributes of the Truth, but not as Quran. In al-Kafi: It is said that whoever recites all the ayahs of sajdah in one gathering and prostrates for each, Allah suffices him for what concerns him. And what was mentioned in al-Bada'i about the dislike of leaving out the ayah of sajdah from a surah he recites, because it involves cutting the arrangement of the Quran and changing its composition, and following the arrangement and composition is commanded. Allah Almighty said: 'So when We have recited it, then follow its recitation' (al-Qiyamah 75:18), i.e., its composition. So changing it is disliked, necessitating that dislike. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And I say: Although that is its implication, he later stated in al-Bada'i contrary to it, saying: If he recites the ayah of sajdah from among the surahs, it does not harm him. This is because he read 'from among the surahs' [؟]... For what I saw in al-Zuhayriyya and also in al-Tatarkhaniyya attributed to it: When he raises his head from prostration, he stands then sits. Likewise stated in Sharh al-Munya and in al-Zuhayriyya that it is recommended to stand after raising from it. His statement (necessitates dislike of that) is a report about what was in his statement 'and what was mentioned in al-Bada'i', i.e., it necessitates dislike in reciting all the ayahs of sajdah in one gathering. His statement: But he later stated in al-Bada'i contrary to it, apparently his speech is contradictory because it indicates that what he stated later involves changing its composition. The best is what is in Sharh al-Munya where he said: There is a problem because changing the composition only occurs by dropping some words or ayahs from the surah, not by mentioning a word or ayah from it, as previously stated that reciting an ayah from among the ayahs is like reciting a surah from among the surahs. So just as reciting scattered surahs from the Quran does not change the composition and arrangement, reciting an ayah from each surah does not change it. Yes, it would imply that if he leaves out the ayah of sajdah from the end of the surah, it is not disliked, but there is something in it. End. That is, it is better to mention the author of al-Bada'i... This and what al-Ramli narrated from al-Maqdisi that reading those ayahs consecutively in a gathering is a change of arrangement and creating a new composition, contrary to what was stated in al-Bada'i later because that is a single ayah. End. It is apparent if he delays the prostrations until after the recitation. But if he prostrates immediately after each ayah, then it is not, because that separates the composition, as they said regarding moving from one ayah to another from the same surah in two rak'ahs, it is not disliked if there are two or more ayahs between them; but in one rak'ah, it is disliked absolutely, as pointed out in Sharh al-Munya. Likewise, reciting two surahs with two surahs separating them is disliked in each rak'ah but not in two rak'ahs, as pointed out in al-Fath. Contemplate. Therefore, and Allah knows best, he said: 'disdain' until 'resembles'. The surahs do not harm him because they are from the Quran, and reciting what is from the Quran is obedience like reciting a surah from among the surahs. Qadi Khan restricted it to being outside of prayer, so it is apparent that if it is during prayer, it is disliked, so it is a restriction of his statement 'not the reverse'. Then he said in al-Bada'i: If he recites an ayah of sajdah and there are people present, if they are in wudu and prepared for prostration, he recites it loudly; if they are not prepared, he should lower his recitation, because if he recites it loudly, he would impose something on them that they might be lazy in performing, thus falling into sin. End. The commentator mentioned: If he recites the ayah of sajdah except the letter at its end, he does not prostrate; if he recites the letter of sajdah alone, he does not prostrate unless he recites most of the ayah of sajdah with the letter of sajdah. In Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If he recites and prostrates and is silent and does not recite and draws near, the prostration becomes obligatory. End. In Fatawa Qadi Khan: A man heard the ayah of sajdah from a group, each one uttering one letter, he is not required to prostrate because he did not hear it from one person. And Allah Almighty knows best, and He is most merciful to His servants.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on sujud al-tilawa rulings. It covers several points: (1) Following the imam in sujud: The congregation prostrates with the imam, and it is recommended not to raise their heads before him. This is not considered actual following (iqtida') because if the imam's prostration becomes invalid for a reason that does not affect them, their prostration remains valid. (2) The reciter is not required to go forward or stand in a row; he prostrates wherever he is, and others follow. For a woman leading a man in this prostration is permissible according to Abu Bakr. (3) Intention and takbir: The reciter intends in his heart and says 'I prostrate for tilawa prostration' and 'Allahu Akbar'. (4) The main ruling: It is disliked (makruh) to recite a surah and deliberately skip the ayah of sajdah, but not the reverse (i.e., reciting only the sajdah ayah is not disliked). The reasoning: skipping resembles disdain; reciting alone is a sign of haste. Imam Muhammad prefers reciting one or two ayahs before or after to avoid misunderstanding. (5) Reciting all sajdah ayahs in one sitting: Al-Bada'i initially said it is disliked because it breaks the order of the Quran, citing the verse 'follow its recitation'. However, he later contradicted this, saying that reciting an ayah from among surahs does not harm, as it is like reciting one surah from among many. The commentary resolves this by explaining that changing the composition only occurs by omitting part of a surah, not by selecting individual ayahs. (6) If reciting an ayah of sajdah in front of people: if they are prepared to prostrate, recite loudly; if not, lower the voice to avoid causing them sin through laziness. (7) Partial recitation: if one recites the ayah except its last letter, no prostration; if one recites only the verse of sajdah itself, no prostration unless one recites most of the ayah including the sajdah letter. (8) If one hears the ayah from a group each saying a letter, no prostration is required. These rulings are based on specific conditions and aim to preserve the dignity of the Quran and the proper manner of recitation.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawa): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran (ayat as-sajdah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on reciting the sajdah verse loudly when people are present who are not prepared for prostration?
A) It is recommended to recite loudly to encourage them.
B) It is obligatory to recite loudly.
C) It is better to lower the voice to avoid imposing a hardship on them.
D) It makes no difference.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawa has specific practical conditions: following the imam is not iqtida', intention is required, and recitation volume depends on audience readiness.

Travel Prayer: The Condition of Three Days Moderate Journey
Explanation of the condition for shortening prayer: three days moderate travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for shortening prayer (qasr) and explain how the phrase 'siran wasatan' defines the required travel distance.

Core Idea
A journey of three days at moderate pace triggers the obligation to shorten prayer.

This lesson examines the first condition for qasr in the Hanafi school: the minimum travel distance. The matn states that a traveler must intend a journey of three days at a moderate pace. The commentary by al-Zayla'i clarifies that this is an estimation of distance, not speed. Understanding this distinction is critical to correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that qasr (shortening prayer) is the act being discussed, and its ruling is wajib when conditions are met.
Qasr is not a concession but an obligation for qualifying travelers.
2
Isolate the condition stated in the matn
The matn says: 'Whoever passes the houses of his town intending a moderate journey of three days... shortens.' This gives two conditions: leaving the town and intending a three-day moderate journey.
The phrase 'siran wasatan' is key.
3
Parse 'siran wasatan' using al-Zayla'i's commentary
Al-Zayla'i explains that 'wasatan' (moderate) is an adjective for an omitted infinitive, and the actual meaning is 'the distance covered in three days at moderate pace.' It is an estimation, not a requirement to travel for exactly three days.
The emphasis is on distance, not speed or duration.
4
Understand the condition is about distance, not speed
The moderate pace (siran wasatan) serves as a measure to estimate the distance. The same distance covered faster or slower still triggers the ruling.
5
Note the estimated distance in modern terms
Based on three days moderate travel, the estimated distance is approximately 77-84 km (48-52 miles). This is the mufta bihi threshold.
This is a later specification; the primary source uses the temporal measure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسافر
من جاوز بيوت مصره مريداً سيراً وسطاً ثلاثة أيام في بر أو بحر أو جبل قصر
باب صلاة المسافر
قول المصنف : (سيراً وسطاً) قال الشارح الزيلعي : وسطاً صفة لمصدر محذوف والعامل فيه السير المذكور لأنه مقدر بأن والفعل تقديره مريداً أن يسير سيراً وسطاً في ثلاثة أيام، ومراده التقدير لا أن فيها سيراً وسطاً ولا أن يسير يريد ذلك السير وإنما يريد قدر تلك المسافة، وكان ينبغي أن يقول مريداً سيراً وسطاً في بر أو بحر أي مريداً مسيرة ثلاثة أيام بسير وسط، أو نقول: في كلامه تقديم وتأخير وحذف تقديره مريداً ثلاثة أيام سيراً وسطاً أي بسير وسط ا هـ. قال في النهر : ودعاه البحر الرائق ج ٢ م ١٥
Chapter of the Traveler
Whoever passes the houses of his town intending a moderate journey of three days on land, sea, or mountain, shortens. Chapter of Travel Prayer
He said: 'a moderate journey' – the commentator al-Zayla'i said: 'moderate' is an adjective for an omitted infinitive, and the agent is the mentioned journey because it is estimated with 'an' and the verb, the estimation being: intending to travel a moderate journey in three days. His intent is estimation, not that there is a moderate journey nor that he travels intending that journey; rather, he intends the distance of that journey. He should have said: intending a moderate journey on land or sea, i.e., intending a journey of three days at moderate pace. Or we say: in his wording there is fronting, delaying, and deletion; the estimation is: intending three days of moderate journey, i.e., at moderate pace. End. He said in al-Nahr: and al-Bahr al-Raiq called it...
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on travel prayer. The matn states that a traveler shortens prayer when he passes beyond the buildings of his town with the intention of traveling a distance that takes three days at a moderate pace, whether traveling by land, sea, or mountain. The commentary by al-Zayla'i explains the phrase 'siran wasatan' (a moderate journey). He clarifies that 'wasatan' (moderate) describes a deleted infinitive; the intended meaning is the distance, not a specific speed. The author (al-Bahr al-Raiq) suggests that the matn could be rephrased for clarity: the intent is to travel for three days at a moderate pace. The distance is approximately 48-52 miles (about 77-84 km) according to later Hanafi texts, though here it is defined temporally. The key point: the obligation to shorten prayer (qasr) is established when the journey meets this distance condition.

Key Terms
سيراً وسطاً (siran wasatan): A journey at moderate pace; the distance covered in three days by normal walking or riding without speed or delay.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayers to two rak'ahs during travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for shortening prayer while traveling?
A) Traveling for three days at a fast pace.
B) Passing beyond the town houses with intention of a three-day moderate journey.
C) Traveling at least 100 miles.
D) Being outside one's town for one day.

Key Takeaway
Shortening prayer becomes obligatory when a traveler intends a journey of three days at moderate pace, which in modern terms is approximately 77-84 km.

Sajdah Tilawah: Recitation in Prayer and Etiquette with Listeners
Rulings on reciting sajdah verses in and out of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on reciting a verse of prostration inside prayer and determine when to recite it loudly or softly in the presence of others.

Core Idea
Reciting Quran is obedience, but inside prayer loud sajdah recitation is disliked if it obligates unprepared listeners.

This lesson covers two interrelated rulings from al-Bahr al-Raiq: the permissibility of reciting a verse of prostration in prayer (with a makruh qualification) and the etiquette of reciting it in the presence of others — whether to raise or lower one's voice depending on their readiness to perform the sajdah. The Hanafi school balances individual worship with communal responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Reciting any Quranic verse, including a sajdah verse, is an act of obedience (ta'ah) and is permissible outside prayer.
The default ruling is that there is no harm in reciting a surah containing a sajdah verse.
2
Apply Qadikhan's qualification
Qadikhan restricts the default ruling: if the recitation occurs inside prayer, it becomes makruh (disliked). This is a specific Hanafi nuance.
The dislike is due to the potential disruption of the prayer flow or obligation on others.
3
Assess the listener's state
When reciting for others, check if they are in wudu and prepared to prostrate. If yes, recite loudly so they can join; if not, lower the voice.
This ruling from al-Bada'i' applies outside prayer.
4
Identify the reason for lowering
Reciting loudly to unprepared listeners obligates them to perform sajdah, which they might neglect, causing them to sin. Lowering the voice prevents this.
This shows the welfare of others is a leading consideration.
5
Synthesize the overall fiqh ruling
Outside prayer: no restriction on reciting verses with sajdah. Inside prayer: makruh. With unprepared listeners: must lower voice to avoid sin.
This synthesis reflects the balanced approach of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السور لم يضره ذلك لأنها من القرآن وقراءة ما هو من القرآن طاعة كقراءة سورة من بين السور. وقيده قاضيخان بأن يكون في غير الصلاة فظاهر أنه لو كان في الصلاة كره فهو مقيد لقوله لا عكسه. ثم قال في البدائع ولو قرأ آية السجدة وعنده ناس فإن كانوا متوضئين متأهبين للسجدة قرأها جهراً، وإن كانوا غير متأهبين ينبغي أن يخفض قراءته لأنه لو جهر بها لصار موجباً عليهم شيئاً ربما يتكاسلون عن أدائه فيقعون في المعصية اهـ. وذكر الشارح : : ولو قرأ آية السجدة إلا الحرف الذي في آخرها لا يسجد، ولو قرأ الحرف الذي يسجد فيه وحده لا يسجد إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة بحرف السجدة. وفي مختصر البحر : لو قرأ وسجد وسكت ولم يقرأ واقترب تلزمه السجدة .اهـ. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : رجل سمع آية السجدة من قوم من كل واحد منهم حرفاً ليس عليه أن يسجد لأنه لم يسمعها من والله سبحانه أعلم وبعباده أرحم .
The surah does not harm him because it is from the Quran, and reciting what is from the Quran is obedience, like reciting a surah from among the surahs. Qadikhan qualified it to be outside prayer, so it is apparent that if it were in prayer, it would be disliked; so it is restricted to his statement, not the opposite. Then he said in al-Bada'i: If he recites a verse of prostration and has people with him, if they are in a state of wudu and prepared for prostration, he recites it loudly; if they are not prepared, he should lower his recitation because if he recites it loudly, he would obligate them to something they might be lazy in performing, thus falling into sin. The commentator said: If he recites a verse of prostration except the letter at its end, he does not prostrate; if he recites the letter alone in which prostration is made, he does not prostrate unless he recites most of the verse of prostration including the letter of prostration. In Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If he recites and prostrates and remains silent and does not recite and approaches, the prostration becomes obligatory upon him. In Fatawa Qadikhan: A man who hears a verse of prostration from a group, each one contributing one letter, does not have to prostrate because he did not hear it from one person. Allah the Exalted knows best and is more merciful to His servants.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage discusses several rulings regarding sajdah tilawah (prostration upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration). It states that reciting a surah from the Quran is an act of obedience, and there is no harm in reciting a verse like from surahs. Qadikhan qualifies that this is only outside prayer; if in prayer, it is disliked (makruh). Al-Bada'i' mentions that if one recites a verse of prostration while people are present who are in a state of wudu and prepared for prostration, he should recite it loudly; otherwise, he should lower his voice to avoid causing them to fall into sin by neglecting the prostration. The commentator (al-Sharih) states that if one recites a verse of prostration except the letter at the end, he does not prostrate. If he recites only the letter of prostration alone, he does not prostrate unless he recites most of the verse of prostration including the letter of prostration. In Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If one recites and prostrates and remains silent without reciting, and approaches, the sajdah becomes obligatory. In Fatawa Qadikhan: A person who hears a verse of prostration from a group, each uttering one letter, does not have to prostrate because he did not hear the full verse from one person. Allah knows best.

Key Terms
آية السجدة (ayat al-sajdah): A verse in the Quran that contains a command or recommendation to prostrate.
السجدة (al-sajdah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it recommended to recite a verse of prostration loudly?
A) Always, to fulfill the obligation.
B) When the listeners are in wudu and prepared for sajdah.
C) Only in prayer.
D) When the listeners are not prepared.

Key Takeaway
Reciting a verse of prostration outside prayer is permissible but inside prayer it is disliked according to Qadikhan; with unprepared listeners, lower the voice to avoid causing sin.

Conditions for Wujub of Sajdah Tilawah: Completeness of Recitation
Rulings on incomplete recitation of sajdah verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the recitation of a verse of prostration is incomplete and state whether sajdah is obligatory, applying the Hanafi conditions.

Core Idea
Sajdah tilawah is only wajib if the reciter recites the full verse or most of it including the prostration letter.

This lesson examines the conditions for sajdah tilawah when the recitation of the verse is partial. The commentator (al-Sharih) and Mukhtasar al-Bahr provide three scenarios: missing the last letter, reciting only the prostration letter, and reciting and prostrating without further recitation. Understanding these conditions ensures that one does not perform or omit sajdah incorrectly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario: missing last letter
If a person recites a verse of prostration but omits the last letter (the letter of prostration, i.e., the letter at the end of the verse that indicates prostration), no sajdah is required.
The prostration is specifically tied to that letter.
2
Identify the second scenario: only the prostration letter
If one recites only the letter of prostration (e.g., the word 'asjud' or similar) without the rest of the verse, no sajdah is required unless he recites most of the verse including that letter.
The mere utterance of the prostration word is insufficient.
3
Identify the third scenario: reciting and prostrating without further recitation
If one recites the verse, prostrates, and remains silent (without reciting further) and then approaches (i.e., continues the recitation later?), the sajdah is still obligatory upon him.
This indicates that once the verse is recited, the obligation is established.
4
Extract the condition (shart)
The common condition is that the recitation must include the prostration letter and be a majority of the verse. The third scenario reinforces that the obligation is fixed upon complete recitation.
The school emphasizes the meaning and completeness.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
If one recites half of a sajdah verse without the prostration letter, no sajdah. If one recites three-fourths including the prostration letter, sajdah is wajib.
This clarifies the 'majority' criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السور لم يضره ذلك لأنها من القرآن وقراءة ما هو من القرآن طاعة كقراءة سورة من بين السور. وقيده قاضيخان بأن يكون في غير الصلاة فظاهر أنه لو كان في الصلاة كره فهو مقيد لقوله لا عكسه. ثم قال في البدائع ولو قرأ آية السجدة وعنده ناس فإن كانوا متوضئين متأهبين للسجدة قرأها جهراً، وإن كانوا غير متأهبين ينبغي أن يخفض قراءته لأنه لو جهر بها لصار موجباً عليهم شيئاً ربما يتكاسلون عن أدائه فيقعون في المعصية اهـ. وذكر الشارح : : ولو قرأ آية السجدة إلا الحرف الذي في آخرها لا يسجد، ولو قرأ الحرف الذي يسجد فيه وحده لا يسجد إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة بحرف السجدة. وفي مختصر البحر : لو قرأ وسجد وسكت ولم يقرأ واقترب تلزمه السجدة .اهـ. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : رجل سمع آية السجدة من قوم من كل واحد منهم حرفاً ليس عليه أن يسجد لأنه لم يسمعها من والله سبحانه أعلم وبعباده أرحم .
The surah does not harm him because it is from the Quran, and reciting what is from the Quran is obedience, like reciting a surah from among the surahs. Qadikhan qualified it to be outside prayer, so it is apparent that if it were in prayer, it would be disliked; so it is restricted to his statement, not the opposite. Then he said in al-Bada'i: If he recites a verse of prostration and has people with him, if they are in a state of wudu and prepared for prostration, he recites it loudly; if they are not prepared, he should lower his recitation because if he recites it loudly, he would obligate them to something they might be lazy in performing, thus falling into sin. The commentator said: If he recites a verse of prostration except the letter at its end, he does not prostrate; if he recites the letter alone in which prostration is made, he does not prostrate unless he recites most of the verse of prostration including the letter of prostration. In Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If he recites and prostrates and remains silent and does not recite and approaches, the prostration becomes obligatory upon him. In Fatawa Qadikhan: A man who hears a verse of prostration from a group, each one contributing one letter, does not have to prostrate because he did not hear it from one person. Allah the Exalted knows best and is more merciful to His servants.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage discusses several rulings regarding sajdah tilawah (prostration upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration). It states that reciting a surah from the Quran is an act of obedience, and there is no harm in reciting a verse like from surahs. Qadikhan qualifies that this is only outside prayer; if in prayer, it is disliked (makruh). Al-Bada'i' mentions that if one recites a verse of prostration while people are present who are in a state of wudu and prepared for prostration, he should recite it loudly; otherwise, he should lower his voice to avoid causing them to fall into sin by neglecting the prostration. The commentator (al-Sharih) states that if one recites a verse of prostration except the letter at the end, he does not prostrate. If he recites only the letter of prostration alone, he does not prostrate unless he recites most of the verse of prostration including the letter of prostration. In Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If one recites and prostrates and remains silent without reciting, and approaches, the sajdah becomes obligatory. In Fatawa Qadikhan: A person who hears a verse of prostration from a group, each uttering one letter, does not have to prostrate because he did not hear the full verse from one person. Allah knows best.

Key Terms
آية السجدة (ayat al-sajdah): A verse in the Quran that contains a command or recommendation to prostrate.
السجدة (al-sajdah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, if someone recites only the prostration letter of a verse, when does sajdah become obligatory?
A) Always.
B) Only if he recites most of the verse including that letter.
C) Only if he recites the full verse.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah tilawah is only wajib when the recitation includes the prostration letter and constitutes most of the verse; incomplete recitation does not obligate sajdah.

Group Recitation: Hearing Sajdah Verse from Multiple People
Ruling on hearing sajdah verse from multiple people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when hearing a verse of prostration from multiple people does not obligate sajdah tilawah, applying the Hanafi condition of hearing from a single reciter.

Core Idea
Hearing a verse of prostration from multiple people each contributing one letter does not make the sajdah wajib.

This short but important ruling from Fatawa Qadikhan addresses a specific scenario: if a verse of prostration is heard from a group of people, each person uttering one letter (or a part), the listener is not obligated to perform sajdah tilawah. The reason is that the verse was not heard from a single individual in its complete form. This reflects the Hanafi principle that the obligation arises from hearing a complete verse from one source.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A man hears the letters of a verse of prostration being recited by different people, each contributing one letter.
Example: Person A says 'أ', Person B says 'س', etc.
2
Identify the ruling
According to Fatawa Qadikhan, the listener does not have to perform sajdah (ليس عليه أن يسجد).
This is a specific application of the condition that the verse must be heard from one reciter.
3
Identify the basis (illah)
The ruling is because he did not hear the verse from one person (من والله? 'min wahid'? Actually the text says 'لم يسمعها من والله' which seems to mean 'he did not hear it from one source').
The reason is the lack of a single source of the full verse.
4
Extract the general principle
The obligation of sajdah tilawah upon hearing requires that the verse be heard in its entirety from a single reciter. If heard piecemeal from multiple people, no obligation.
This ensures clear attribution and completeness.
5
Apply to similar scenarios
If someone hears a verse from a recording where different speakers say separate words, the ruling would be similar.
Modern application: group recitation in a classroom may create similar situations.

Conditions for Qasr: Intention of Three-Day Travel and Leaving the Dwelling Area
Definition of travel distance and conditions for qasr, with detailed spatial rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main conditions for shortening prayer in the Hanafi school and apply them to determine when a traveler begins qasr.

Core Idea
Qasr begins only when you intend a three-day moderate journey and leave all dwellings, including suburbs.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the foundational ruling for qasr al-salah in the Hanafi school. The matn states that whoever passes the dwellings of his city intending a three-day moderate journey shortens the four-rak'ah fard. But what does 'passing the dwellings' mean? Does it include suburbs? What about villages connected to the city? The commentator unravels these details, grounding the ruling in the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions.

Guided Path
1
State the matn and identify the core ruling
The matn says: 'Whoever passes the dwellings of his city, intending a moderate travel of three days... shortens the four obligatory rak'ahs.' This is the basis for the Hanafi position that qasr is wajib (per Abu Hanifa) for the traveler.
The ruling applies only to four-rak'ah prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha). Fajr and Maghrib are not shortened.
2
Analyze the condition of intention (niyyah)
The traveler must intend to cover a distance of three days' moderate travel. Without this specific intention, even if traveling far, qasr does not apply.
The three-day distance is estimated at approximately 48-56 miles (sayr wasat).
3
Examine the spatial condition: leaving the dwellings
Qasr begins when one passes the dwellings of his city, including its rabad (suburbs). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether one must also pass villages connected to the rabad.
Qadikhan's detail: If a connected village is within a bowshot (300-400 cubits) and no farmland in between, it is considered part of the city, and qasr begins only after passing it.
4
Apply the rules to a concrete scenario
Given a scenario, determine the exact point when qasr starts: e.g., a traveler leaving a city with a connected village within a bowshot must pass that village before shortening.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the hukm of qasr
Abu Hanifa holds qasr is wajib; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. The mufta bihi (operative view) follows the Sahibayn, but the matn here reflects Abu Hanifa's view.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the conditions discussed; both sides agree on the conditions.

In al-Nahr: What is in al-Kafi, although it is apparent that he recited the verse of prostration consecutively and then prostrated for it, it is possible that he prostrated for each one after its recitation, and this is not disliked. What is in the book from his statement 'not the opposite' includes this because there is no change in the order of the Quran, so it is understood accordingly. Then what al-Maqdisi said is based on what was noted in al-Nahr that what is in al-Bada'i' is only about a surah (singular), not surahs (plural) as the author mentioned, for it is a distortion of his statement: 'And Qadikhan qualified it' meaning he qualified the lack of dislike of the opposite to be outside prayer. He said in al-Dhakhira: They said: It must be disliked in the state of prayer because confining to a single verse in prayer is disliked. Chapter of the Prayer of the Traveler. The statement of the author: 'moderate travel' – al-Zaylai said: 'moderate' is an adjective for a deleted infinitive, and the operator is the previously mentioned 'travel' because it is estimated with 'an' and the verb, the estimate being 'intending to travel a moderate travel in three days'. His intent is estimation, not that there is a moderate travel nor that he intends that travel, but rather he intends the measure of that distance. It would have been better to say 'intending a moderate travel by land or sea', i.e., intending a journey of three days with moderate travel. Or we say: In his speech there is fronting and delaying and deletion; the estimate is 'intending three days of moderate travel', i.e., with moderate travel. He said in al-Nahr: And al-Bahr al-Ra'iq called it... [page 226] ...for clarity. For this reason, our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) interpreted his statement 'and udhiyah (sacrificial animal) is waived for the poor and the traveler' as leaving the town or village until the udhiyah is waived by that amount. This is in al-Mujtaba. And it is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that among the rulings that change with legal travel is the dropping of udhiyah, and he made it like qasr. Its apparent meaning is that it is not dropped except with legal travel, and its verification will come in its place. The addition in 'prayer of the traveler' is the addition of a thing to its condition and the action to its doer. His statement: 'Whoever passes the dwellings of his city, intending a moderate travel of three days by land, sea, or mountain, shortens the four obligatory rak'ahs' is an explanation of the location where qasr begins, the condition for qasr, its duration, and its ruling. As for the first, it is passing the dwellings of the city, based on the authentic report that he (peace be upon him) shortened Asr at Dhu al-Hulayfah. And from Ali that he left Basra and prayed Zuhr four then said: 'If we had passed this khuss (hut made of reeds) we would have prayed two rak'ahs.' Khuss is a house made of reeds. This is how it was recorded in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The rabad (suburb) of the city enters into the dwellings of the city, which is what is around the city of houses and dwellings. The sanctuary of the mosque is also called rabad. The apparent meaning of the author's statement is that passing the village connected to the rabad of the city is not a condition, and there is disagreement. The apparent meaning of al-Mujtaba favors that it is not a condition, which is also indicated by the words of the authors of the texts like al-Hidayah. Fath al-Qadir definitively stated that it is a condition and objected to al-Hidayah on that. Qadikhan in his Fatawa corrected that it is necessary to pass the village connected to the rabad of the city, contrary to the village connected to the courtyard of the city, because in that case, passing the courtyard is considered, not the village. The author did not mention passing the courtyard due to difference. Qadikhan detailed in his Fatawa: If between him and the city there is less than the distance of a bowshot and there is no farmland between them, then passing the courtyard is also considered; if there is farmland or the distance between him and the city is a bowshot, then passing the inhabited area of the city is considered. He was absolute in passing, so it refers to the side from which he departed, and passing a neighborhood parallel to him from the other side is not considered. If there is on the side from which he departed a neighborhood separate from the city, and in the old days it was connected to the city, he does not shorten prayer until he passes that neighborhood. This is in al-Khulasa. Al-Mujtaba mentioned that the measure of a bowshot is 300 to 400 cubits, which is the most correct. In al-Muhit: Likewise, if he returns from his travel to the city, he does not complete (to full prayer) until he enters the inhabited area. As for the second, it is that he intends a journey of three days; if he were to travel around the world without intending to cover that journey... to the point that there is nothing in the speech that operates on 'three', because it is not valid for 'intending' to operate on it, because then it would be an object, but the meaning is adverbial, and 'travel' is not (operating) because when the infinitive is described, it does not operate. So what he said is determined. But al-Ayni said: This strain is unnecessary; 'travel' can be the object of 'intending', and 'moderate' and 'three days' are its attributes, i.e., occurring in three days. His statement: 'Due to the lack of validity of intention and resolution from a boy.' I say: It is mentioned in al-Siraj and also in al-Tatarikhaniyya from al-Zahiriyya: A menstruating woman when she becomes pure from her menses, and between her and the destination is less than a journey of three days, she prays four, and that is the correct view. So let it be considered. In al-Sharnibalaliyya after attributing to Mukhtasar al-Zahiriyya: It is not hidden that she is not lower in rank than one who converts to Islam, so her right would be qasr like him. Apparently, this is based on the statement.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage covers the chapter on the traveler's prayer. It begins by explaining why this chapter is placed after the chapter on tilawah (recitation), as travel is an incidental condition like recitation but recitation is an act of worship in itself. The author defines travel linguistically as covering a distance without a specific time limit. Then follows a note from al-Nahr about a ruling on sajdah tilawah, clarifying a previous point. The main matn is then presented: 'Whoever passes the dwellings of his city, intending a moderate travel of three days by land, sea, or mountain, shortens the four-rak'ah obligatory prayer.' The commentator (Zaylai) explains the grammar, noting that 'moderate travel' qualifies a deleted infinitive. He discusses the meaning of 'intending' and the estimate of distance. Then follows a detailed discussion of what constitutes 'passing the dwellings' (mujawezah buyut misrihi). The correct view is that the traveler starts shortening prayer upon leaving the built-up area of the city, including its suburbs (rabad). There is a disagreement about whether one must also pass villages connected to the rabad. Qadikhan distinguishes based on distance and presence of farmland. The distance of a bowshot (ghalwah) is 300 to 400 cubits. Additionally, the intention to travel three days is essential; without intention, one does not shorten. The passage ends with rulings on a menstruating woman and a minor, noting that if a woman menstruates and the distance is less than three days, she prays full; but there is a view that she should shorten like a convert.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah obligatory prayer to two rak'ahs during travel.
سير وسط (sayr wasat): Moderate travel speed, used to estimate the distance of three days travel (approximately 48-56 miles in modern terms).
ربض (rabad): The suburb or surrounding built-up area of a city, including houses and dwellings.
غلوة (ghalwah): A bowshot, a unit of distance ranging from 300 to 400 cubits (approx. 150-200 meters).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary spatial requirement for beginning qasr (shortening prayer)?
A) Leaving the city walls.
B) Passing all dwellings of the city, including suburbs (rabad).
C) Reaching a point three miles outside the city.
D) Passing the last village in the region.

Key Takeaway
Qasr begins when the traveler leaves the built-up area of his city (including suburbs and connected villages within a bowshot per some scholars) with the intention of a three-day moderate journey.

Minimum Travel Period for Shortening Prayer: Three-Day Rule
Establishing the three-day minimum travel period for qasr and its application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi minimum travel period for shortening prayer and apply it to cases of uncertain journey length and change of legal status during travel.

Core Idea
Travel leniencies require a three-day journey; mere departure from one's city does not suffice.

The Hanafi school uniquely defines the traveller (musafir) as one who undertakes a journey of at least three days. This lesson unpacks that rule, its proof from the hadith of wiping, and its application to two subtle branch-cases: an amir who does not know his travel duration, and a boy and non-Muslim who become legally responsible mid-journey. By the end, you will understand why intention alone is insufficient without actual distance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
Locate the opening phrase 'three days is the period for not availing leniencies' and recognize that it sets the minimum travel duration for all travel concessions (qasr, wiping, etc.) in the Hanafi school.
This rule is based on the hadith about wiping for three days.
2
Examine the Proof (Dalil)
The hadith 'The resident wipes for one day and night, and the traveller for three days' is cited. Since the traveller is defined by the three-day period, all travel leniencies tied to being a traveller share this minimum.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but relied upon in Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Apply to the Amir Case
An amir leads an army with unknown travel duration. On the outward journey, if the distance is uncertain, he prays complete (as a resident) because the condition of a three-day journey is not yet certain. On return, if the actual travel would be three days, he shortens.
This shows that the actual distance, not mere intention, triggers the license.
4
Apply to the Boy and Christian Case
A boy (minor) and a Christian (adult) set out intending a three-day journey. The boy reaches puberty during travel; the Christian accepts Islam. The Christian shortens from that point because his prior valid intention counts; the boy prays complete because his initial intention was invalid (not legally responsible).
The remaining distance after valid intention is less than three days, so the Christian's shortening applies only if the remainder meets the condition.
5
Synthesize the Principle
The core principle: travel leniencies require both a valid intention (from a legally responsible person) and an actual journey of at least three days. If either is missing at the outset, the license does not apply until both conditions are met.
This principle resolves seemingly contradictory rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثلاثة أيام لا يترخص وعلى هذا قالوا: أمير خرج مع جيشه في طلب العدو ولم يعلم أين يدركهم فإنهم يصلون صلاة الإقامة في الذهاب وإن طالت المدة، وكذلك المكث [في الموضع؟]، في الرجوع فإن كانت مدة سفر قصروا وعلى اعتبار القصد تفرع في صبي ونصراني خرجا قاصدين مسيرة ثلاثة أيام ففي أثنائها بلغ الصبي وأسلم الكافر، يقصر الذي أسلم فيما بقي ويتم الذي بلغ لعدم صحة القصد والنية من الصبي حين أنشأ السفر بخلاف النصراني والباقي بعد صحة النية أقل من ثلاثة أيام وسيأتي أيضاً.
Three days is the period for not availing leniencies, and based on this they said: An amir who goes out with his army in pursuit of the enemy and does not know where he will overtake them – they pray the prayer of a resident (i.e., complete) on the outward journey even if the duration is long, and similarly staying in a place [؟], on the return if the journey duration is long they shorten. And based on consideration of intention, a branch-case arises: a boy and a Christian set out intending a three-day journey; during it the boy reaches puberty and the Christian accepts Islam. The one who accepts Islam shortens for the remainder, and the one who reached puberty prays complete due to the lack of valid intention and resolve from the boy when he initiated the journey, unlike the Christian. And what remains after valid intention is less than three days, and this will also come later.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing that the minimum travel period for leniencies (like shortening prayer and wiping over socks for three days) is a three-day journey. It begins by stating the rule: fewer than three days does not permit leniencies. Then it applies the rule to an amir (military commander) whose journey duration is unknown: while in active pursuit, he prays complete (as a resident) because the intention for travel is not directed toward a known destination? The text seems to say that if he stays in a place (maybe awaiting the enemy) he also prays complete, but on return if the actual travel time would be three days, he shortens. This shows that the actual distance matters, not just intent. Then it gives two branch-cases: a boy and a non-Muslim traveling. The boy's travel intention is not valid since he is not legally responsible; if he reaches puberty during the journey, he must pray complete from that point because his initial intention was deficient. The Christian, however, is originally a responsible adult; when he accepts Islam, his valid intention continues, so he shortens for the remainder of the journey (if the remainder is at least three days? Actually the text says 'and what remains after valid intention is less than three days' implying that if the remaining distance is less than three days, he completes; but the Christian shortens because his prior travel distance counts toward the three days? The text is ambiguous. The author notes that the complete discussion will come later. The proof for the three-day rule is indirectly referenced through the hadith about wiping (mentioned later in the full text). The commentary emphasizes that the three-day measure is the relied-upon criterion, not fixed distances like farsakhs. The examples illustrate that intention must be accompanied by actual travel distance for the license to apply.

Key Terms
مسافر (musafir): A person who undertakes a journey of at least three days travel to a single destination.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rakat prayers to two rakat when the travel condition is met.
إقامة (iqaamah): The state of being a resident, not travelling; performing prayers as complete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum travel duration for shortening prayer?
A) 15 farsakhs
B) One day's journey
C) Three days' journey
D) 48 miles

Key Takeaway
Travel leniencies require an actual journey of at least three days, coupled with a valid intention from a legally responsible person, as established by the hadith and illustrated by the branch-cases.
