Ruling on Becoming a Resident by Entering Hometown or Intending to Stay
Rulings on when a traveler becomes a resident in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a traveler becomes a resident (muqim) and apply the Hanafi ruling that entering the city with intention to reside or intending to stay 15 days makes completion of prayer obligatory.

Core Idea
A traveler becomes a resident by entering his hometown or by intending to stay 15 days in a suitable location.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the precise conditions under which a traveler (musafir) ceases to shorten prayers and must complete them. It addresses critical distinctions: entering one's original hometown versus a new city, the role of intention, and the exception for the latecomer (lahiq). The proof from the hadith of 'Ali (RA) establishes that entering the city is a key requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is becoming a resident (muqim) for prayer. The ruling is fard 'ayn to complete the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of 'Ali (RA) narrated by Bukhari in a suspended form. 'Ali shortened prayer while seeing the houses of Kufa and did not complete until entering.
This is the primary textual proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that entering the city is a condition for becoming a resident. 'Ali did not consider himself a resident until actual entry, despite being within sight.
The operative phrase is 'not until we enter it'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi sources say that if the traveler returns before three days, mere intention to return suffices to become a resident. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq disagrees and insists on entry.
The difference hinges on the definition of the cause of travel.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author prefers the requirement of entry based on the hadith and the principle that the cause of travel is leaving homes with the intention of a three-day journey.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دخول مصره فشمل ما إذا نوى الإقامة به أولاً، وشمل ما إذا كان في الصلاة كما إذا سبقه حدث وليس عنده ماء فدخله للماء إلا اللاحق إذا أحدث ودخل مصره ليتوضأ لا يلزمه الإتمام ولا يصير مقيماً بدخوله المصر. كذا في الفتاوى الظهيرية. وشمل ما إذا كان سار ثلاثة أيام أو أقل لكن المذكور في الشرح أنه يتم إذا سار أقل بمجرد العزم على الرجوع وإن لم يدخل مصره لأنه نقض للسفر قبل الاستحكام إذ هو يحتمل النقض. قال في فتح القدير : وقياسه أن لا يحل فطره في رمضان إذا كان بينه وبين بلده يومان. وفي المجتبى : لا يبطل السفر إلا بنية الإقامة أو دخول الوطن أو الرجوع قبل الثلاثة ا هـ . والمذكور في الخانية والظهيرية وغيرهما أنه إذا رجع لحاجة نسيها ثم تذكرها فإن كان له وطن أصلي يصير مقيماً بمجرد العزم على الرجوع، وإن لم يكن له وطن أصلي يقصر ا هـ. والذي يظهر أنه لا بد من دخول المصر مطلقاً لأن العلة مفارقة البيوت قاصداً مسيرة ثلاثة أيام لا استكمال سفر ثلاثة أيام بدليل ثبوت حكم السفر بمجرد ذلك فقد تمت العلة لحكم السفر فيثبت حكمه ما ما لم تثبت علة حكم الإقامة وروى البخاري تعليقاً أن علياً خرج فقصر وهو يرى البيوت فلما قيل له : هذه الكوفة قال : لا حتى ندخلها، يريد أنه صلى ركعتين والكوفة بمرأى منهم فقيل له إلى آخره. وقيد بنية الإقامة لأنه لو دخل بلداً ولم ينو أنه يقيم فيها خمسة عشر يوماً وإنما يقول غداً أخرج أو بعد غد أخرج حتى بقي على ذلك سنين قصر . وفي المجتبى : والنية إنما تؤثر بخمس شرائط : أحدها ترك السير حتى لو نوى الإقامة وهو يسير لم يصح . وثانيها صلاحية الموضع حتى لو أقام في بحر أو جزيرة لم تصح واتحاد الموضع والمدة والاستقلال بالرأي اهـ. وأطلق النية فشمل الحكمية كما لو وصل الحاج إلى الشام وعلم أن القافلة إنما تخرج بعد خمسة عشر يوماً وعزم أن لا يخرج إلا معهم لا يقصر لأنه كناوي الإقامة. كذا في المحيط. وشمل ما إذا نواها في خلال الصلاة في الوقت فإنه يتم، سواء كان في أولها أو وسطها أو في آخرها وسواء كان منفرداً أو مقتدياً أو مدركاً أو مسبوقاً. أما اللاحق إذا أدرك أول الصلاة والإمام مسافر فأحدث أو نام فانتبه بعد فراغ الإمام ونوى الإقامة لم يتم لأن اللاحق في الحكم كأنه خلف الإمام، فإذا فرغ الإمام فقد استحكم الفرض فلا يتغير في حق الإمام فكذا في حق اللاحق ولو نواها بعد ما صلى ركعة ثم خرج الوقت فإنه يتحول فرضه إلى الأربع، ولو خرج الوقت وهو في الصلاة فنوى الإقامة فإنه لا يتحول فرضه إلى الأربع في حق تلك الصلاة. كذا في الخلاصة. وقيد بنصف شهر لأن نية إقامة ما دونها لا توجب الإتمام لما روي عن ابن عباس وابن عمر أنهما قدراها بذلك والأثر في المقدرات كالخبر، وأقام بمكة مع أصحابه سبعة أيام وهو يقصر، وقيد بالبلد والقرية لأن نية الإقامة لا تصح في غيرهما فلا تصح في مفازة ولا جزيرة ولا بحر ولا سفينة. وفي الخانية والظهيرية والخلاصة : ثم نية الإقامة لا تصح إلا في موضع الإقامة ممن يتمكن من الإقامة، وموضع الإقامة العمران والبيوت المتخذة من الحجر والمدر والخشب لا الخيام والأخبية والوبر ا هـ. وقيد الشارحون اشتراط صلاحية الموضع بأن يكون سار ثلاثة أيام فصاعداً، أما إذا لم ثلاثة أيام فلا يشترط أن تكون الإقامة في بلد أو قرية بل تصح ولو في المفازة وفيه من البحث ما قدمناه.
His entering his city (misr) includes the case where he intended to reside there from the beginning, and includes the case where he is in prayer, such as if an event (hadath) overtakes him and he has no water, so he enters his city for water, except for the latecomer (lahiq) if he has an event and enters his city to perform wudu, he is not required to complete (the prayer) and does not become a resident by entering his city. Thus in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya. And it includes the case where he has traveled three days or less, but mentioned in the sharh that he completes if he travels less merely by resolving to return, even if he does not enter his city, because it is a repudiation of travel before it is established, since it is subject to repudiation. He said in Fath al-Qadir: By analogy, it would not be permissible for him to break his fast in Ramadan if there are two days between him and his city. And in al-Mujtaba: Travel is not invalidated except by intention to reside, entering the homeland, or returning before three days. And mentioned in al-Khaniyya, al-Zahiriyya, etc., that if he returns for a need he forgot and then remembers it, then if he has an original homeland, he becomes a resident merely by resolving to return; if he has no original homeland, he shortens. And what appears is that entering the city is absolutely necessary because the cause is leaving homes with the intention of a three-day journey, not completing a three-day journey, as evidenced by the ruling of travel being established merely by that. So the cause for the ruling of travel is complete, so its ruling applies as long as the cause for the ruling of residence is not established. And al-Bukhari narrated in a suspended (ta'liq) form that 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) went out and shortened (the prayer) while seeing the houses, and when it was said to him: This is Kufa, he said: Not until we enter it. Meaning he prayed two rak'ahs while Kufa was in their sight. It is restricted by intention to reside because if he enters a city and does not intend to stay there for fifteen days, but says 'Tomorrow I will leave' or 'The day after tomorrow' until he remains like that for years, he shortens. And in al-Mujtaba: Intention only takes effect with five conditions: First, cessation of travel, so if he intends residence while traveling, it is not valid. Second, suitability of the place, so if he stays in a sea or island, it is not valid. And unity of place, duration, and independence of opinion. And intention is unrestricted, so it includes implicit intention, as when a pilgrim reaches Syria and knows that the caravan will only leave after fifteen days and resolves not to leave except with them, he does not shorten because he is like one intending residence. Thus in al-Muhit. And it includes if he intends it during prayer within the time, then he completes, whether at the beginning, middle, or end, whether alone, following an imam, catching up, or preceded. As for the latecomer (lahiq) who catches the beginning of the prayer with the imam while the imam is a traveler, then he has an event or sleeps and wakes up after the imam finishes and intends residence, he does not complete because the latecomer is in effect as if behind the imam. So when the imam finishes, the obligation is firmly established and does not change for the imam, and similarly for the latecomer. If he intends residence after praying one rak'ah and then the time exits, his obligation shifts to four. If the time exits while he is in prayer and he intends residence, his obligation does not shift to four with respect to that prayer. Thus in al-Khulasa. And it is restricted to half a month because intention of residence for less does not necessitate completion, as narrated from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar that they estimated it as such, and the athar in estimated matters is like khabar. And he stayed in Mecca with his companions for seven days while shortening. And it is restricted to city and village because intention of residence is not valid in other places, so it is not valid in a desert, island, sea, or ship. And in al-Khaniyya, al-Zahiriyya, and al-Khulasa: Intention of residence is only valid in a place of residence for one who is able to reside. The place of residence is inhabited areas and houses made of stone, mud, and wood, not tents, shelters, and hair (woolen structures). And the commentators restricted the condition of suitability of place to one who has traveled three days or more. As for if he has not traveled three days, it is not required that the residence be in a city or village, rather it is valid even in a desert, and there is in it the investigation we mentioned.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the rules by which a traveler (musafir) becomes a resident (muqim) and must complete the four-rak'ah prayers instead of shortening them. The text begins by stating that entering one's hometown (misr) causes the traveler to become a resident, provided he intended to reside there from the beginning. However, there is an exception for the latecomer (lahiq) who enters his city to perform wudu due to an event; he does not become a resident. The passage then addresses the case where a traveler returns before completing three days of travel. Some sources hold that mere intention to return is enough to become a resident, while others require actually entering the city. The author prefers the latter view, citing the hadith of 'Ali (RA) who shortened prayer while seeing Kufa but did not complete until he entered. The text then lists the conditions for a valid intention to reside (niyyat al-iqama): cessation of travel, suitability of the place (a town or village, not desert or sea), unity of place, a duration of at least fifteen days, and independence of opinion. It also discusses the ruling when intention is formed during prayer, distinguishing between different scenarios. The passage emphasizes that entering a city alone is not sufficient; one must also have the intention to stay for the prescribed period. The hadith of 'Ali is used as proof that entering the city is necessary. The text also explains that the intention to reside can be implicit, such as when a pilgrim knows the caravan will leave after fifteen days and resolves to stay. Finally, it restricts the validity of intention to reside to towns and villages, not tents or nomadic dwellings.

Key Terms
مصر (miṣr): The city that is one's hometown (waṭan aṣlī) or the place where one intends to reside permanently.
إقامة (iqāma): The intention to stay in a place for 15 days or more, which nullifies the concession of shortening prayer (qasr).
قصر (qaṣr): To shorten the four-rak'ah prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha) to two rak'ahs during travel.
لاحق (lāḥiq): A latecomer who joins the imam after part of the prayer has passed; in this context, one who catches the first rak'ah with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does entering one's city (misr) cause the traveler to become a resident (muqim) and complete prayers?
A) Always when entering the city.
B) Only if he intends to stay 15 days or intends residence from the beginning.
C) Only if he is returning from a journey of less than three days.
D) Only if he is the imam in prayer.

Key Takeaway
A traveler becomes a resident and must complete prayers by entering his hometown with intention to reside or by intending to stay 15 days in a suitable place; mere entry or intention alone is insufficient without the other.

Conditions for a Traveler's Intention of Residence
Commentarial expansion defining two key conditions for niyyat al-iqama

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a traveler's intention of residence changes his legal status to resident (muqim), and apply the ruling to scenarios involving duration, place, and travel distance.

Core Idea
A traveler becomes a resident only by intending to stay 15 days in a town or village; less duration or improper place keeps him as a musafir.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains when a traveler's intention to stay in a place removes his concession of qasr (shortening prayers). It discusses the necessary duration (half-month), the required type of location (civilized settlement), and the implications of travel distance. It also touches on an edge case of marriage as a basis for residence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Locate the core condition: intention of residence (niyyat al-iqama) must be for at least half a month (15 days) in a city or village. This makes the traveler a resident (muqim) required to complete prayers.
The passage explicitly states 'half a month' and restricts place.
2
Recognize the proof
Note the evidence: the practice of Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar, who estimated the duration as half a month. An athar (companion report) is treated like a hadith in fixed measures.
This is a dalil naqli; the proof is considered zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
3
Understand the place condition
The place must be a city (balad) or village (qarya) with permanent buildings (stone, mud, wood). Tents, pavilions, deserts, islands, ships are invalid.
The passage quotes al-Khaniyyah et al. for the definition of proper residence.
4
Consider the travel distance condition
Commentators add that for a traveler who has traveled at least three days, the place must be suitable (city/village). If travel is less than three days, residence in any place (even desert) is valid for completing prayer.
This is a condition on the condition: for long-distance travelers, the place matters; for short-distance, any place works.
5
Examine the marriage sub-issue
If a traveler marries in a city, he becomes a resident by marriage, regardless of intention. Similarly, a female traveler becomes a resident by marriage.
This is an exception from al-Qunyah based on hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حق الإمام فكذا في حق اللاحق ولو نواها بعد ما صلى ركعة ثم خرج الوقت فإنه يتحول فرضه إلى الأربع، ولو خرج الوقت وهو في الصلاة فنوى الإقامة فإنه لا يتحول فرضه إلى الأربع في حق تلك الصلاة. كذا في الخلاصة. وقيد بنصف شهر لأن نية إقامة ما دونها لا توجب الإتمام لما روي عن ابن عباس وابن عمر أنهما قدراها بذلك والأثر في المقدرات كالخبر، وأقام بمكة مع أصحابه سبعة أيام وهو يقصر، وقيد بالبلد والقرية لأن نية الإقامة لا تصح في غيرهما فلا تصح في مفازة ولا جزيرة ولا بحر ولا سفينة. وفي الخانية والظهيرية والخلاصة : ثم نية الإقامة لا تصح إلا في موضع الإقامة ممن يتمكن من الإقامة، وموضع الإقامة العمران والبيوت المتخذة من الحجر والمدر والخشب لا الخيام والأخبية والوبر ا هـ. وقيد الشارحون اشتراط صلاحية الموضع بأن يكون سار ثلاثة أيام فصاعداً، أما إذا لم ثلاثة أيام فلا يشترط أن تكون الإقامة في بلد أو قرية بل تصح ولو في المفازة وفيه من البحث ما قدمناه. وقول المصنف حتى يدخل مصره أولى من قول صاحب المجمع «إلى أن يدخل وطنه» لأن الوطن مكان الإنسان ومحله كما في المغرب، وليس الإتمام متوقفاً على دخوله بل على دخول مصره، وإن لم يدخل وطنه ويصير المصر مصراً للإنسان بكونه ولد فيه. واختلفوا فيما إذا دخل المسافر مصراً وتزوج بها والظاهر أنه يصير مقيماً لحديث عمر رضي الله عنه ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «من تزوج في بلدة فهو منها» والمسافرة تصير مقيمة بنفس التزوج عندهم. كذا في القنية.
The right of the Imam, so likewise in the right of the latecomer. If he intended it after praying one rak'ah then the time expired, then his obligation shifts to four. If the time expired while he was in prayer and then he intended residence, his obligation does not shift to four with respect to that prayer. Thus in al-Khulasa. And he restricted with half a month because an intention of residence less than that does not oblige completion, due to what was narrated from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar that they estimated it as such, and an athar regarding fixed measures is like a khabar. And he stayed in Makkah with his companions seven days while he shortened. And he restricted with city and village because intention of residence is not valid in other than them, so it is not valid in a desert, an island, a sea, or a ship. In al-Khaniyyah, al-Zahiriyyah, and al-Khulasa: Then intention of residence is not valid except in a place of residence from one who is able to reside; the place of residence is civilization and houses made of stone, mud, and wood, not tents, pavilions, and hair (wool). End quote. And the commentators restricted with the condition of the place's suitability being that one has traveled three days or more; but if he has not traveled three days, it is not required that the residence be in a city or village, but it is valid even in a desert, and there is in it from the investigation what we have mentioned. And the author's statement 'until he enters his city' is better than the author of al-Majma''s statement 'until he enters his homeland' because the homeland is a person's place and abode as in al-Mughrib; and completion is not dependent on his entering it but on entering his city, even if he has not entered his homeland; and a city becomes a city for a person by his being born there. And they differed regarding when a traveler enters a city and marries there: the apparent is that he becomes a resident due to the hadith of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) and due to his statement (peace be upon him) 'Whoever marries in a city is from it.' And a woman traveler becomes a resident by marriage itself according to them. Thus in al-Qunyah.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expounds the conditions under which a traveler's intention of residence (niyyat al-iqama) makes him a resident (muqim) required to complete his prayers. The opening discusses a specific case: if a traveler intends residence mid-prayer after one rak'ah and then the prayer time expires, his obligation becomes four rak'ahs. But if the time expires while still in prayer and then he intends residence, that does not change his obligation for that prayer. The main ruling is that intention of residence must be for at least half a month (15 days) based on the practice of Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar, who fixed this duration. An athar is treated as a hadith in matters of fixed quantities. Moreover, the place must be a city or village, not a desert, island, sea, or ship. According to al-Khaniyyah and others, the residence place must be inhabited structures of stone, mud, or wood, not tents or hair dwellings. Commentators add that the place must be at least three days' travel away for the condition to apply, otherwise residence in a desert is valid. The author prefers the condition of entering one's city (misr) over the homeland (watan), as completion depends on entering the city where one is considered a resident, even if not born there. A final sub-issue: if a traveler marries in a city, he becomes a resident.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): The traveler's intention to stay in a place for a specific duration, which changes his legal status from traveler to resident.
نصف شهر (nisf shahr): Half a month, i.e., 15 days, as the minimum duration for a traveler's intention to become a resident.
بلد (balad): A town or city with permanent buildings, suitable for residence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum duration a traveler must intend to stay in a village to become a resident?
A) 4 days
B) 7 days
C) 15 days
D) 20 days

Key Takeaway
A traveler's intention of residence must be for at least half a month (15 days) in a permanent settlement (city or village) to change his status from musafir to muqim.

Intention of Residence in Two Places: The Story of 'Isa ibn Aban
Explains ruling with historical story and resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for valid intention of residence and explain why intending residence in two places (like Makkah and Mina) is invalid, using the story of 'Isa ibn Aban as a proof.

Core Idea
Residence requires continuous stay in one place; leaving before 15 days invalidates initial intention.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a subtle issue: if a traveler intends to stay in Makkah for a month but must go to Mina for Hajj, does he become a resident? The author explains that intending residence in two places is invalid, and then relates the famous story of 'Isa ibn Aban, whose confusion over this very point led him to abandon hadith studies and dedicate himself to fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Intention of residence in Makkah and Mina). What is the Hanafi ruling? (Invalid; he does not complete prayer).
The act is niyyat al-iqama in two separate locations.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
What proof does the author cite? (Rational argument: if residence in two places were allowed, travel would never be realized because stages add up.)
This is a dalil aqli: if it were valid in two, it would be valid in many, leading to absurdity.
3
Analyze the story of 'Isa ibn Aban
How was 'Isa corrected twice? First, when he completed prayers assuming residence, he was told he would leave for Mina, so his intention was invalid. Second, after returning, when he shortened prayers intending to travel with his friend, he was told he was still a resident because he had not left Makkah yet.
The story illustrates the principle that intention must be for continuous stay in one place.
4
Understand the resolution of the apparent contradiction
Why was 'Isa told to shorten first and then complete? Initially, his intended stay before leaving was less than 15 days. After returning from Mina, the remaining stay (20 days) exceeded 15, so he became a resident upon return.
The condition is not that all 15 days be consecutive without any departure; it is about the total intended stay in one location.
5
Apply the principle to the Hajj scenario
For a pilgrim entering Makkah before Hajj: if the total intended stay (before and after Mina) is at least 15 days in Makkah, he becomes a resident. The time spent in Mina does not break residence as long as the stay after return is 15+.
This resolves the initial confusion: the pilgrim must re-evaluate his intention after returning from Mina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا) بمكة ومنى) أي لو نوى الإقامة بمكة خمسة عشر يوماً فإنه لا يتم الصلاة لأن الإقامة لا تكون في مكانين إذ لو جازت في مكانين الجازت في أماكن فيؤدي إلى أنَّ السفر لا يتحقق لأن إقامة المسافر في المراحل لو جمعت كانت خمسة عشر يوماً أو أكثر إلا إذا نوى أن يقيم بالليل في أحدهما فيصير مقيماً بدخوله فيه لأن إقامة المرء تضاف إلى مبيته. يقال فلان يسكن في حارة كذا وإن كان بالنهار في الأسواق ثم بالخروج إلى الموضع الآخر لا يصير مسافراً. وذكر في كتاب المناسك أن الحاج إذا دخل مكة في أيام العشر ونوى الإقامة نصف شهر لا يصح لأنه لا بد له من الخروج إلى عرفات فلا يتحقق الشرط. وقيل: كان سبب تفقه عيسى بن أبان هذه المسألة وذلك أنه كان مشغولاً بطلب الحديث قال : فدخلت في أول العشر من ذي الحجة مع صاحب لي وعزمت على الإقامة شهراً وجعلت أتم الصلاة، فلقيني بعض أصحاب أبي حنيفة فقال : أخطأت فإنك تخرج إلى منى وعرفات، فلما رجعت من منى بدا لصاحبي أن يخرج وعزمت على أن أصاحبه وجعلت أقصر الصلاة فقال لي صاحب أبي حنيفة : أخطأت فإنك مقيم بمكة فما لم تخرج منها لا تصير مسافراً فقلت : في موضعين فرحلت إلى مجلس محمد واشتغلت بالفقه . قال في البدائع : وإنما أوردنا هذه الحكاية ليعلم مبلغ العلم فيصير مبعثة للطلبة على طلبه. قيد بالمصرين ومراده موضعان صالحان للإقامة لا فرق بين المصرين أو القريتين أو المصر والقرية للاحتراز عن نية الإقامة في موضعين من مصر واحد أو قرية واحدة فإنها صحيحة لأنهما متحدان حكماً، ألا ترى أنه لو خرج إليه مسافراً لم يقصر قوله : وقصر إن نوى أقل منها أو لم ينو وبقي سنين) أي أقل من نصف شهر وقد قدمنا تقريره قوله : (أو) نوى عسكر ذلك بأرض الحرب وإن حاصروا مصر أو حاصروا أهل البغى في دارنا تفقه عيسى بن أبان الخ) نقل العلامة ملا علي القاري هذه الحكايه في في شرحه على لباب المناسك ثم قال : في كلام صاحب الإمام تعارض حيث حكم في الأول بأنه مسافر فلا يجوز له التمام، وحكم في الثاني بأنه مقيم فلا يجوز له القصر مع أن المسألة بحالها ولعل التقدير فلما رجعت إلى منى ونويت الإقامة بمكة مع صاحبي بدا الخ. ومفهموم مسألة المتون أنه لو نوى في أحدهما خمسة عشر يوماً صار مقيماً فحينئذ المسافر إذا دخل مكة واستوطن بها أو أراد الإقامة فيها شهراً مثلاً فلا شك أنه . مقيماً، ولا يصير يضر حينئذ خروجه إلى منى وعرفات ولا تنقضي إقامته إذ لا يشترط تحقق كونه خمسة عشر يوماً متوالية بها بحيث لا يخرج منها والله أعلم ا.هـ. أقول : وكذا استشكل العلامة ابن أمير حاج قوله إنك مقيم، ثم أجاب بأنه سماه مقيماً بناء على زعمه الأول وأقول وبالله التوفيق : لا إشكال أصلاً فإن المفهوم من هذه الحكاية أنه إذا نوى الإقامة بمكة شهراً ومن نيته أن يخرج إلى عرفات ومنى قبل أ يمكث بمكة خمسة عشر يوماً لا يصير مقيماً لأنه يكون ناوياً لإقامة مستقبلة فلا تعتبر ، فإذا رجع من منى وعرفات إلى مكة نيته السابقة صار مقيماً لأن الباقي من الشهر أكثر من خمسة عشر، وهنا كذلك لأن فرض المسألة أنه دخل في أول العشر ومعلوم أن الحاج يخرج في اليوم الثامن إلى منى ويرجع إلى مكة في اليوم الثاني عشر فلما دخل إلى مكة أول العشر ونوى إقامة شهر لم تصح نيته أول المدة لأنه لا يحصل له إقامة خمسة عشر يوماً إلا بعد رجوعه من منى فلذا أمره صاحب الإمام بالقصر أول المدة وبالإتمام بعد العود لأنه لما عاد إلى مكة وهو على نيته السابقة كان ناوياً أن يقيم فيها عشرين يوماً بقية الشهر. هذا ما ظهر لي والله تعالى أعلم قوله : (فلما رجعت من منى أي إلى مكة . وقوله بد الصاحبي أن يخرج أي عزم على أن يخرج من مكة مسافراً، وقوله «وجعلت أقصر الصلاة أي في مكة بعد عزمه على السفر مع صاحبه قول المصنف : (أو حاصروا
His statement: '(no) in Makkah and Mina' means: if he intends residence in Makkah for fifteen days, he does not complete the prayer because residence cannot be in two places. Indeed, if it were permissible in two places, it would be permissible in many places, leading to travel being unattainable because the traveler's stays in stages if collected would be fifteen days or more. Except if he intends to stay at night in one of them, then he becomes a resident by entering it because one's residence is attributed to his overnight stay. It is said: so-and-so lives in such-and-such a lane even though he is in the markets during the day. Then by going out to the other place, he does not become a traveler. It is mentioned in Kitab al-Manasik that if the pilgrim enters Makkah during the ten days and intends residence for half a month, it is not valid because he must go out to 'Arafat, so the condition is not fulfilled. And it was said: the reason for 'Isa ibn Aban's engagement in fiqh was this issue. For he was busy seeking hadith. He said: I entered at the beginning of the ten days of Dhul-Hijjah with a companion of mine and intended to stay for a month and started completing the prayer. Then some of Abu Hanifa's companions met me and said: You are mistaken because you will go out to Mina and 'Arafat. Then when I returned from Mina, my companion decided to leave, and I intended to accompany him and started shortening the prayer. Then the companion of Abu Hanifa said to me: You are mistaken because you are a resident in Makkah; as long as you have not left it, you do not become a traveler. So I said: Two places? Then I journeyed to the study circle of Muhammad and engaged in fiqh. In al-Bada'i': We only mentioned this story to show the extent of knowledge and to motivate students to seek it. He restricted with two cities, meaning two places suitable for residence, with no difference between two cities, two villages, or a city and a village, to exclude the intention of residence in two places within one city or one village, for that is valid because they are legally one. Do you not see that if one went out to it as a traveler, he would not shorten. His statement: 'and he shortens if he intends less than that or does not intend and stays for years' – meaning less than half a month, and we have already explained it. His statement: 'or he intends an army in the land of war' ... 'Isa ibn Aban etc.' The scholar Mulla 'Ali al-Qari transmitted this story in his commentary on Lubab al-Manasik and then said: In the statement of the Imam there is contradiction: he ruled in the first that he is a traveler so he may not complete, and in the second that he is a resident so he may not shorten, even though the issue is the same. Perhaps the estimation is: 'when I returned to Mina and intended residence in Makkah with my companion, he decided...' The understanding of the matn's issue is that if he intends fifteen days in one of them, he becomes a resident. Then the traveler, if he enters Makkah and settles there or intends to stay for a month, without doubt he is a resident, and then his going out to Mina and 'Arafat does not harm him, nor does his residence end, because it is not a condition that he actually stays fifteen consecutive days without leaving. And Allah knows best. End quote. I say: Similarly, the scholar Ibn Amir Hajj objected to his statement 'you are a resident' and then answered that he called him a resident based on his first assumption. I say, and with Allah is success: There is no difficulty at all. The understanding from this story is that if he intends residence in Makkah for a month and from his intention is to go out to 'Arafat and Mina before staying in Makkah for fifteen days, he does not become a resident because he intends residence in the future, so it is not considered. Then when he returns from Mina and 'Arafat to Makkah with his previous intention, he becomes a resident because the remainder of the month is more than fifteen. And here it is similar because the assumed case is that he entered at the beginning of the ten days, and it is known that the pilgrim goes out on the eighth day to Mina and returns to Makkah on the twelfth day. So when he entered Makkah at the beginning of the ten days and intended to stay for a month, his intention did not take effect at the beginning of the period because he does not achieve residence for fifteen days except after his return from Mina. Therefore the Imam ordered him to shorten at the beginning and to complete after returning, because when he returned to Makkah with his previous intention, he intended to stay for twenty days for the remainder of the month. This is what appeared to me, and Allah most high knows best. His statement: 'When I returned from Mina' – i.e., to Makkah. His statement: 'My companion decided to leave' – i.e., he resolved to leave Makkah as a traveler. His statement: 'I started shortening the prayer' – i.e., in Makkah after his resolve to travel with his companion. The author's statement: 'or they besiege'.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on the phrase 'la' (no) in the matn regarding intending residence in Makkah and Mina. The ruling: if a traveler intends to stay in Makkah for fifteen days, he does not become a resident because he must go to Mina and 'Arafat, effectively intending residence in two places. Residence in two places is invalid; otherwise, travel would never be realized. The exception is if he intends to stay overnight in one place, as residence is attached to one's night quarters. Then the famous story of 'Isa ibn Aban is recounted: during Hajj, he first completed prayers intending to stay in Makkah for a month, but was corrected because he would leave to Mina. After returning, he intended to accompany his friend leaving Makkah and began shortening, but was again corrected because he was still a resident. Confused, 'Isa left to study fiqh under Imam Muhammad. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) resolves the apparent contradiction: the first correction was because his intention of residence at the start was invalid due to the forthcoming exit; after returning, his remaining stay (20 days) was more than 15, so he became a resident. The condition is not that all 15 days be consecutive without any departure; it is about the total intended stay in one location. Thus, the story teaches the importance of precise intention in fiqh.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة في موضعين (niyyat al-iqama fi mawdi'ayn): Intending to stay in two separate locations such that one cannot be considered a resident of either.
مكة (Makkah): The holy city; a place where a traveler may intend residence, but leaving to Mina/Arafat affects validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the story of 'Isa ibn Aban, why did the companion of Abu Hanifa tell him he was incorrect when he first started completing prayers?
A) Because he had not intended a full month
B) Because he would leave Makkah to go to Mina and 'Arafat
C) Because he was not a traveler
D) Because he should have been shortening from the beginning

Key Takeaway
For valid residence intention, the total intended stay in one location must be at least 15 days, and leaving for necessary purposes before completing 15 days does not invalidate if the remaining stay after return still exceeds 15.

Ruling on Shortening Prayer for an Army in Enemy Territory
Commentary on the conditions under which an army may shorten prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shortening prayer for an army in enemy territory and explain why the intention to reside is considered unstable.

Core Idea
In enemy territory, an army’s intention to stay is unstable due to the threat of fighting or flight, so they retain traveler's concession.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq discusses a nuanced aspect of shortening prayer. The army, even if they intend to stay half a month, does not become a resident because their situation is one of uncertainty. The commentator illustrates this principle with analogies and a fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
The passage states that an army may shorten prayer if it intends half a month in enemy land. This applies whether they are fighting or besieging, and whether in dar al-harb or dar al-Islam in non-city areas with rebels.
The ruling is general: no distinction between active combat or siege.
2
Understand the Key Principle: Invalidity of Intention to Reside in Enemy Territory
The reason given is that niyyat al-iqamah (intention to reside) is not valid in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy because the army's situation is unstable—they hesitate between staying and fleeing. This makes their intention unstable.
This is the core legal 'illa (effective cause) for the ruling.
3
Analyze the Analogy with the Merchant
The commentator compares the army to a merchant who enters a city for a need and intends to stay up to 15 days to fulfill it. The merchant is not a resident because his stay is conditional and hesitant, similar to the army.
This analogy (qiyas) reinforces the principle that unstable intention does not establish residency.
4
Identify the Exception and the Fatwa
An exception is when a person enters dar al-harb with safe conduct (aman) and intends to stay half a month; he becomes a resident because there is no threat. Also, a person who swears by divorce to travel and intends a short nearby trip does not fulfill his oath because his intention is not genuine.
The fatwa illustrates that genuine intention is required for legal consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب المسافر
أن
الحرب وإن حاصروا مصر أو حاصروا أهل البغي في دارنا في غيره) معطوف على قوله «نوی أقل منه أي وقصر إن نوى عسكر نصف شهر بأرض الحرب، ولا فرق بين أن يكون العسكر مشغولين بالقتال أو المحاصرة، ولا فرق في المحاصرة بين أن تكون للمدينة أو للحصن بعد أن دخلوا المدينة، ولا فرق بين أن يكون العسكر في أرض الحرب أو أرض الإسلام مع أهل البغي في غير المصر لأن نية الإقامة في دار الحرب أو البغي لا تصح لأن حالهم يخالف عزيمتهم للتردد بين القرار والفرار، ولهذا قال أصحابنا في تاجر دخل مدينة لحاجة ونوى أن يقيم خمسة عشر يوماً لقضاء تلك الحاجة لا مقيماً لأنه متردد بين يصير يقضي حاجته فيرجع وبين أن لا يقضي فيقيم فلا تكون نيته مستقرة كنية العسكر في دار الحرب. وهذا الفصل حجة على من يقول من أراد الخروج إلى مكان ويريد أن يترخص ترخص السفر ينوي مكاناً أبعد منه وهذا غلط . كذا ذكر التمرتاشي ا هـ. كذا في معراج الدراية. وعلى هذا واقعة الفتوى وهي أن إنساناً يحلف بالطلاق أنه يسافر في هذا الشهر فينوي مسيرة ثلاثة أيام ويقصد مكاناً قريباً فهذا لم يكن مخلصاً له لتعارض نيته إذ الأولى ليست بنية أصلاً وأطلق في العسكر فشمل ما إذا كانت الشوكة لهم وقيد به لأن من دخل دار الحرب بأمان فنوى إقامة نصف شهر فيها فإنه يتم أربعاً لأن أهل الحرب لا يتعرضون له لأجل الأمان. كذا في النهاية.
Book of Prayer, Chapter on the Traveller. That [the phrase] 'and if they besiege a city or besiege the people of rebellion in our land in other than it' is coordinated with his saying 'intended less than it,' i.e., and he may shorten if an army intends half a month in the land of war. There is no difference between whether the army is occupied with fighting or besieging, and no difference in besieging between whether it is for a city or a fortress after they have entered the city. And no difference between whether the army is in the land of war or the land of Islam with the people of rebellion in other than the city, because the intention of residence in the land of war or rebellion is not valid because their state contradicts their determination due to hesitation between staying and fleeing. For this reason, our companions said concerning a merchant who entered a city for a need and intended to stay fifteen days to fulfill that need: he is not a resident because he is hesitant between possibly fulfilling his need and returning and possibly not fulfilling so he stays, so his intention is not stable like the intention of the army in the land of war. This chapter is an argument against those who say: one who intends to go to a place and wishes to avail himself of the concessions of travel intends a place farther than it, and this is a mistake. Thus mentioned al-Tamartashi. End. Thus in Miraj al-Diraya. And upon this is the case of the fatwa: that a person swears by divorce that he will travel in this month, so he intends a journey of three days and intends a nearby place, then this would not be a deliverance for him due to the contradiction of his intention, since the first is not an intention at all. And he spoke absolutely concerning the army, so it includes when they are predominant, and he qualified by it because one who enters the land of war with safe conduct and intends residence for half a month therein, then he completes four [rak'ats] because the people of war do not harm him due to the safe conduct. Thus in al-Nihaya.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding shortening of prayer (qasr) for an army. The base text states that an army may shorten if it intends half a month in enemy land. The commentator explains that this applies whether they are fighting or besieging, and whether the siege is of a city or fortress after entering. The key principle is that intention to reside (niyyat al-iqamah) in enemy or rebel territory is invalid because the army's situation is one of uncertainty—they are torn between staying and fleeing, so their intention is unstable. This is similar to a merchant who enters a city for a specific need and intends to stay until it is fulfilled; he is not considered a resident because his stay is conditional. The commentator then refutes an incorrect view that one could circumvent travel concessions by intending a longer distance. He then presents a fatwa: if a person swears by divorce to travel within a month, and intends a short three-day journey to a nearby place, he does not fulfill his oath because his true intention is not travel. Finally, the exception is noted: if a person enters enemy land with safe conduct (aman) and intends to stay half a month, he must complete the prayer because his intention is stable—the enemy does not harm him, so his state is different from that of a combatant army.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqamah): The intention to stay in a place for a duration that transforms a traveler into a resident, thereby requiring full prayer.
قصر الصلاة (qasr al-salat): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayers to two rak'ahs for a traveler.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law is not enforced and Muslims are not safe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason that an army's intention to reside in enemy territory is not valid?
A) They are always in a state of combat.
B) They are hesitant between staying and fleeing.
C) They do not have a permanent settlement.
D) They are under the authority of the enemy.

Key Takeaway
An army in enemy territory remains a traveler for prayer purposes because its intention to stay is inherently unstable due to the uncertainty of war.

Validity of Intention for a Prisoner in Enemy Land
Citing authoritative works on the prisoner's inability to form a valid intention for residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a prisoner's intention for residency is invalid and apply it to similar cases like a fugitive or a person summoned by authority.

Core Idea
A prisoner's intention for residency is invalid due to his helpless state.

In this passage, we examine the situation of a prisoner who escapes from the disbelievers and intends to reside in a cave for fifteen days. The Hanafi position is that such an intention does not make him a resident, so he remains a traveler and may shorten his prayers. The ruling is grounded in the prisoner's lack of control and stability. We will explore the reasoning and analogous cases cited from classical Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The prisoner's intention to reside for fifteen days does not make him a resident. He remains a traveler.
This is stated clearly in al-Khulasa.
2
Understand the 'illah (reason)
The prisoner's state is unstable; he may be recaptured or threatened. Therefore, his intention is not considered valid for residency.
The same applies to one who flees from the enemy after embracing Islam.
3
Examine analogous cases
Fatawa Qadikhan extends the same ruling to a person summoned by the governor or caliph to be brought to him. Such a person is like a prisoner.
This shows the principle applies whenever the person is not in control of his situation.
4
Distinguish the case of a conquering army
If a Muslim army conquers a city and adopts it as a home, they become residents and must complete prayer. If they do not adopt it, they remain travelers even if they intend to stay a month.
The key difference is adopting the city as a home (ittikhadh dar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار إلى أن الأسير لو انفلت من أيدي الكفار وتوطن في غار ونوى الإقامة خمسة عشر يوماً لم يصر مقيماً كما لو علم أهل الحرب بإسلامه فهرب منهم يريد السفر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها لم تعتبر نيته كذا في الخلاصة. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: وحكم الأسير في دار الحرب حكم العبد لا تعتبر نيته والرجل الذي يبعث إليه الوالي أو الخليفة ليؤتى به إليه فهو بمنزلة الأسير وفي التجنيس : عسكر المسلمين إذا دخلوا دار الحرب وغلبوا في مدينة إن اتخذوها داراً يتمون الصلاة، وإن لم يتخذوها داراً ولكن أرادوا والإقامة بها شهراً أو أكثر فإنهم يقصرون لأنها في الوجه الثاني بقيت دار حرب وهم محاربون فيها وفي الوجه الأول لا ا هـ .
And he indicated that if a prisoner escapes from the hands of the disbelievers and settles in a cave and intends residence for fifteen days, he does not become a resident, just as if the people of war knew of his Islam and he fled from them intending a journey of three days and nights, his intention is not considered. Thus in al-Khulasa. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: The ruling of a prisoner in the land of war is like that of a slave; his intention is not considered. And the man who is sent for by the governor or caliph to be brought to him is like a prisoner. And in al-Tajnis: The Muslim army when they enter the land of war and overcome a city, if they adopt it as a home, they complete the prayer; and if they do not adopt it as a home but intend to reside there for a month or more, then they shorten because in the second case it remains a land of war and they are at war therein, and in the first case not. End.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for a prisoner who escapes and intends to reside in enemy land. The author indicates that such an intention does not make him a resident, because his situation is unstable—he may be recaptured or threatened. The same applies to a person who flees after embracing Islam. The citation from Fatawa Qadikhan equates the prisoner to a slave in that his intention is not considered. Also, the one summoned by the authorities is similar. The text from al-Tajnis provides a distinction for an army: if they conquer a city and adopt it as their abode, they must complete the prayer (become residents), but if they do not adopt it and only intend to stay, they remain travelers and may shorten.

Key Terms
أسير (aseer): A prisoner of war captured by enemies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A runaway slave
B) A person summoned by the governor or caliph
C) A merchant travelling for trade
D) A soldier who is not fighting

Key Takeaway
A prisoner in enemy land cannot establish residency through intention because his state is unstable; he remains a traveler.

Ruling on Tent Dwellers (Ahl al-Akhiyah) and Their Status as Residents
Commentary establishing tent dwellers as residents by default.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tent dwellers' status as residents, identify when they become travelers, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute about others who intend residence with them.

Core Idea
Tent dwellers are residents by default—their seasonal moves are not travel.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key principle: the default state for a person is residence (iqama), and travel is an accidental exception. Even Bedouins who move with their livestock are considered residents as long as their movement is within their customary range. Only when they relocate permanently to a distant summer or winter residence with a three-day journey do they become travellers on the road. The also addresses the definition of 'khiba' and an intra-Hanafi disagreement about others who try to join the tent dwellers as residents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject and Ruling
Note that the passage addresses 'ahl al-akhiyah' (tent dwellers) and rules that they are residents (muqimun) by default. Their intention of residence is valid even in the desert.
The ruling is that they perform complete prayers, not shortened.
2
Understand the Legal Basis (Ta'leel)
The proof is that residence is the original state (asl) and travel is accidental (aarid). Moving from one pasture to another does not break residence because it is part of their normal lifestyle.
This is an istihsani reasoning based on custom and original state.
3
Recognize the Exception for Seasonal Relocation
If they depart from their summer residence to their winter residence with a journey of three days (approx. 48 miles/77 km) between them, they become travelers on that road.
The three-day distance is the threshold for travel in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Define Key Terminology
The term 'khiba' refers specifically to tents made of wool or hair (not goat hair). Understand the linguistic distinction to avoid confusion when the ruling is applied.
The passage quotes Diya' al-Huloom and al-Mughrib for definitions.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
For non-tent dwellers who intend residence with them, there are two narrations from Abu Yusuf, while Abu Hanifa rules they do not become residents. The author declares Abu Hanifa's view as the correct one (al-sahih).
Also note the brief mention of a sailor being a traveler.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بخلاف أهل (الأخبية حيث تصح منهم نية الإقامة في الأصح وإن كانوا في المفازة لأن الإقامة أصل فلا تبطل بالانتقال من مرعى إلى آخر إلا إذا ارتحلوا عن موضع إقامتهم في الصيف وقصدوا موضع إقامتهم في الشتاء وبينهما مسيرة ثلاثة أيام فإنهم يصيرون مسافرين في الطريق. وظاهر كلام البدائع أن أهل الأخبية مقيمون لا يحتاجون إلى نية الإقامة فإنه جعل المفاوز لهم كالأمصار والقرى لأهلها ولأن الإقامة للرجل أصل والسفر عارض لا ينوون السفر وإنما ينتقلون من ماء إلى ماء ومن مرعى إلى آخر ا هـ. والأخبية جمع خباء البيت من صوف أو وبر. فإن كان من الشعر فليس بخباء كذا في ضياء الحلوم. وفي المغرب : الخباء الخيمة من الصوف ا هـ . والمراد هنا الأعم لما في البدائع من التسوية بين من يسكن في بيت صوف أو بيت شعر. وقيد بأهل الأخبية لأن غيرهم من المسافرين لو نوى الإقامة معهم فعن أبي يوسف روايتان وعند أبي حنيفة لا يصيرون مقيمين وهو الصحيح، كذا في البدائع. وفي المجتبى والملاح مسافر إلا عند الحسن وسفينته أيضاً ليست بوطن
His saying: 'Unlike the dwellers of tents (ahl al-akhiyah), for their intention of residence is valid in the most correct view even if they are in the desert, because residence is the original state and is not nullified by moving from one pasture to another, unless they depart from their summer residence and head to their winter residence with a journey of three days between them, then they become travelers on the road. The apparent wording of al-Bada'i' is that the tent dwellers are residents and do not need an intention of residence, for he made the deserts like cities and villages for their inhabitants, and because residence for a person is the original state and travel is accidental; they do not intend travel, they only move from water to water and from pasture to pasture. End. And al-akhiyah is the plural of khiba', a house of wool or hair. If it is of goat hair, it is not a khiba'. Thus in Diya' al-Huloom. And in al-Mughrib: al-khiba' is a tent of wool. End. And the meaning here is general, as in al-Bada'i' equating between one who lives in a wool house or a hair house. And he restricted it to the tent dwellers because others among travelers, if they intend residence with them, there are two narrations from Abu Yusuf, and according to Abu Hanifa they do not become residents, and that is the correct view. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Mujtaba: the sailor is a traveler except according to al-Hasan, and his ship is also not a home.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage explains that tent dwellers (Bedouin nomads) are considered residents even though they move from place to place, because their fundamental state (asl) is residence. Their movements are not journeys but rather transitions within their home range. The author notes that they do not even need to intend residence; they are residents by default. However, if they move to a distant summer or winter residence with a three-day journey, they become travelers on that route. The passage also defines the term 'akhbiyah' and notes that it specifically refers to tents of wool or hair, not goat hair. Other travelers who join these tent dwellers do not automatically become residents; according to Abu Hanifa, they remain travelers. The correct view is that they do not become residents. Finally, the sailor is considered a traveler, and his ship is not a home.

Key Terms
أهل الأخبية (ahl al-akhiyah): Tent dwellers, specifically those living in wool or hair tents, typically Bedouins.
خباء (khiba'): A tent made of wool or hair (not goat hair).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Whenever they intend to travel
D) When they move from water to water

Key Takeaway
Tent dwellers are presumed residents; their habitual moving does not constitute travel until a three-day seasonal relocation.

Clarification of the Prisoner's Intention: Residence vs. Travel
Commentary clarifying that the prisoner's intention is invalid only for residence, not for travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the invalidity of a prisoner's intention for residence and the validity of his intention for travel, and apply the ruling on shortening prayer.

Core Idea
A prisoner's intention is invalid only for residence—not for travel; he still shortens prayer.

This lesson resolves a common ambiguity: when a text says a prisoner's intention is 'not considered,' it refers to his intention to become a resident, not his intention to travel. The commentator cites evidence from al-Dhakhira and al-Tatarkhaniyya showing that a fleeing prisoner shortens prayer, proving that his travel status remains valid. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of qasr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial claim
The text states: 'His intention is not considered.' Recognize that this is ambiguous—it could apply to all intentions or only to residence.
The claim is from a previous part of the text.
2
Examine the evidence from al-Dhakhira
Al-Saruji reports from al-Dhakhira that a prisoner who escapes and firmly intends to stay in a cave for half a month still shortens prayer because he is at war with the enemy. This shows his travel status persists.
Similarly, a convert fleeing persecutors shortens.
3
Apply the principle of limitation
The commentator clarifies that the negative ruling (la tu'tabaru niyyatuhu) is restricted to residence intention. The prisoner's unstable situation negates a valid residence intent.
The underlying reason (illah) is the prisoner's state of fear and uncertainty.
4
Derive the practical ruling
Therefore, the prisoner shortens prayer. His travel intention is valid and he is considered a traveler.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لم يصر مقيماً) ظاهر ما في الفتح أن علة ذلك عدم قطعه بالإقامة هذه المدة لأنه إذا وجد فرصة قبل تمام المدة يخرج كمن دخل المصر لحاجة معينة ونوى الإقامة مدتها قوله : (لم تعتبر نيته قال في شرح المنية : هكذا وقع في الخلاصة وفتاوى قاضيخان، ولعل المراد ولم تعتبر نيته الإقامة بعد ذلك وإلا فقد ذكر السروجي عن الذخيرة أن الأسير إذا انفلت من العدوّ فوطن نفسه على إقامة نصف شهر في غار أو نحوه قصر لأنه محارب للعدو، وكذا إذا أسلم فهرب منهم فطلبوه ليقتلوه فخرج هارباً مسيرة السفر ا.هـ. فهذا يدل على أنه يقصر، صرح بأنه يقصر في التاتارخانية بعلامة المحيط فتعين حمل تلك العبارة على ما قلنا ولا يصح غير ذلك أي ليس المراد من قوله لا تعتبر نيته أن نية السفر في هذه الحالة لا تصح بل المراد لا تعتبر نيته، للإقامة وهو في هذه الحالة لأن حالته تنافي عزيمته . ا هـ.
His saying: 'He does not become a resident.' The apparent meaning in al-Fath is that the reason is his lack of certainty of residing for that period, because if he finds an opportunity before the end of the period he will leave, like one who enters a city for a specific need and intends to stay for its duration. His saying: 'His intention is not considered.' He said in Sharh al-Munyah: Thus it occurred in al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadikhan, and perhaps the meaning is 'his intention for residence is not considered after that'; otherwise, al-Saruji mentioned from al-Dhakhira that if a prisoner escapes from the enemy and firmly intends residence for half a month in a cave or the like, he shortens because he is fighting the enemy. Similarly, if he embraces Islam and flees from them, and they seek to kill him, so he flees a journey distance, he shortens. End. This indicates that he shortens. It is explicitly stated that he shortens in al-Tatarkhaniyya with the mark of al-Muhit. So it is necessary to interpret that expression as we have said, and no other [interpretation] is valid. That is, the meaning of 'his intention is not considered' is not that his intention for travel is invalid in this situation, but rather the meaning is that his intention for residence is not considered while he is in this situation because his state contradicts his determination. End.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage clarifies the earlier ruling that a prisoner's intention is 'not considered.' The commentator notes that this specifically means his intention for residence is invalid, not his intention to travel. The proof is from al-Dhakhira and al-Tatarkhaniyya where it is clear that a prisoner who escapes and intends to stay in a cave for half a month actually shortens his prayer, because he is in a state of war with the enemy. Similarly, one who flees after conversion shortens. Therefore, the negative ruling (la tu'tabaru niyyatuhu) applies to residence intention only; his travel status remains valid, and he may shorten prayer. The reason is that his situation contradicts the stability required for residence (his state is one of fear and uncertainty).

Key Terms
لم تعتبر نيته (lam tu'tabar niyyatuhu): His intention is not considered; in this context, specifically his intention for residence is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His intention for travel is invalid, so he prays full prayers.
B) His intention for residence is invalid, but his travel status remains, so he shortens prayer.
C) He becomes a resident and prays full prayers.
D) He has no intention at all, so he prays full prayers.

Key Takeaway
The prisoner's intention for residence is invalid due to instability, but his travel intention remains valid, so he shortens prayer.

Traveller Praying Behind a Resident Imam
Ruling with brief legal cause (illah)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a traveller following a resident imam must complete the prayer and explain why taba'iyya changes the traveller's obligation.

Core Idea
A traveller following a resident imam must complete four rak'ats — the follower adopts the imam's obligation.

When a traveller (musafir) joins a congregational prayer led by a resident imam, a unique ruling applies: the traveller must complete the full prayer instead of shortening it. This lesson examines the source passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that states this rule and explains the underlying principle of taba'iyya (following). Understanding this ruling ensures correct practice when travelling and attending local mosques.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the passage: a traveller (musafir) prays behind a resident imam (muqim) within the prayer time.
The imam is not travelling; he is a resident.
2
Determine the Ruling
The text says 'sahha wa atamma' — the prayer is valid and the traveller completes (yutimmu) to four rak'ats.
Completion means praying the full four rak'ats, not shortening to two.
3
Analyse the Legal Cause (Illah)
The reason given: 'li-anna fardahu yataghayyaru ila al-arba' li al-taba'iyya' — his obligation changes to four due to following.
Taba'iyya means the follower takes the ruling of the imam in matters of obligation.
4
Apply to Practice
In practice, if a traveller joins a resident imam for any prayer, he must pray the full number of rak'ats as if he were resident.
This applies to fard prayers; nafl prayers are unaffected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو اقتدى مسافر بمقيم في الوقت صح وأتم لأنه يتغير فرضه إلى الأربع للتبعية كما
His saying: 'And if a traveller follows a resident in the time, it is valid and he completes [the prayer] because his obligatory duty changes to four due to following, just as...'
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage states a well-known Hanafi ruling: if a traveller (musafir) prays behind a resident imam, he must complete the prayer to four rak'ats. The reason given is that his obligation changes from two to four due to the principle of following (taba'iyya). The text is incomplete, but the ruling is clear: the traveller does not shorten when following a resident imam.

Key Terms
اقتدى (iqtada): To follow an imam in congregational prayer.
التبعية (al-taba'iyya): The principle that the follower takes the ruling of the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the traveller's travel ends when he enters a mosque
B) Because the follower's obligation changes due to the principle of taba'iyya
C) Because the resident imam forces the traveller to pray four
D) Because the prayer is invalid if shortened

Key Takeaway
A traveller must complete four rak'ats when following a resident imam because the principle of taba'iyya makes the follower share the imam's obligation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Traveler Following Resident: Obligation Changes to Four
Core ruling on traveler following resident within time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a traveler must complete four rak'ahs when following a resident imam within the prayer time, explain the legal basis of taba'iyya, and apply the exception when the prayer is invalidated.

Core Idea
Following a resident imam transforms the traveler's two-rak'ah obligation into four due to taba'iyya.

In Hanafi fiqh, a traveler normally prays two rak'ahs for zuhr, asr, and isha. However, when he follows a resident imam inside the prayer time, his obligation shifts to four rak'ahs. This lesson unpacks the main ruling, its rational proof, and the key condition that the change only applies during the prayer time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a traveler (musafir) following a resident (muqim) imam in prayer inside the time. The ruling is: the prayer is valid and the traveler must complete four rak'ahs.
The 'time' refers to the entire prayer time of the imam's prayer (e.g., zuhr).
2
Understand the legal basis: taba'iyya
The traveler's obligation changes because of following (taba'iyya). This is analogous to a traveler intending to stay (niyat iqama), which also changes his obligation to four. The proof is a rational analogy (qiyas).
The text compares with rebels and army inside a city who intend to stay – their intention is valid, so the traveler's change is also valid.
3
Note the exception: invalidation of the prayer
If the traveler's prayer becomes invalid (e.g., he breaks his wudu), he only needs to pray two rak'ahs when repeating. The change to four was contingent on the act of following; once that act is nullified, the obligation reverts.
This contrasts with following a resident in a supererogatory prayer, where the follower must still complete four even if invalidated.
4
Recognize the condition: within the prayer time
The change only occurs when the traveler follows within the prayer time. After the time ends, the traveler's obligation is fixed and cannot change, making the following invalid (like an obligatory follower behind a supererogatory imam).
The time is the entire period for that prayer (e.g., zuhr time).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مقتضى التعليل أنها لا تصح وظاهر كلام العناية والمعراج اختياره وبه جزم الشرنبلالي في نور الإيضاح والله أعلم قوله : (لم يصر مقيماً) ظاهر ما في الفتح أن علة ذلك عدم قطعه بالإقامة هذه المدة لأنه إذا وجد فرصة قبل تمام المدة يخرج كمن دخل المصر لحاجة معينة ونوى الإقامة مدتها قوله : (لم تعتبر نيته قال في شرح المنية : هكذا وقع في الخلاصة وفتاوى قاضيخان، ولعل المراد ولم تعتبر نيته الإقامة بعد ذلك وإلا فقد ذكر السروجي عن الذخيرة أن الأسير إذا انفلت من العدوّ فوطن نفسه على إقامة نصف شهر في غار أو نحوه قصر لأنه محارب للعدو، وكذا إذا أسلم فهرب منهم فطلبوه ليقتلوه فخرج هارباً مسيرة السفر ا.هـ. فهذا يدل على أنه يقصر، صرح بأنه يقصر في التاتارخانية بعلامة المحيط فتعين حمل تلك العبارة على ما قلنا ولا يصح غير ذلك أي ليس المراد من قوله لا تعتبر نيته أن نية السفر في هذه الحالة لا تصح بل المراد لا تعبر نيته، للإقامة وهو في هذه الحالة لأن حالته تنافي عزيمته . اهـ. وكذا في غير بخلاف أهل الأخبية ولو اقتدى مسافر بمقيم في الوقت صح وأتم وبعده لا تتغير نية الإقامة لاتصال المغير بالسبب وهو الوقت وفرض المسافر قابل للتغير حال قيام الوقت كنية الإقامة فيه، وإذا كان التغيير لضرورة الاقتداء فلو أفسده صلى ركعتين لزواله بخلاف ما لو اقتدى بالمقيم في فرضه ينوي النفل حيث يصلي أربعاً إذا أفسده لأنه التزم أداء صلاة الإمام وهنا لم يقصد سوى إسقاط فرضه غير أنه تغير ضرورة متابعته. ويستثنى من مسألة الكتاب ما لو اقتدى المقيم بالمسافر فأحدث الإمام فاستخلف المقيم فإنه لا يتغير فرضه إلى الأربع مع أنه صار مقتدياً بالخليفة المقيم لأنه لما كان المؤتم خليفة عن المسافر كان المسافر كأنه الإمام فيأخذ الخليفة صفة الأول حتى لو لم يقعد على رأس الركعتين فسدت صلاة الكل. ثم في اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم إذا لم يجلس الإمام قدر التشهد في الركعتين عامداً أو ساهياً وتابعه المسافر فقد قيل تفسد صلاة المسافر، وقيل لا تفسد كذا في السراج الوهاج. والفتوى على عدم الفساد لأن صلاته صارت أربعاً بالتبعية كذا في التجنيس وصححه في القنية. وأشار المصنف إلى أن الإمام المسافر لو نوى الإقامة لزم المأموم المسافر الإتمام وإن لم ينو للتبعية، فلو أم المسافر مسافرين ومقيمين فلما صلى ركعتين وتشهد فقبل أن يسلم تكلم واحد من المسافرين أو قام فذهب ثم نوى الإمام الإقامة فإنه يتحول فرضه وفرض المسافرين الذين لم يتكلموا إلى الأربع وصلاة من تكلم تامة فلو تكلم بعد نية الإمام الإقامة فسدت صلاته ولزمه صلاة المسافر ركعتين. ذكره الأسبيجابي .قوله : (وبعده (لا) أي بعد خروج الوقت لا يصح اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم لأن فرضه لا يتغير بعد الوقت لانقضاء السبب كما لا يتغير بنية الإقامة فيكون اقتداء المفترض بالتنفل في حق القعدة أو القراءة أو التحريمة. كذا ذكر الشارح والمذكور في الهداية وغيرها في حق القعدة أو القراءة، ولم أر من ذكر التحريمة غير الشارح والحدادي وتوضيحه أن المسافر إذا اقتدى بالمقيم أول الصلاة فإن القعدة تصير فرضاً في حق المأموم وغير فرض في حق الإمام وهو المراد بالنفل في عبارتهم لأنه ما قابل الفرض فيدخل فيه الواجب فإن القعدة الأولى واجبة. وإن اقتدى به في الشفع الثاني وكان الإمام قد قرأ في الشفع الأول فالقراءة في الشفع الثاني نافلة في حق الإمام فرض في حق المأموم ، فإن كان الإمام صلى الشفع الأول بغير قراءة واقتدى به في الشفع الثاني ففيه روايتان كما في البدائع ومقتضى المتون عدم الصحة مطلقاً، قوله: (ويستثنى الخ) دفعه في النهر بأنه لا حاجة إليه لأن ظاهر كلام المصنف أن معنى اقتدی» نوی الاقتداء به قوله : ومقتضى التعليل في هذه المسألة (الصحة فيه نظر لأن كون القراءة نافلة في الشفع الثاني إذا قرأ في الأول أيضاً لا يقتضي أن تكون فرضاً فيه إذا لم يقرأ في الأول لاحتمال التحاقها بالأول فيكون الثاني خالياً عن القراءة أصلاً كما صرح به في الفتح وسيأتي عن المحيط، ولكن قدم الخلاف في باب السهو أن القراءة في الأخريين هل هي أداء أم قضاء، وعلى
His saying: (And if a traveler follows a resident [imam] within the time, it is valid and he completes [four], because his obligatory [prayer] changes to four due to following, just as... [further text follows]
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the case of a traveler (musafir) praying behind a resident (muqim) imam. The main ruling: if a traveler follows a resident imam within the prayer time, his prayer is valid and he must complete four rak'ahs because his original obligation of two rak'ahs changes to four due to his following (taba'iyya). Outside the time, this change does not occur. The commentary then explains exceptions: if the traveler's prayer becomes invalid (e.g., he breaks it), he only needs to pray two rak'ahs because the change was contingent on the following. If a resident follows a traveler and then the traveler appoints the resident as a successor (khalifah), the resident's obligation does not change to four. There is a dispute about whether the traveler's prayer is invalid if the imam does not sit for tashahhud in the first two rak'ahs; the fatwa is that it is not invalid because the traveler's prayer has become four through following. Also discussed: if a traveler imam intends iqama during the prayer, his followers who have not spoken must complete four, while those who spoke earlier are separate. Finally, the text explains that following a resident outside the time is like an obligatory follower behind a supererogatory leader, which is invalid in certain aspects like the sitting, recitation, or takbirat al-ihram. The commentary clarifies that if the imam in the second pair has already recited in the first pair, the recitation in the second pair is supererogatory for the imam but obligatory for the follower. The passage ends with a discussion on whether recitation in the last two rak'ahs is adā' or qadā'.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer.
مسافر (musafir): A person undertaking a journey of three days or more, who may shorten prayers.
مقيم (muqim): A person who is not traveling, either resident by default or by intention.
تبعية (taba'iyya): The state of following an imam, which may affect the follower's obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler follows a resident imam within the prayer time, but then his prayer becomes invalid (e.g., he breaks his wudu), how many rak'ahs must he pray when he repeats it?
A) Two rak'ahs as a traveler.
B) Four rak'ahs because he already intended to complete.
C) Two rak'ahs because the change to four was contingent on the following, which is now gone.
D) It depends on whether he intended to stay.

Key Takeaway
A traveler's obligation changes to four rak'ahs when following a resident imam within the prayer time, but if the prayer is invalidated, he returns to two.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
Nuances: Omission of Tashahhud, Second Pair Recitation, and Out-of-Time Following
Intra-Hanafi disputes and edge cases on traveler following resident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on the traveler's prayer when the imam omits tashahhud, distinguish between the two narrations on following in the second pair, and explain why following outside the time is invalid.

Core Idea
The traveler's change to four rak'ahs is robust, but technical disputes on tashahhud omission and second pair recitation require careful analysis.

While the core ruling is clear, the text addresses several nuances: what happens if the imam omits tashahhud, whether the traveler can follow in the second pair if the imam did not recite in the first, and the case of following after the prayer time has expired. These nuances highlight the precision of Hanafi fiqh in preserving the integrity of the follower's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the tashahhud omission dispute
The text presents two views: some say the traveler's prayer becomes invalid if the imam omits tashahhud (first sitting) intentionally or forgetfully; others say it does not. The fatwa is on non-invalidity because the traveler's prayer became four due to following.
This dispute is intra-Hanafi; the mufta bihi is non-invalidity.
2
Evaluate the second pair recitation issue
If the traveler follows the imam in the second pair (the last two rak'ahs), and the imam has already recited in the first pair, then the recitation in the second pair is supererogatory for the imam but obligatory for the follower. However, if the imam did not recite in the first pair, there are two narrations: one invalidates the following, another allows it.
The matns (core texts) incline toward absolute non-validity if the imam omitted recitation in the first pair.
3
Understand the out-of-time case
Following a resident imam after the prayer time has expired is invalid because the traveler's obligation cannot change once the cause (time) is gone. This situation is compared to an obligatory follower behind a supererogatory imam, which is invalid in certain aspects (sitting, recitation, takbirat al-ihram).
The text notes that the out-of-time case invalidates the following in terms of sitting, recitation, and takbirat al-ihram.
4
Recognize the exception for resident following traveler
The text mentions an exception: if a resident follows a traveler imam, and then the imam has an event appointing the resident as successor, the resident's obligation does not change to four; he remains a follower of the traveler in effect.
This shows that taba'iyya works only for traveler-following-resident, not vice versa in this exception.

في حق المأموم ، فإن كان الإمام صلى الشفع الأول بغير قراءة واقتدى به في الشفع الثاني ففيه روايتان كما في البدائع ومقتضى المتون عدم الصحة مطلقاً، قوله: (ويستثنى الخ) دفعه في النهر بأنه لا حاجة إليه لأن في الأول لاحتمال التحاقها بالأول فيكون الثاني خالياً عن القراءة أصلاً كما صرح به في الفتح وسيأتي عن المحيط، ولكن قدم الخلاف في باب السهو أن القراءة في الأخريين هل هي أداء أم قضاء، وعلى
His saying: (And if a traveler follows a resident [imam] within the time, it is valid and he completes [four], because his obligatory [prayer] changes to four due to following, just as... [further text follows]
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the case of a traveler (musafir) praying behind a resident (muqim) imam. The main ruling: if a traveler follows a resident imam within the prayer time, his prayer is valid and he must complete four rak'ahs because his original obligation of two rak'ahs changes to four due to his following (taba'iyya). Outside the time, this change does not occur. The commentary then explains exceptions: if the traveler's prayer becomes invalid (e.g., he breaks it), he only needs to pray two rak'ahs because the change was contingent on the following. If a resident follows a traveler and then the traveler appoints the resident as a successor (khalifah), the resident's obligation does not change to four. There is a dispute about whether the traveler's prayer is invalid if the imam does not sit for tashahhud in the first two rak'ahs; the fatwa is that it is not invalid because the traveler's prayer has become four through following. Also discussed: if a traveler imam intends iqama during the prayer, his followers who have not spoken must complete four, while those who spoke earlier are separate. Finally, the text explains that following a resident outside the time is like an obligatory follower behind a supererogatory leader, which is invalid in certain aspects like the sitting, recitation, or takbirat al-ihram. The commentary clarifies that if the imam in the second pair has already recited in the first pair, the recitation in the second pair is supererogatory for the imam but obligatory for the follower. The passage ends with a discussion on whether recitation in the last two rak'ahs is adā' or qadā'.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer.
مسافر (musafir): A person undertaking a journey of three days or more, who may shorten prayers.
مقيم (muqim): A person who is not traveling, either resident by default or by intention.
تبعية (taba'iyya): The state of following an imam, which may affect the follower's obligation.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in prayer; the first tashahhud is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa, if a traveler follows a resident imam and the imam omits the first tashahhud (intentionally or forgetfully), what is the ruling on the traveler's prayer?
A) It becomes invalid; the traveler must repeat.
B) It is valid; the traveler completes four rak'ahs.
C) It becomes supererogatory; the traveler prays two rak'ahs.
D) It is valid only if the traveler intended to stay.

Key Takeaway
The traveler's prayer is robust against the imam's omission of tashahhud, but following in the second pair without recitation in the first is problematic, and following outside the time is invalid.
