Conditions for a Resident Following a Traveller After Time
States conditions for validity when resident follows traveller after time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the validity of a resident following a traveller after the prayer time has expired and explain the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
A resident may validly follow a traveller after time if the prayer is four rak'ahs and missed for the follower.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced scenario: a resident (muqim) joining a traveller (musafir) for a prayer after its time has expired. The default ruling that one obligated cannot follow one performing supererogatory is here set aside under specific conditions. Through careful reasoning, the Hanafi school establishes validity where the prayer is four rak'ahs and the follower's obligation is a missed prayer, resolving potential conflicts between the imam's and follower's intentions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that the implication of legal reasoning is validity (sihha) for a resident following a traveller after time, under certain conditions.
The ruling is not general permissibility but conditional.
2
Understand the reasoning
The act is valid because it is not iqtida' al-muftarid bi al-mutanaffil; the follower is not obligated in the traveller's sitting or recitation, and the tahrimah is valid for both.
This distinguishes from the general prohibition of an obligated person following a supererogatory prayer.
3
List the conditions from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj
Two conditions: (1) the prayer must be missed (fa'itah) for both imam and follower, and (2) the prayer must be four rak'ahs.
Exceptions for two or three rak'ah prayers, or when the follower holds a different madhhab view.
4
Note the refinement
The commentator suggests that the better condition is that the prayer be missed only for the follower, not necessarily for the imam.
Example: a traveller (for whom Zuhr is missed) follows a resident (for whom it is on time) – still valid.
5
Apply to examples
The passage gives examples from al-Bada'i: if the follower sleeps until time exits, he completes four; if he speaks after time, he prays two rak'ahs.
These illustrate the practical outcomes of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومقتضى التعليل في هذه المسألة الصحة لأنه ليس اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل لا في حق القعدة ولا القراءة، وأما التحريمة فهي لا تكون إلا فرضاً ولم يظهر قول الحدادي لأن تحريمة الإمام اشتملت على الفرض لا غير وأجاب في المحيط عما إذا لم يقرأ في الأوليين وقرأ في الأخريين بأن القراءة في الأخريين قضاء عن الأوليين والقضاء يلتحق بمحله فلا يبقى للأخريين قراءة ا هـ. يعني فلا مطلقاً وقيد في السراج الوهاج عدم صحة الاقتداء بعد يصح الوقت بقيدين : الأول أن تكون فائتة في حق الإمام والمأموم الثاني أن تكون الصلاة رباعية، أما إذا كانت ثنائية أو ثلاثية أو كانت فائتة في حق الإمام مؤداة في حق المأموم كما إذا كان المأموم يرى قول أبي حنيفة في الظهر والإمام يرى قولهما وقول الشافعي فإنه يجوز دخوله معه في الظهر بعد المثل قبل المثلين فإنها صحيحة اهـ. وهو تقييد حسن لكن الأولى أن يكون الشرط كونها فائتة في حق المأموم فقط، سواء كانت فائتة في حق الإمام أو لا بأن صلى ركعة من الظهر مثلاً أو ركعتين ثم خرج الوقت فاقتدى به مسافر لأن الظهر فائتة في حق المسافر لا في حق المقيم. والقيد الأول مفهوم من قوله صح وأتم فإنه يفيد أن الكلام في الرباعية الذي يظهر فيها القصر والإتمام بل لا حاجة إليه أصلاً لأن السفر مؤثر في الرباعي فقط . وقيد بكون الاقتداء بعد خروج الوقت لأنه لو اقتدى به في الوقت ثم خرج الوقت قبل الفراغ من الصلاة تبطل صلاته ولا يبطل اقتداؤه به لأنه لما صح اقتداؤه به وصار تبعاً له صار حكمه حكم المقيمين، وإنما يتأكد وجوب الركعتين بخروج الوقت في حق المسافر. ولو نام خلف الإمام حتى خرج الوقت ثم انتبه أتمها أربعاً ولو تكلم بعد خروج الوقت أو قبل خروجه يصلي ركعتين عندنا. كذا في البدائع.
And the implication of the legal reasoning in this issue is validity, because it is not an act of one obligated following one performing supererogatory, neither in the matter of the sitting nor in the recitation. As for the opening takbir, it is only obligatory. And the statement of al-Hadadi did not appear [clear] because the opening takbir of the imam includes only the obligatory. And al-Muhit answered regarding the case when he did not recite in the first two [rak'ahs] and recited in the last two: the recitation in the last two is a make-up for the first two, and the make-up attaches to its place, so the last two have no recitation. End. Meaning, so not at all. And it is restricted in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: the validity of following after the time has exited [is subject to] two conditions: first, that [the prayer] be a missed one for both the imam and the follower; second, that the prayer be four-rak'ah. As for if it is two or three, or if it is missed for the imam but performed on time for the follower – as when the follower holds the view of Abu Hanifa regarding Zuhr and the imam holds the view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] and al-Shafi'i – then it is permissible for him to join him in Zuhr after mithl [the length of lengthened shadow] before mithlayn, then it is valid. End. And it is a good restriction, but the first is that the condition be that it is missed only for the follower, whether it is missed for the imam or not – like if he prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr for example or two rak'ahs, then time exited, and a traveller followed him, because Zuhr is missed for the traveller not for the resident. And the first condition is understood from his statement 'valid and complete', as it indicates the discussion is about the four-rak'ah in which shortening and completing appear; indeed there is no need for it at all because travel affects only the four-rak'ah. And it is restricted to following after the exit of time, because if he followed him within the time then time exited before finishing the prayer, his prayer becomes invalid but his following does not become invalid – because when his following was valid and he became a follower, his ruling became the ruling of residents. And the obligation of two rak'ahs becomes confirmed only upon the exit of time for the traveller. And if he slept behind the imam until time exited then woke up, he completes it as four. And if he spoke after the exit of time or before it, he prays two rak'ahs according to us. Thus in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses the case of a resident (muqim) following a traveller (musafir) after the prayer time has exited. The author first explains the underlying reasoning: the act is valid because the muqtadi is not obligated in the sitting (qa'dah) or recitation (qira'ah) due to following a traveller, and the opening takbir (tahrimah) is only for the obligatory prayer. He then refutes al-Hadadi's view that the imam's tahrimah includes only the obligatory, making the muqtadi's act a case of one obligated following a supererogatory performer, stating that the traveller's tahrimah is valid for both his own obligatory prayer and the follower's obligation. He cites al-Muhit on the issue of recitation: if the imam reads in the last two rak'ahs without reading in the first two, it is considered a make-up for the first two, so the last two effectively have no recitation. Then, from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, he lists two conditions for the validity of following after time: (1) the prayer must be missed (fa'itah) for both imam and follower, and (2) the prayer must be four rak'ahs. He provides exceptions: if the prayer is two or three rak'ahs, or if it is missed only for the imam (e.g., the follower follows a different school), then the ruling differs. He then offers a refinement: the better view is that the condition applies only to the follower being in a missed state, not the imam, as when a traveller (for whom Zuhr is missed) follows a resident (for whom it is not missed). He explains that the first condition is implicit in the phrase 'valid and complete' because the discussion is about four-rak'ah prayers where qasr and itmam apply. He also specifies that the following must occur after time exits; if it occurs within time and then time exits before completion, the prayer is invalidated for the muqtadi. The final examples from al-Bada'i illustrate practical consequences: if a follower sleeps until time exits, he must complete four rak'ahs; if he speaks after time exits, he prays two rak'ahs.

Key Terms
اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل (iqtidā' al-muftarid bi al-mutanaffil): The act of one offering an obligatory prayer following an imam offering a supererogatory prayer; generally invalid in Hanafi fiqh.
فائتة (fā'itah): A missed prayer that was not performed in its prescribed time; qada prayer.
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer and makes it a sacred act (tahrim).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the refined view in this passage, which of the following is the correct condition for validity?
A) The prayer must be missed for both the imam and the follower.
B) The prayer must be four rak'ahs and missed only for the follower.
C) The following must occur within the time.
D) The imam must recite in both first and last rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
A resident may validly join a traveller after time if the prayer is four rak'ahs and missed for the follower, based on the Hanafi reasoning that the follower is not obligated in the traveller's supererogatory elements.

Validity of a Traveller Leading Residents in Prayer
States the ruling of a traveller leading residents with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and identify the proof for a traveller leading residents in prayer.

Core Idea
A traveller leading residents is valid; the Prophet did it and said 'We are travelers.'

Many assume a traveller cannot lead residents because of differing prayer lengths. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that it is valid, supported by the Prophet's own practice and the legal principle of building the weak upon the strong.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a resident following a traveller in prayer. The ruling is sahih (valid) both within the time and after its exit.
The matn states 'and its opposite is valid in both' – meaning a traveller leading a resident.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The traveller's prayer is two rak'ahs in both states, and the sitting (qa'dah) is obligatory for the imam but not for the follower. Building the weak (follower's prayer without obligation of sitting) upon the strong (imam's prayer) is permissible in Hanafi fiqh.
Principle: binā' al-ḍa'īf 'alā al-qawī (building the weak on the strong).
3
Examine the dalil (proof)
The Prophet ﷺ while travelling led the people of Mecca in prayer and said: 'Complete your prayer, for we are a traveling party.' This act and statement establish permissibility and form the basis of the ruling.
Hadith reference: Prophet's action (fi'l) and statement (qawl).
4
Note the authority level
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by al-Mabsut. It is not overridden by istihsan.
Authority: zahir_riwayah; cross-madhhab: mukhtalaf fih (Shafi'i may differ).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبعكسه صح فيهما) وهو اقتداء المقيم بالمسافر فهو صحيح في الوقت وبعده لأن صلاة المسافر في الحالين واحدة والقعدة فرض في حقه غير فرض في حق المقتدي، وبناء الضعيف على القوي جائز وقد أم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو مسافر أهل مكة وقال : أتموا صلاتكم فإنا قوم سفر. وهو جمع سافر كركب جمع راكب. ويستحب أن يقول ذلك بعد السلام كل مسافر صلى بمقيم لاحتمال أن خلفه لا يعرف حاله ولا يتيسر له الاجتماع بالإمام قبل ذهابه فيحكم حينئذ بفساد صلاة نفسه بناء على ظن إقامة الإمام ثم إفساده بسلامه على رأس الركعتين، وهذا محمل ما في الفتاوى إذا اقتدى بالإمام لا يدري أمسافر هو أم مقيم لا يصح لأن العلم بحال الإمام شرط الأداء بجماعة ا هـ . لا أنه شرط في الابتداء لما في المبسوط : رجل صلى الظهر بالقوم بقرية أو مصر ركعتين وهم يدرون أمسافر هو أم مقيم فصلاتهم فاسدة، سواء كانوا مقيمين أم مسافرين لأن الظاهر من حال من في موضع الإقامة أنه مقيم والبناء على الظاهر واجب حتى يتبين خلافه، فإن سألوه فأخبرهم أنه مسافر جازت صلاتهم وفي القنية : وإن كان خارج المصر لا تفسد ويجوز الأخذ بالظاهر في مثله. وإنما كان قول الإمام ذلك مستحباً لأنه لم يتعين معرفاً صحة سلامه لهم فإنه ينبغي أن يتموا ثم يسألوه فتحصل المعرفة. واختلفوا هل يقوله بعد التسليمة الأولى أو بعد التسليمتين؟ الأصح الثاني في السراج الوهاج.
His statement: (And its opposite is valid in both) – that is, a resident following a traveller is valid in both [within time and after] because the traveller's prayer is the same in both situations, and the sitting is obligatory for him but not for the follower, and building the weak upon the strong is permissible. And the Prophet ﷺ led people as a traveller in Mecca and said: 'Complete your prayer, for we are a traveling party.' And it is recommended that every traveller who leads a resident say that after the salam, because it is possible that those behind him do not know his situation and it is not easy for them to gather with the imam before he leaves; then they might judge their prayer invalid based on assuming the imam is resident and then invalidate it by his salam after two rak'ahs. This is the bearing of what is in al-Fatawa: if one follows an imam not knowing whether he is a traveller or resident, it is not valid because knowledge of the imam's state is a condition for performing in congregation. End. It is not a condition at the beginning, according to al-Mabsut: a man led people in Zuhr in a village or town, praying two rak'ahs while they did not know whether he was a traveller or resident; their prayers are invalid, whether they were residents or travellers, because the apparent condition of someone in a place of residence is that he is a resident, and building upon the apparent is obligatory until its opposite becomes clear. If they asked him and he informed them that he is a traveller, their prayer becomes valid. And in al-Qunyah: if he is outside the town, it is not invalid and it is permissible to take the apparent in like case. And the imam's saying that is only recommended because it is not determined as a means to make his salam valid for them; rather it is better that they complete then ask him, so knowledge is obtained. And they differed: does he say it after the first taslim or after both? The more correct is the second in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically on the topic of a traveller (musafir) leading a resident (muqim). The matn states: 'Wa bi'aksihi sahha fihima' (and its opposite is valid in both), meaning a traveller leading a resident is valid both within the prayer time and after time exits. The commentator explains the reasoning: the traveller's prayer is the same in both states (qasr), and the sitting (qa'dah) is obligatory for the traveller but not for the resident follower, so there is no issue of building weak upon strong. Moreover, the Prophet ﷺ himself led the people of Mecca as a traveller and instructed them to complete their prayer, saying 'Inna qawmu safar' (we are a traveling party). From this, the Hanafi school recommends that any traveller imam who leads residents say this after the salam, to prevent confusion. If the followers assume the imam is resident, they might think their prayer is invalid when he says salam after two rak'ahs. The text cites al-Fatawa that knowledge of the imam's state is a condition for the validity of following; without it, the prayer is invalid. However, al-Mabsut clarifies that this condition is for the continuity (not the beginning) of the congregation: if followers perform the prayer with an imam whose state is unknown, their prayer is invalid even if they are travellers themselves, because the default in a residence is that the person is resident. But if they ask and are told he is a traveller, it becomes valid. Outside the town, the default is not assumed. The recommendation (istihbab) to say the phrase is not to make the salam valid per se, but to inform the followers. There is also a difference of opinion on whether to say it after the first salam or after both; the relied-upon view (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj) is after both.

Key Terms
بناء الضعيف على القوي (binā' al-ḍa'īf 'alā al-qawī): Legal principle: a weaker act can be built upon a stronger act; here the muqtadi's prayer (weak due to not being obligated in sitting) is valid because built upon the imam's stronger prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the primary proof for the validity of a resident following a traveller imam?
A) Qiyas on a resident leading a traveller
B) The Prophet's action and statement when he led Meccans as a traveller
C) The principle of istihsan
D) Ijma' of the Companions

Key Takeaway
A traveller leading a resident in prayer is valid, proven by the Prophet's own practice.

Recommendation for a Traveller Imam to Announce Travel
Details the recommendation and its timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the recommendation, its rationale, and identify the preferred timing for the announcement according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
It is mustahabb for a traveller imam to say 'Inna qawmu safar' after both taslims to prevent followers from invalidating their prayer.

The Prophet's statement 'Inna qawmu safar' is not only a proof for validity but also a recommended practice for any traveller imam. This lesson explores why it is recommended, the conditions under which followers might mistakenly deem their prayer invalid, and the scholarly difference on when exactly the imam should say it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommendation
The text says it is mustahabb (recommended) for every traveller who leads residents to say 'Inna qawmu safar' after the salam.
The phrase is a notification, not a condition for validity.
2
Understand the rationale
Followers might assume the imam is a resident and thus think their prayer is invalid when he says salam after two rak'ahs. The announcement prevents this false assumption.
The default of someone in a town is residence; building on the apparent is obligatory until clarified.
3
Examine the condition of knowledge
Al-Mabsut states that if followers do not know the imam's state, their prayer is invalid unless they ask and are informed. The announcement serves as that information.
Knowledge is a condition for the continuity of congregation, not for initiation.
4
Determine the preferred timing
The scholars differed: is it said after the first taslim or after both? The more correct (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj) is after both taslims.
The first taslim ends the prayer; saying after both ensures full completion.

Source Text

When a Resident Follower Stands and the Imam Intends Iqama
Ruling from Fath al-Qadir on resident follower and imam's iqama

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on a resident follower who stands before the imam's salam when the imam intends iqama, and determine the validity of the follower's prayer.

Core Idea
If a resident follower separates before the imam's salam, the timing of the imam's iqama intention determines validity.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from Fath al-Qadir: a resident follower stands up to complete his prayer separately before the imam's salam. If at that moment the imam intends iqama (to become a resident), the ruling depends on whether the follower has already prostrated. The key is the follower's exit from the imam's prayer must not be final. Let's unpack the conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial action
The resident follower stands up before the imam's salam, intending to complete his prayer alone. This is the trigger.
This action occurs before the imam's taslim.
2
Determine the imam's intention
The imam then intends iqama (to stay in the locality for at least 15 days) – this changes his own prayer from two to four rak'ahs. The timing of this intention relative to the follower's prostration is crucial.
The intention of iqama must be genuine; for prayer purposes, it affects the number of rak'ahs.
3
Assess the follower's prostration
If the imam intends iqama before the follower prostrates (in his separate prayer), the follower must abandon his separation and return to following the imam. If he does not return and prostrates, his prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
The prostration is a key marker: before prostration, the follower's exit is not yet final.
4
Contrast the opposite scenario
If the imam intends iqama after the follower has already prostrated, then the follower's separation is firm, and he completes his prayer alone validly. If he then abandons his separation and follows the imam, his prayer becomes invalid because separation was obligatory.
Once the follower prostrates, he is no longer bound to the imam.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the follower must be attentive to the imam's actions. If the imam signals a change (e.g., intents iqama), the follower must not finalize his separation until after the imam's salam or until he is sure the imam has not changed his intention.
This scenario is rare but illustrates the precision of Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قام المقتدي المقيم قبل سلام الإمام فنوى الإمام الإقامة قبل سجوده رفض ذلك وتابع الإمام، فإن لم يفعل وسجد فسدت لأنه ما لم يسجد لم يستحكم خروجه عن صلاة الإمام قبل سلام الإمام وقد بقي ركعتان على الإمام بواسطة التغير فوجب عليه الاقتداء فيهما، فإذا انفرد فسدت بخلاف ما لو نوى الإمام بعد ما سجد المقتدى فإنه يتم منفرداً، فلو رفض وتابع فسدت لاقتدائه حيث وجب الانفراد كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الخانية والخلاصة : مسافر أم قوماً مقيمين فلما صلى ركعتين نوى الإقامة لا لتحقيق الإقامة بل ليتم صلاة المقيمين لا يصير مقيماً ولا ينقلب فرضه أربعاً ! وفي العمدة: مسافر سبقه الحدث فقدم مقيماً صلاة الإمام وبتأخر ويقدم مسافراً يسلم ثم يتم المقيم صلاته. وفي الخلاصة : مسافر أم مسافرين فأحدث فقدم مسافراً آخر فنوى الثاني الإقامة لا يجب على القوم أن يصلوا أربعاً ! وفي الهداية : وإذا صلى المسافر بالمقيم ركعتين سلم وأتم المقيمون صلاتهم لأن المقتدي التزم الموافقة في الركعتين فينفرد في الباقي كالمسبوق إلا أن أنه لا يقرأ في الأصح لأنه مقتد تحريمة لا فعلاً والفرض صار مؤدى فيتركها احتياطاً بخلاف المسبوق لأنه أدرك قراءة نافلة فلم يتأد الفرض فكان الإتيان أولى ا هـ . وفي الخانية : لا قراءة عليهم يتم.
And if the resident follower stood up before the imam's salam, and the imam intended to stay before his prostration, he should abandon that and follow the imam; if he does not do so and prostrates, his prayer becomes invalid, because as long as he did not prostrate his exit from the imam's prayer is not established before the imam's salam, and there remain two rak'ahs upon the imam due to the change, so it is obligatory upon him to follow in them; if he separates, it becomes invalid, contrary to if the imam intended after the follower had prostrated, for then he completes separately. And if he abandons and follows, it becomes invalid due to his following when separation was obligatory. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Khaniyyah and al-Khulasa: A traveller led a group of residents; when he prayed two rak'ahs he intended to stay, not to actually settle but to complete the prayer of the residents; he does not become a resident nor does his obligatory prayer become four! And in al-Umdah: A traveller was overtaken by a hadath, so he put forward a resident to lead the imam's prayer, and it is delayed; and he puts forward a traveller who says salam, then the resident completes his prayer. And in al-Khulasa: A traveller led travellers, then he had a hadath, so he put forward another traveller, and the second intended to stay; it is not obligatory upon the people to pray four! And in al-Hidayah: When a traveller leads residents and prays two rak'ahs, he says salam, and the residents complete their prayer, because the follower committed to following in the two rak'ahs; he separates in the remainder like a latecomer, except that he does not recite in the correct view, because he is a follower in the opening takbir not in action, and the obligatory prayer was performed, so he leaves it out of caution, unlike the latecomer who caught a supererogatory recitation so the obligation was not performed, so performing it is better. End. And in al-Khaniyyah: There is no recitation upon them.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings from different sources within the Hanafi school regarding a traveller imam and changes in his intention or status. The first case (from Fath al-Qadir) concerns a resident follower who stands up to separate before the imam's salam. If the imam then intends iqama (to become a resident) before the follower prostrates, the follower must return and follow; if he prostrates (making his separation firm), his prayer is invalid. If the imam intends after the follower's prostration, the follower's prayer is valid as separate. The second case (from al-Khaniyyah and al-Khulasa) states that if a traveller imam intends iqama not for actual residence but only to complete the prayer for the residents, he does not actually become a resident and his obligation remains two rak'ahs. The third case (from al-Umdah) deals with a traveller imam who has a hadath (breaks wudu); he can put forward either a resident or another traveller to lead the remainder, with specific rules. The fourth case (from al-Khulasa) involves a traveller imam having a hadath and putting forward another traveller who then intends iqama; the followers are not obliged to pray four rak'ahs. Finally, the Hidayah ruling explains that when a traveller leads residents and says salam after two rak'ahs, the residents complete their prayer individually, similar to a latecomer (masbuq), but with the difference that the follower does not recite in the extra rak'ahs because his obligation was fulfilled (by the imam's recitation). The passage ends by citing al-Khaniyyah that there is no recitation upon them.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqāmah): Intention to stay in a place for at least fifteen days, which changes a traveller's status to resident.
المقتدي المقيم (al-muqtadī al-muqīm): A resident (non-traveller) follower who is praying behind a traveller imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Fath al-Qadir ruling, when does the resident follower's prayer become validly separate from the imam?
A) When the follower stands up
B) When the imam intends iqama
C) When the follower prostrates in his separate prayer
D) When the imam says salam

Key Takeaway
The validity of a resident follower's separation hinges on whether his prostration occurs before or after the imam's intention of iqama.

Traveller Imam's Intention of Iqama Only for the Prayer
Ruling from al-Khaniyyah and al-Khulasa on traveller imam's iqama intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of a traveller imam's intention of iqama when it is solely to complete the residents' prayer, and distinguish it from a genuine intention to settle.

Core Idea
Intending iqama only for the prayer does not change the traveller's status nor his obligation.

Sometimes a traveller imam may intend to stay just to allow the residents to complete a full prayer, without actually settling. Does that intention make him a resident? The passage from al-Khaniyyah and al-Khulasa clarifies that such an intention has no effect on his status or his prayer obligation. Let's explore this subtle but important ruling.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
A traveller leads a group of residents. After two rak'ahs, he intends iqama – but not for actual settlement, only to make his prayer four rak'ahs so the residents can complete theirs.
The intention is purely for the prayer, not for residence.
2
Analyze the effect on the imam's status
The imam does not become a resident (muqim) because the intention lacks sincerity for actual settlement. In Hanafi fiqh, niyyat al-iqama requires a genuine plan to stay at least 15 days.
An intention solely for worship does not create residence.
3
Determine the imam's prayer obligation
Since he is still a traveller, his obligatory prayer remains two rak'ahs (qasr). He should not pray four; if he does, his prayer becomes a nafl? Actually, the ruling says his obligation does not become four – he remains on qasr.
The number of rak'ahs is tied to actual journey status.
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a traveller imam realizes that leading residents requires more rak'ahs, he should not intend iqama artificially. Instead, he should pray two and let the residents complete on their own, as per the Hidayah ruling in another part.
This ruling prevents misuse of niyyat al-iqama.

ولو قام المقتدي المقيم قبل سلام الإمام فنوى الإمام الإقامة قبل سجوده رفض ذلك وتابع الإمام، فإن لم يفعل وسجد فسدت لأنه ما لم يسجد لم يستحكم خروجه عن صلاة الإمام قبل سلام الإمام وقد بقي ركعتان على الإمام بواسطة التغير فوجب عليه الاقتداء فيهما، فإذا انفرد فسدت بخلاف ما لو نوى الإمام بعد ما سجد المقتدى فإنه يتم منفرداً، فلو رفض وتابع فسدت لاقتدائه حيث وجب الانفراد كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الخانية والخلاصة : مسافر أم قوماً مقيمين فلما صلى ركعتين نوى الإقامة لا لتحقيق الإقامة بل ليتم صلاة المقيمين لا يصير مقيماً ولا ينقلب فرضه أربعاً ! وفي العمدة: مسافر سبقه الحدث فقدم مقيماً صلاة الإمام وبتأخر ويقدم مسافراً يسلم ثم يتم المقيم صلاته. وفي الخلاصة : مسافر أم مسافرين فأحدث فقدم مسافراً آخر فنوى الثاني الإقامة لا يجب على القوم أن يصلوا أربعاً ! وفي الهداية : وإذا صلى المسافر بالمقيم ركعتين سلم وأتم المقيمون صلاتهم لأن المقتدي التزم الموافقة في الركعتين فينفرد في الباقي كالمسبوق إلا أن أنه لا يقرأ في الأصح لأنه مقتد تحريمة لا فعلاً والفرض صار مؤدى فيتركها احتياطاً بخلاف المسبوق لأنه أدرك قراءة نافلة فلم يتأد الفرض فكان الإتيان أولى ا هـ . وفي الخانية : لا قراءة عليهم يتم.
And if the resident follower stood up before the imam's salam, and the imam intended to stay before his prostration, he should abandon that and follow the imam; if he does not do so and prostrates, his prayer becomes invalid, because as long as he did not prostrate his exit from the imam's prayer is not established before the imam's salam, and there remain two rak'ahs upon the imam due to the change, so it is obligatory upon him to follow in them; if he separates, it becomes invalid, contrary to if the imam intended after the follower had prostrated, for then he completes separately. And if he abandons and follows, it becomes invalid due to his following when separation was obligatory. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Khaniyyah and al-Khulasa: A traveller led a group of residents; when he prayed two rak'ahs he intended to stay, not to actually settle but to complete the prayer of the residents; he does not become a resident nor does his obligatory prayer become four! And in al-Umdah: A traveller was overtaken by a hadath, so he put forward a resident to lead the imam's prayer, and it is delayed; and he puts forward a traveller who says salam, then the resident completes his prayer. And in al-Khulasa: A traveller led travellers, then he had a hadath, so he put forward another traveller, and the second intended to stay; it is not obligatory upon the people to pray four! And in al-Hidayah: When a traveller leads residents and prays two rak'ahs, he says salam, and the residents complete their prayer, because the follower committed to following in the two rak'ahs; he separates in the remainder like a latecomer, except that he does not recite in the correct view, because he is a follower in the opening takbir not in action, and the obligatory prayer was performed, so he leaves it out of caution, unlike the latecomer who caught a supererogatory recitation so the obligation was not performed, so performing it is better. End. And in al-Khaniyyah: There is no recitation upon them.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings from different sources within the Hanafi school regarding a traveller imam and changes in his intention or status. The first case (from Fath al-Qadir) concerns a resident follower who stands up to separate before the imam's salam. If the imam then intends iqama (to become a resident) before the follower prostrates, the follower must return and follow; if he prostrates (making his separation firm), his prayer is invalid. If the imam intends after the follower's prostration, the follower's prayer is valid as separate. The second case (from al-Khaniyyah and al-Khulasa) states that if a traveller imam intends iqama not for actual residence but only to complete the prayer for the residents, he does not actually become a resident and his obligation remains two rak'ahs. The third case (from al-Umdah) deals with a traveller imam who has a hadath (breaks wudu); he can put forward either a resident or another traveller to lead the remainder, with specific rules. The fourth case (from al-Khulasa) involves a traveller imam having a hadath and putting forward another traveller who then intends iqama; the followers are not obliged to pray four rak'ahs. Finally, the Hidayah ruling explains that when a traveller leads residents and says salam after two rak'ahs, the residents complete their prayer individually, similar to a latecomer (masbuq), but with the difference that the follower does not recite in the extra rak'ahs because his obligation was fulfilled (by the imam's recitation). The passage ends by citing al-Khaniyyah that there is no recitation upon them.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqāmah): Intention to stay in a place for at least fifteen days, which changes a traveller's status to resident.
تحقيق الإقامة (taḥqīq al-iqāmah): Actual settlement – the genuine intention to reside.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khaniyyah and al-Khulasa, if a traveller imam intends iqama only to complete the residents' prayer, what happens?
A) He becomes a resident and must pray four rak'ahs.
B) He remains a traveller and his obligation stays two rak'ahs.
C) His prayer becomes invalid.
D) The residents must also intend iqama.

Key Takeaway
An insincere intention of iqama solely for prayer purposes does not change the traveller's status or obligation.

Traveller Imam's Substitution and Residents Completing Prayer
Rulings from al-Umdah, al-Khulasa, and al-Hidayah on substitution and completion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings when a traveller imam has a hadath and substitutes another imam, and when a traveller leads residents and says salam after two rak'ahs.

Core Idea
When a traveller imam is excused, the substitution and the residents' completion follow specific rules similar to a masbuq.

This lesson covers two connected scenarios from al-Umdah and al-Hidayah. First, a traveller imam breaks wudu and must put forward another imam. Second, when a traveller imam leads residents and says salam after two rak'ahs, the residents continue like masbuqs but without recitation. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi approach to congregational prayer continuity.

Guided Path
1
Scenario 1: Hadath substitution
A traveller imam has a hadath (breaks wudu) during the prayer. He can put forward either a resident or another traveller to lead the remainder. The text says 'وقدم مقيماً صلاة الإمام وبتأخر' – he puts forward a resident to lead the imam's prayer, and it is delayed? Or he puts forward a traveller who says salam, then the resident completes.
The substitution must be for the remaining part; the new imam continues where the old left off.
2
Scenario 2: Traveller leading residents – after two rak'ahs
When a traveller leads residents and prays two rak'ahs, he says salam. The residents then stand and complete the remaining two rak'ahs individually (or as a congregation without an imam?). They are like masbuqs who missed the first two rak'ahs, but there is a key difference: they do not recite in the extra rak'ahs because their obligation was fulfilled by the imam's recitation.
The Hidayah ruling compares them to masbuqs but with a distinction.
3
The recitation issue
The passage states that the residents do not recite in the remaining rak'ahs because the imam's recitation counted for them. This is the preferred view (الأصح). In al-Khaniyyah, it says explicitly 'لا قراءة عليهم' (no recitation upon them).
Some Hanafi sources may say they should recite, but the relied-upon view is no recitation.
4
Applying the rulings
In both scenarios, the key is maintaining the validity of the prayer. Substitution must be done correctly, and residents completing after a traveller imam should not recite, unlike a typical masbuq who recites.
These rules ensure the prayer is performed correctly without unnecessary additions.

Salah — Prayer

Traveler Imam Leading Residents: Completion Without Recitation
Sharh on Kanz al-Daqaiq: how residents complete prayer behind a traveler imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a traveler imam leading residents, explain the qiyas to the masbuq, and identify when residents do or do not recite in the remaining rak'ahs.

Core Idea
A resident who prays two rak'ahs behind a traveler imam completes alone without recitation, like a masbuq but with a key difference in recitation.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rule from al-Hidayah: when a traveler imam leads residents and prays only two rak'ahs, the residents complete the remaining two rak'ahs by themselves. The ruling is grounded in qiyas to the masbuq (latecomer), but the residents do not recite in those remaining rak'ahs, unlike a masbuq. We also explore the recommendation (istihbab) of the imam announcing his travel and intra-Hanafi differences on the exact wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the core ruling
The scenario: a traveler (musafir) imam leads residents (muqimin) in a four-rak'ah prayer (Dhuhr, Asr, or Isha). The imam prays two rak'ahs and says salam. The core ruling from al-Hidayah: the residents complete the remaining two rak'ahs by themselves.
This ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the qiyas to the masbuq
The proof is qiyas: just as a latecomer (masbuq) follows the imam only for the rak'ahs he catches and then completes alone, so does the resident muqtadi. The effective cause (illa) is that the muqtadi committed to follow only for the number of rak'ahs the imam performs (two in this case).
The text explicitly says: 'li-anna al-muqtadi iltazama al-muwafaqah fi al-rak'atayn fa-yanfaridu fi al-baqi ka al-masbuq'.
3
Note the key difference in recitation
Unlike the masbuq, the resident does NOT recite (qira'ah) in the remaining rak'ahs. Reasoning: the resident is still a follower (muqtadi) in the opening takbir (tahrimah), and the fard of recitation has been fulfilled by the imam's recitation. Recitation is omitted as a precaution (ihtiyat). The masbuq, on the other hand, did not hear the imam's recitation for the rak'ahs he missed, so he recites.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position; some earlier scholars held that residents should recite.
4
Examine the imam's announcement
The passage states it is mustahabb (recommended) for the traveler imam to say after the salam 'We are a traveling people' or similar, to inform the muqtadis. This is not wajib, because the muqtadis can complete and then ask. There is a difference whether to say it after the first taslimah or after both; the correct view (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj) is after both.
The recommendation is based on avoiding confusion; the muqtadis might mistakenly think the imam is a resident and their own prayer invalid.
5
Handle edge cases from the text
If a muqtadi stands before the imam's salam and the imam then intends iqama (residency) before prostrating, the muqtadi must reject his standing and follow the imam; if he prostrates, his prayer is invalid. If the imam intends iqama only to complete the residents' prayer without actually settling, he does not become a resident and his fard remains two. If residents mistakenly complete their prayer with the imam (thinking he is a resident and will pray four), their prayer is invalid because it is following a mutanaffil.
Al-Ramli restricts the last case: if the residents intended to separate (mufaraqah) from the imam, their prayer is valid even if they physically completed with him.

فإنا قوم سفر. وهو جمع سافر كركب جمع راكب. ويستحب أن يقول ذلك بعد السلام كل مسافر صلى بمقيم لاحتمال أن خلفه لا يعرف حاله ولا يتيسر له الاجتماع بالإمام قبل ذهابه فيحكم حينئذ بفساد صلاة نفسه بناء على ظن إقامة الإمام ثم إفساده بسلامه على رأس الركعتين، وهذا محمل ما في الفتاوى إذا اقتدى بالإمام لا يدري أمسافر هو أم مقيم لا يصح لأن العلم بحال الإمام شرط الأداء بجماعة ا هـ . لا أنه شرط في الابتداء لما في المبسوط : رجل صلى الظهر بالقوم بقرية أو مصر ركعتين وهم يدرون أمسافر هو أم مقيم فصلاتهم فاسدة، سواء كانوا مقيمين أم ،مسافرين لأن الظاهر من حال من في موضع الإقامة أنه مقيم والبناء على الظاهر واجب حتى يتبين خلافه، فإن سألوه فأخبرهم أنه مسافر جازت صلاتهم وفي القنية : وإن كان خارج المصر لا تفسد ويجوز الأخذ بالظاهر في مثله. وإنما كان قول الإمام ذلك مستحباً لأنه لم يتعين معرفاً صحة سلامه لهم فإنه ينبغي أن يتموا ثم يسألوه فتحصل المعرفة. واختلفوا هل يقوله بعد التسليمة الأولى أو بعد التسليمتين؟ الأصح الثاني في السراج الوهاج. ولو قام المقتدي المقيم قبل سلام الإمام فنوى الإمام الإقامة قبل سجوده رفض ذلك وتابع الإمام، فإن لم يفعل وسجد فسدت لأنه ما لم يسجد لم يستحكم خروجه عن صلاة الإمام قبل سلام الإمام وقد بقي ركعتان على الإمام بواسطة التغير فوجب عليه الاقتداء فيهما، فإذا انفرد فسدت بخلاف ما لو نوى الإمام بعد ما سجد المقتدى فإنه يتم منفرداً، فلو رفض وتابع فسدت لاقتدائه حيث وجب الانفراد كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الخانية والخلاصة : مسافر أم قوماً مقيمين فلما صلى ركعتين نوى الإقامة لا لتحقيق الإقامة بل ليتم صلاة المقيمين لا . يصير مقيماً ولا ينقلب فرضه أربعاً ! وفي العمدة: مسافر سبقه الحدث فقدم مقيماً صلاة الإمام وبتأخر ويقدم مسافراً يسلم ثم يتم المقيم صلاته. وفي الخلاصة : مسافر أم مسافرين فأحدث فقدم مسافراً آخر فنوى الثاني الإقامة لا يجب على القوم أن يصلوا أربعاً ! وفي الهداية : وإذا صلى المسافر بالمقيم ركعتين سلم وأتم المقيمون صلاتهم لأن المقتدي التزم الموافقة في الركعتين فينفرد في الباقي كالمسبوق إلا أن أنه لا يقرأ في الأصح لأنه مقتد تحريمة لا فعلاً والفرض صار مؤدى فيتركها احتياطاً بخلاف المسبوق لأنه أدرك قراءة نافلة فلم يتأد الفرض فكان الإتيان أولى ا هـ . وفي الخانية : لا قراءة عليهم يتم

قوله: (وإنما كان قول الإمام ذلك مستحباً) أي لا واجباً قوله : (لا يصير مقيماً ولا ينقلب فرضه أربعاً) قال في الظهيرية تلوه حتى لو أتم المقيمون صلاتهم معه فسدت صلاتهم لأن هذا اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل ولا يصح ا هـ. قال الرملي : يجب تقييده بما إذا لم ينووا مفارقته، أما إذا نووا مفارقته لا تفسد صلاتهم وإن وافقوه في الإتمام صورة إذ لا مانع من صحة مفارقته بعد إتمام فرضه واتصال النفل منه بصلاته لا يمنعها بلا شبهة. وفي قوله «لم أتم المقيمون معه» إشارة إلى
Book of Prayer, Chapter on the Traveler. ... We are a traveling people. It is recommended that every traveler who prays with a resident say that after the salam, because those behind him might not know his situation and may not be able to meet him before he leaves, so they would deem their own prayer invalid based on the assumption that the imam is a resident, and then his salam after two rak'ahs would invalidate their prayer. This is the interpretation of what is in al-Fatawa: if one follows an imam not knowing whether he is a traveler or resident, it is not valid because knowledge of the imam's state is a condition for the performance of congregational prayer, but not for its initiation. In al-Mabsut: a man prayed Dhuhr with people in a village or city, performing two rak'ahs while they knew he was a traveler? Their prayer is invalid, whether they were residents or travelers, because the apparent state of one in a place of residence is that he is a resident, and acting on the apparent is obligatory until the contrary becomes clear. If they asked him and he informed them he is a traveler, their prayer becomes valid. In al-Qunyah: if he is outside the city, it is not invalid and acting on the apparent is permissible in such a case. The imam's saying that is only recommended because it is not specified as a means to know the validity of his salam for them; rather, they should complete then ask him, so knowledge is attained. They differed whether he says it after the first taslimah or after both? The correct is the second in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. ...
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing rulings related to a traveler imam leading resident muqtadis. The text begins by explaining the recommendation (istihbab) for a traveler imam to announce after the salam that he is a traveler, citing the reason that muqtadis may mistakenly think he is a resident and thus believe their own prayer invalid when he prays only two rak'ahs. The passage then clarifies that knowledge of the imam's state is a condition for the validity of the congregational prayer (shart al-ada'), not for its initiation (shart al-ibtida'), based on a narration from al-Mabsut. It discusses the case where muqtadis follow an imam without knowing his state: if they ask and he informs them, their prayer is valid. Then, it presents the main rule from al-Hidayah: if a traveler imam prays two rak'ahs with residents and says salam, the residents complete their prayer by themselves. The reasoning is that the muqtadi committed to follow only for two rak'ahs, so he separates for the remainder, like a latecomer (masbuq). However, unlike the masbuq, he does not recite (qira'ah) in the remaining rak'ahs because he is a follower in the tahrimah (opening takbir) but not in the actions, and the fard has been fulfilled by the imam's recitation; he leaves it out as an ihtiyat (precaution). The text then quotes from al-Khaniyah that there is no qira'ah upon them, no forgetfulness (sahw) if they err, and they do not follow one another. It then discusses several sub-cases: a resident muqtadi who stands before the imam's salam and the imam intends iqama before his prostration—the muqtadi must reject his standing and follow; if he does not and prostrates, his prayer is invalid. Also, if a traveler imam intends iqama not actually to settle but to complete the residents' prayer, he does not become a resident and his fard does not become four. The commentary further clarifies that the imam's saying is only mustahabb, not wajib, and that if residents complete their prayer with him (thinking he is a resident), their prayer is invalid because it is following a mutanaffil (one performing nafl) by a muqtadi who is praying fard. Al-Ramli restricts this to when they do not intend to separate; if they intend separation, their prayer is valid. The passage ends abruptly with a reference to the statement 'they did not complete with him'.

Key Terms
مقيم (muqim): A resident; one who is not traveling and therefore prays the full four rak'ahs for Dhuhr, Asr, and Isha.
مسافر (musafir): A traveler who fulfills the conditions for qasr (shortening prayer), typically a journey of three days or more.
مقتدي (muqtadi): Follower in congregational prayer; one who prays behind an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a traveler imam leads residents in prayer and prays two rak'ahs, what should the residents do in the remaining two rak'ahs?
A) They should also pray two rak'ahs and say salam with him.
B) They should complete the remaining two rak'ahs on their own without recitation.
C) They should recite aloud in the remaining two rak'ahs.
D) Their prayer is invalid and they must repeat it.

Key Takeaway
When a traveler imam leads residents, the residents complete the prayer alone without recitation, supported by qiyas to the masbuq but with a key difference in the recitation rule.

The Three Homelands: Definitions and Invalidations
Definition of original and residency homelands and rules for their nullification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define watan asli and watan iqama, state the conditions for each, and apply the invalidation rules to determine whether a traveler prays qasr or tamam.

Core Idea
Your original homeland is only lost by moving your family; residency ends by travel, a new home, or returning to origin.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the Hanafi classification of homelands (watan), which directly affects whether a traveler shortens his prayers. The key distinction is between one's permanent home (watan asli) and a temporary residence (watan iqama). Once you understand how each is established and invalidated, you can determine the prayer obligation in many common scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of watan
Based on the passage, list watan asli, watan iqama, and watan al-safar, and note the basis for each (family, duration, etc.).
Watan asli is for permanent settlement; watan iqama for 15+ days; watan safar is everywhere else.
2
Define watan asli and its invalidation
Watan asli requires family and intention to stay permanently; it is invalidated only by another watan asli (moving family elsewhere). Note the hadith of Uthman (ra).
The rule: a thing is invalidated by its like, not by what is inferior.
3
Define watan iqama and its invalidation
Watan iqama is a place where the traveler intends to stay 15 days or more; it is invalidated by watan asli, another watan iqama, or travel.
Three invalidators: superior (asli), equal (iqama), opposite (travel).
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Al-Muhit reports a difference: does watan asli require both family and property, or only family? Al-Mujtaba gives a practical fatwa that both towns remain watan asli if one has family in both.
The mufta bihi position is that family is essential; property alone does not make watan asli.
5
Apply the rules to a scenario
Given a hypothetical person with family in one town and property in another, determine his watan and prayer length.
Use the rule: only moving family invalidates watan asli; property alone does not.

كتاب الصلاة باب المسافر
وبعكسه
فيهما ويبطل الوطن الأصلي بمثله لا السفر ووطن الإقامة بمثله والسفر صح
فيما يقضون ولا سهو عليهم إذا سهوا ولا يقتدي أحدهم بالآخر ا هـ . فلو اقتدى أحدهم بالآخر فسدت صلاة المقتدي لأنه اقتدى في موضع يجب عليهم الانفراد وصلاة الإمام تامة . كذا في البدائع. وفي القنية : اقتدى مقيم بمسافر فترك القعدة مع إمامه فسدت فالقعدتان فرض في حقه، وقيل لا تفسد وهي نفل في حق المقتدي ا هـ .
قوله : (ويبطل الوطن الأصلي بمثله لا السفر ووطن الإقامة بمثله والسفر والأصلي) لأن الشيء يبطل بما هو . مثله لا بما هو دونه فلا يصلح مبطلاً له : وروي أن عثمان رضي الله عنه كان حاجاً يصلي بعرفات أربعاً فاتبعوه فاعتذر وقال : إني تأهلت بمكة وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «من تأهل ببلدة فهو منها والوطن الأصلي هو وطن الإنسان في بلدته أو بلدة أخرى اتخذها داراً وتوطن بها مع أهله وولده وليس من قصده الارتحال عنها بل التعيش بها وهذا الوطن يبطل بمثله لا غير وهو أن يتوطن في بلدة أخرى وينقل الأهل إليها فيخرج الأول من أن يكون وطناً أصلياً حتى لو دخله مسافراً لا يتم قيدنا بكونه انتقل عن الأول بأهله لأنه لو لم ينتقل بهم ولكنه استحدث أهلاً في بلدة أخرى فإن الأول لم يبطل ويتم فيهما . وقيد بقوله «بمثله» لأنه لو باع داره ونقل عياله وخرج يريد أن يتوطن بلدة أخرى ثم بداله أن لا يتوطن ما قصده أولاً ويتوطن بلدة غيرها فمر ببلده الأول فإنه يصلي أربعاً لأنه لم يتوطن غيره. وفي المحيط : ولو كان له أهل بالكوفة وأهل بالبصرة فمات أهله بالبصرة وبقي له دور وعقار بالبصرة، قيل البصرة لا تبقى وطناً له لأنها إنما كانت وطناً بالأهل لا بالعقار، ألا ترى أنه لو تأهل ببلدة لم يكن له فيها عقار صارت وطناً له . وقيل : تبقى وطناً له لأنها كانت وطناً له بالأهل والدار جميعاً، فبزوال أحدهما لا يرتفع الوطن كوطن الإقامة تبقى ببقاء الثقل وإن أقام بموضع آخر ا هـ. وفي المجتبى : نقل القولين فيما إذا نقل أهله ومتاعه وبقي له دور وعقار ثم قال : وهذا جواب واقعة ابتلينا بها وكثير من المسلمين المتوطنين في البلاد ولهم دور وعقار في القرى البعيدة منها يصيفون بها بأهلهم ومتاعهم فلا بد من حفظها أنهما وطنان له لا يبطل أحدهما بالآخر. وقوله «لا السفر» أي لا يبطل الأصلي بالسفر حتى يصير مقيماً بالعود إليه من غير نية الإقامة، وكذا لا يبطل بوطن الإقامة. وأما وطن الإقامة فهو الوطن الذي يقصد المسافر الإقامة فيه وهو صالح لها نصف شهر وهو ينتقض بواحد من ثلاثة : بالأصلي لأنه فوقه وبمثله وبالسفر لأنه صنده .
ذلك وسكوت قاضيخان وصاحب الخلاصة عن صلاة المقيمين ربما يكون لهذا التفصيل والله تعالى أعلم قوله : (ولا سهو عليهم إذا سهوا هذا مبني على ما قاله الكرخي وهو خلاف ما تقدم تصحيحه عن البدائع .
قوله : (وكذا لا يبطل بوطن (الإقامة قال في النهر : ولو صرح المصنف به لعلم السفر بالأولى
Book of Prayer, Chapter on the Traveler. And its opposite. In both: the original homeland is invalidated by its like, not by travel; and the residency homeland is invalidated by its like, by travel, and by the original. ... He said: (And the original homeland is invalidated by its like, not by travel, and the residency homeland by its like, by travel, and by the original). Because a thing is invalidated by what is its like, not by what is inferior, so it cannot be an invalidator. It is narrated that Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) was performing Hajj and prayed four at Arafat, so they followed him, and he apologized saying: 'I have taken a wife in Mecca,' and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever takes a wife in a town, he is from it.' The original homeland is a person's homeland in his own town or another town he takes as a residence and settles there with his family and children, not intending to leave it but to live there. This homeland is invalidated only by its like, i.e., by settling in another town and moving his family there, so the first ceases to be an original homeland such that if he enters it as a traveler, he does not complete. Our restriction 'by moving from the first with his family' is because if he did not move them but acquired a new family in another town, the first is not invalidated and he prays complete in both. ... As for the residency homeland, it is the homeland where the traveler intends to reside and is suitable for residence for half a month. It is nullified by one of three: by the original homeland because it is superior, by its like, and by travel because it is against it. ... And the silence of Qadikhan and the author of al-Khulasa regarding the prayer of residents may be due to this detail, and Allah knows best. He said: (And there is no forgetfulness upon them if they forget) - this is based on what al-Karkhi said, contrary to what was previously corrected from al-Bada'i. He said: (And similarly, it is not invalidated by the residency homeland) - al-Nahr said: If the author had clarified this, the ruling on travel would be known by priority.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'The original homeland is invalidated by its like, not by travel; and the residency homeland by its like, by travel, and by the original.' The commentator explains the definitions of the three types of watan (homeland) in Hanafi fiqh: watan asli (original homeland), watan iqama (residency homeland), and watan al-safar (travel homeland). Watan asli is the place where a person has settled with his family and property with no intention of leaving permanently. It is invalidated only by another watan asli, i.e., by moving the family to another town and settling there. Once a new watan asli is established, the old one ceases to be watan asli, and if one enters it again, he prays as a traveler (qasr) unless he intends to reside. If one only acquires property or a new family without moving the original family, both towns remain watan asli, and he prays complete in both. This is supported by the narration about Uthman (ra) who married in Mecca and thus considered it his homeland. Watan iqama is a place where a traveler intends to reside for at least fifteen days. It is weaker than watan asli and is nullified by (1) returning to one's watan asli, (2) establishing another watan iqama, or (3) traveling (since travel is opposite to residence). Watan al-safar is simply any place that is not watan asli or watan iqama; the traveler shortens his prayer there. The passage also addresses a subsidiary issue: if residents follow each other in prayer after the imam's salam (as discussed in the previous lesson), there is disagreement about whether they should recite and whether forgetfulness (sahw) applies. The commentator notes that al-Karkhi's view (no sahw) contradicts what was corrected from al-Bada'i. The passage ends with a note that if the original text had clarified the non-invalidation by watan iqama, the ruling on travel would be understood by primary analogy.

Key Terms
وطن أصلي (watan asli): The original homeland where a person has settled with his family and intends to live permanently; it invalidates only by another watan asli.
وطن إقامة (watan iqama): A homeland of residency where a traveler intends to stay for fifteen days or more; it is invalidated by watan asli, another watan iqama, or travel.
وطن سفر (watan safar): A travel homeland, i.e., any place that is not watan asli or watan iqama; the traveler shortens prayer here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following invalidates a watan iqama according to the Hanafi school?
A) Traveling to a different city for a day trip.
B) Intending to stay for 10 days in another city.
C) Returning to one's original homeland (watan asli).
D) Selling one's property in the residency.

Key Takeaway
Your original homeland is defined by family settlement, not property; it is lost only by moving your family to another permanent home.

Nullification of Dwelling Types in Traveler's Prayer
Commentary on matn ruling about nullification of dwellings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for nullification of the original dwelling and the dwelling of stay, and distinguish the two narrations regarding the condition of preceding travel for the dwelling of stay.

Core Idea
The original dwelling nullifies only by its like; dwelling of stay nullifies by its like, original, or travel.

When does a traveler become a resident in prayer? The Hanafi school teaches that the type of dwelling (watan) determines whether one completes or shortens ṣalāh. This lesson unpacks the classification of dwellings and their nullification, grounding the rulings in the incident of Sayyidunā ‘Uthmān (raḍiya Allāhu ‘anhu) and a key prophetic statement. We will also examine an internal Hanafi dispute on the conditions for a dwelling of stay.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two dwelling types
Identify the original dwelling (watan aṣlī) as the permanent home with family, and the dwelling of stay (watan iqāmah) as a temporary residence of at least half a month for a traveler.
The original dwelling is not nullified by travel or temporary stay; only a new original dwelling nullifies it.
2
State nullification rules
Memorize: al-watan al-aṣlī yubṭalu bi-mithlihi lā bi-s-safar; wa-watan al-iqāmah yubṭalu bi-mithlihi wa bi-s-safar wa bi-l-aṣlī.
The matn phrasing is the core rule.
3
Analyze the proof
Examine the incident of ‘Uthmān (ra) who prayed four rak‘ahs at ‘Arafāt because he had married in Makkah, and the prophetic hadith: 'Whoever takes a wife in a town, he is from it.' Understand how this shows that marrying in a town makes it akin to a permanent dwelling.
The hadith is a sunnah āḥād with zannī thubūt and dalālah; it supports the ruling that a spouse creates a new original dwelling.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that within the school, a narration from Imām Muḥammad requires that travel precede the dwelling of stay, while the ẓāhir ar-riwāyah (Abū Ḥanīfah and Abū Yūsuf) does not require it. Recognize the practical difference (thamarah al-khilāf) in a case where a person leaves his city without intention of travel and stays in a village.
The muftā bihī is the ẓāhir ar-riwāyah.
5
Apply the rule to examples
Work through the examples in the passage: the Cairene who goes to Bilbeis, then to al-Ṣāliḥiyyah. Track how each dwelling is nullified by the three factors.
The commentary uses these examples to illustrate the three nullifiers of watan iqāmah.

السفر والثاني أن تكون مدة سفر بينه أي بين الموضع الذي أنشأ منه السفر وبين ما صار إليه منه أي وبين الموضع الذي صار إليه من الموضع الأول ونوى فيه الإقامة، فقوله لو خرج تفريع على الشرط الأول ، وقوله وكذا إذا قصد «الخ تفريع على الشرط الثاني، قوله : العدم تقدم السفر) وعليه فلو خرج من تلك القرية لحاجة ثم قصد الرجوع إلى مصره، ومر بتلك القرية يقصر لأنه قصد مسيرة السفر وليست القرية وطناً له قوله : (مثاله قاهري الخ) أي مثال بطلان وطن الإقامة بواحد من الثلاثة، فقوله فإن قصد الخ فيه بطلانه بالسفر وقوله وإن لم يقصد ذلك الخ» فيه بطلان بمثله لأن ما بين بلبيس والصالحية دون مسافة القصر كما بين بلبيس والقاهرة، وقوله «وإن عاد إلى مصر» فيه بطلانه بالأهلي قوله : (حتى يتم إذا دخله يعني إذا خرج من الصالحية وأراد الرجوع إلى القاهرة ومر ببلبيس يتم لأن وطنه بها لم يبطل بالخروج إلى الصالحية لأنه ليس بوطن مثلة ولا سفر فيبقى وطنه ببلبيس، وهذا التمثيل كله مبني على ظاهر الرواية من عدم اشتراط تقديم السفر لثبوت وظن الإقامة. وفي فتح القدير ورواية الحسن يعني هذه الرواية تبیّن أن السفر الناقض لوطن الإقامة ما ليس فيه مرور على وطن الإقامة أو ما يكون المرور فيه بعد سير مدة السفر ا هـ . ولهذا أتم ببلبيس في أن ما مسألتنا مع ا بين الصالحية والقاهرة مدة سفر لأن فيه مروراً على وطن الإقامة قوله : (ممنوع) قال الرملي : لقائل : يمنعه لأن السفر إنما يبطل وطن الإقامة أن لو خرج منه مسافراً فكذا وطن السكني لأن السفر لم يتصل به تأمل. كذا رأيته بخط بعضهم ا قلت : وقد ذكر مثله الشيخ إبراهيم المداري الحلبي في حاشيته على الدر المختار عن شيخه المحقق السيد علي الضرير ثم قال: وهو وجيه فإن من نوى الإقامة بموضع نصف شهر ثم خرج منه لا يريد السفر ثم عاد مريداً سفراً ومر بذلك أتم مع أنه أنشأ سفراً بعد اتخاذ هذا الموضع دار إقامة، فثبت أن إنشاء السفر لا يبطل وطن الإقامة إلا إذا أنشأ السفر منه فليكن وطن السكنى كذلك، فما صورة الزيلعي صحيح ومن تصويره علمت أنه لا هـ.
Book of Prayer, Chapter on the Traveler. And its opposite. In both it is valid: the original dwelling is nullified by its like, not by travel; the dwelling of stay is nullified by its like and by travel. It is valid regarding what they make up, and there is no forgetfulness upon them if they forget, and one of them should not follow another in prayer. End quote. So if one followed another in prayer, the prayer of the follower becomes invalid because he followed in a situation where they must pray individually, while the prayer of the imam is complete. Thus in al-Badai'. In al-Qunyah: a resident followed a traveler and omitted the sitting with his imam, so his prayer became invalid because the two sittings are obligatory in his case, and it is said it does not become invalid, and it is supererogatory in the follower's case. End quote. His saying: (And the original dwelling is nullified by its like, not by travel, and the dwelling of stay by its like and by travel and by the original) because a thing is nullified by what is its like, not by what is inferior to it, so it is not fit to be a nullifier. And it is narrated that Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, was a pilgrim and prayed four rak'ahs at Arafat, so they followed him, and he apologized saying: I have taken a wife in Mecca. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever takes a wife in a town, he is from it.' The original dwelling is a person's dwelling in his town or another town that he takes as a home and resides there with his wife and children, not intending to leave it but to live there. This dwelling is nullified only by its like, which is when he settles in another town and moves his family there, then the first ceases to be an original dwelling, so that if he enters it as a traveler he does not complete his prayer. We restricted it to moving with his family, because if he did not move with them but acquires a family in another town, the first is not nullified and he completes prayer in both. And he restricted it with 'by its like' because if he sold his house and moved his family and left intending to settle in another town, then later decided not to settle there but to settle in another town, then he passes by his first town, he prays four rak'ahs because he has not settled elsewhere. In al-Muhit: if he had family in Kufa and family in Basra, then his family in Basra died while he still has houses and property in Basra, it is said Basra does not remain his dwelling because it was only a dwelling by family not by property; do you not see that if he married in a town where he had no property, it becomes his dwelling. And it is said: it remains his dwelling because it was his dwelling by both family and house, so with the removal of one, the dwelling does not cease, like the dwelling of stay remains by the remaining of heavy belongings even if he stays elsewhere. End quote. In al-Mujtaba: the two opinions are narrated concerning when he moves his family and belongings and still has houses and property. Then he said: This is an answer to an incident that befell us, and many Muslims settle in cities while having houses and property in distant villages, spending summers there with their families and belongings, so it is necessary to preserve that they are two dwellings for him, one not nullifying the other. His saying: 'not by travel' means that the original dwelling is not nullified by travel, so that he becomes a resident by returning to it without intention to stay. Likewise, it is not nullified by the dwelling of stay. As for the dwelling of stay, it is the dwelling where a traveler intends to stay, and it is valid for half a month, and it is nullified by one of three: by the original dwelling because it is above it, by its like, and by travel because it opposes it. The silence of Qadikhan and the author of al-Khulasa about the prayer of residents may be due to this detail. And Allah knows best. His saying: (And no forgetfulness upon them if they forget) is based on what al-Karkhi said, which contradicts what was previously corrected from al-Badai'. His saying: (Likewise, it is not nullified by the dwelling of stay. He said in al-Nahr: if the author had clarified, the priority would be known. He made it absolute, indicating that preceding travel is not a condition for establishing the original dwelling or the dwelling of stay. The original is by consensus, and for the dwelling of stay there are two narrations: the apparent narration is that it is not a condition; in another from Muhammad, the dwelling only becomes a dwelling of stay on condition that travel precedes it and that between it and the place he came from there is a travel distance. So if he left his city without intention to travel, and arrived at a village and intended to stay there fifteen days, that village does not become a dwelling of stay, even if there is a travel distance between them, because of the lack of preceding travel. Similarly, if he intended a journey of travel distance and left, then when he arrived at a village whose distance from his home is less than travel distance, and he intended to stay there fifteen days, he does not become a resident and that village does not become a dwelling of stay. Example: A Cairene went to Bilbeis and intended to stay there half a month, then left it. If he intended a journey of three days and traveled, his dwelling in Bilbeis is nullified, so if he passes by it on return, he does not complete. If he did not intend that and went to al-Salihiyyah, and he intended to stay there, he completes there and his dwelling in Bilbeis is nullified, so if he returns to it as a traveler, he does not complete. If he did not intend to stay there for half a month... His saying: (on condition that travel precedes it) implies an addition, i.e. intention of travel, as indicated by what follows. Its summary: two conditions are required: first, that the intention of travel precedes; second, that there is a travel distance between the place from which he initiated travel and the place he came to, i.e., the place where he intended to stay. So his saying 'if he left' branches from the first condition, and his saying 'similarly if he intended' branches from the second condition. His saying: 'due to lack of preceding travel' and accordingly, if he left that village for a need, then intended to return to his city and passed by that village, he shortens because he intended a travel distance and the village is not his dwelling. His saying: (Example: a Cairene...) i.e., an example of nullification of the dwelling of stay by one of the three. His saying 'if he intended' shows nullification by travel; his saying 'if he did not intend that' shows nullification by its like because the distance between Bilbeis and al-Salihiyyah is less than the shortening distance, like between Bilbeis and Cairo; his saying 'and if he returns to Cairo' shows nullification by the original dwelling. His saying: (so that he completes when entering it) means if he leaves al-Salihiyyah and wants to return to Cairo and passes by Bilbeis, he completes because his dwelling there was not nullified by going to al-Salihiyyah, since it is neither a dwelling like it nor travel, so his dwelling in Bilbeis remains. All this illustration is based on the apparent narration that preceding travel is not a condition for establishing the dwelling of stay. In Fath al-Qadir and the narration of al-Hasan, i.e., this narration shows that the travel that nullifies the dwelling of stay is that which does not involve passing through the dwelling of stay, or where the passing is after traveling the travel distance. End quote. Hence he completed at Bilbeis in our case where the distance between al-Salihiyyah and Cairo is a travel distance, because it involves passing through the dwelling of stay. His saying: (objectionable) al-Ramli said: an objector may object because travel only nullifies the dwelling of stay if he leaves from it as a traveler; likewise the dwelling of residence because travel was not connected to it. Consider. I saw it in the handwriting of some. I say: similar has been mentioned by Shaykh Ibrahim al-Madari al-Halabi in his hashia on al-Durr al-Mukhtar from his teacher the muhaqqiq al-Sayyid Ali al-Darir, then he said: it is sound, for whoever intends to stay in a place for half a month, then leaves it not intending travel, then returns intending travel and passes by it, he completes, even though he initiated travel after making that place a dwelling of stay. So it is established that initiating travel does not nullify the dwelling of stay unless he initiates travel from it. So let the dwelling of residence be likewise. Thus the picture of al-Zayla'i is correct, and from its depiction you know that it is not. End.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the chapter of the traveler from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It explains the rules regarding how different types of dwellings (watan) affect whether a traveler shortens or completes prayer. The matn states: 'the original dwelling is nullified by its like, not by travel; the dwelling of stay is nullified by its like and by travel.' The commentator elaborates that the original dwelling (watan asli) is where a person lives permanently with family. It can only be nullified by establishing another original dwelling and moving family there, not by mere travel or temporary stay. Evidence is the incident of Uthman (RA) who prayed four at Arafat because he had married in Mecca, and the hadith 'whoever marries in a town, he is from it.' The dwelling of stay (watan iqama) is nullified by any of three: the original dwelling, another dwelling of stay, or travel. The passage then discusses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding whether travel must precede the establishment of a dwelling of stay. The zahir al-riwayah (relied-upon position) says no, while a narration from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan says yes, requiring prior travel of travel distance. The commentary provides examples from Cairo to Bilbeis and al-Salihiyyah. Later objections by al-Ramli are addressed, confirming that initiating travel from the dwelling of stay nullifies it, but mere passage does not.

Key Terms
الوطن الأصلي (al-watan al-asli): The original permanent dwelling where a person resides with family, not intending to leave.
وطن الإقامة (watan al-iqama): A temporary dwelling where a traveler intends to stay for at least half a month.
مدة سفر (muddat safar): The distance of travel that permits shortening prayer, typically three days' journey (approx. 80 km).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ẓāhir ar-riwāyah, what is the minimum stay required for a place to become a dwelling of stay (watan iqama)?
A) 3 days
B) 7 days
C) 15 days (half a month)
D) 30 days

Key Takeaway
The original dwelling is nullified only by another original dwelling; the dwelling of stay is more vulnerable, being nullified by any of three factors: original, like, or travel.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Condition of Preceding Travel for Watan al-Iqama: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on watan al-iqama conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi positions on whether preceding travel is required to establish a watan al-iqama and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A watan al-iqama does not require preceding travel according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions for establishing a watan al-iqama (residence that changes a traveler's status to resident). The dispute centers on whether prior travel and a specific travel distance are necessary. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for correctly determining when a traveler must perform full prayers versus shortening them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Recognize that the issue is whether 'preceding travel' (taqdim al-safar) is a necessary condition for a place to become a watan al-iqama. The passage states that for the original homeland (watan al-asli) there is consensus that no such condition exists, but for watan al-iqama there are two narrations.
2
State the Two Hanafi Positions
According to the zahir al-riwayah, preceding travel is not a condition. According to a riwaya from Imam Muhammad, it is a condition, along with travel distance (three days' journey).
The zahir al-riwayah is the relied-upon position.
3
Analyze the Proofs
The zahir al-riwayah relies on the general principle that a 15-day residence alone changes the ruling, regardless of arrival method. Muhammad's view draws an analogy to the original homeland, which is established by travel.
Both positions are based on valid ijtihad within the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The difference matters when a person leaves his city without travel intent and then decides to stay 15 days. According to Muhammad, he remains a traveler; according to Abu Hanifa, he becomes a resident.
This affects whether prayers are shortened or performed fully.
5
Apply to the Examples
Use the Cairene examples provided in the text to see how each position plays out in specific scenarios, such as travel from Bilbays to al-Salihiyya.
The examples are given based on the zahir al-riwayah.

الموضع الذي أنشأ منه السفر وبين ما صار إليه منه أي وبين الموضع الذي صار إليه من الموضع الأول ونوى فيه الإقامة، فقوله لو خرج تفريع على الشرط الأول ، وقوله وكذا إذا قصد «الخ تفريع على الشرط الثاني، قوله
