وجيه فإن من نوى الإقامة بموضع نصف شهر ثم خرج منه لا يريد السفر ثم عاد مريداً سفراً ومر بذلك أتم مع أنه أنشأ سفراً بعد اتخاذ هذا الموضع دار إقامة، فثبت أن إنشاء السفر لا يبطل وطن الإقامة إلا إذا أنشأ السفر منه فليكن وطن السكنى كذلك
He made it absolute, so he indicated that preceding travel is not a condition for establishing the original homeland and the homeland of residence. The original is by consensus, and regarding the homeland of residence there are two narrations: the apparent narration is that it is not a condition, and in another from Muhammad that a place only becomes a homeland of residence on the condition that travel precedes it and there be a travel distance between it and the place he came from. So if he left his city without the intention of travel and reached a village and intended to reside there for fifteen days, that village does not become a homeland of residence even if there is a travel distance between them due to the lack of preceding travel. Similarly, if he intended a travel distance and left, then when he reached a village whose distance from his homeland is less than a travel distance, he intended to reside there for fifteen days, he does not become a resident and that village does not become a homeland of residence. Example: a Cairene went to Bilbays and intended to reside there for half a month, then left it. If he intended a travel distance of three days and traveled, his homeland in Bilbays is nullified so that if he passes by it on his return he does not perform the full prayer. If he did not intend that and went to al-Salihiyya, then if he intended to reside there he performs the full prayer there and his homeland in Bilbays is nullified so that if he returns to it as a traveler he does not perform the full prayer. If he did not intend to reside there for half a month... even with him. His saying: (on condition that travel precedes it) with an implied addition, i.e., intention of travel, as indicated by what follows. The summary is that two things are required: first, the precedence of the intention of travel, and second, that there be a travel distance between it, i.e., between the place from which he initiated the travel and the place to which he came, i.e., between the place he came from the first place and where he intended to reside. So his saying 'if he left' is a branch of the first condition, and his saying 'similarly if he intended' is a branch of the second condition. His saying: 'the lack of preceding travel' — accordingly, if he left that village for a need then intended to return to his city and passed by that village, he shortens because he intended a travel distance and the village is not his homeland. His saying: 'example: a Cairene' — i.e., an example of the nullification of the homeland of residence by one of the three. So his saying 'if he intended' includes its nullification by travel, and his saying 'if he did not intend that' includes its nullification by its like, because what is between Bilbays and al-Salihiyya is less than the distance of qasr, as between Bilbays and Cairo. His saying 'if he returns to Cairo' includes its nullification by the original. His saying: 'such that he performs full prayer if he enters it' means if he left al-Salihiyya and wanted to return to Cairo and passed by Bilbays, he performs full prayer because his homeland there was not nullified by going to al-Salihiyya because it is not a similar homeland nor travel, so his homeland in Bilbays remains. All this illustration is based on the apparent narration of not requiring the precedence of travel for establishing the homeland of residence. In Fath al-Qadir and the narration of al-Hasan, i.e., this narration, it shows that the travel that nullifies the homeland of residence is that which does not involve passing over the homeland of residence, or passing over it after traveling the distance of travel. Therefore he performed full prayer in Bilbays in our issue with... between al-Salihiyya and Cairo is a travel distance because it involves passing over the homeland of residence. His saying: 'objectionable' — al-Ramli said: one may object because travel only nullifies the homeland of residence if he left it as a traveler, so also the homeland of residence, because travel is not connected to it. Contemplate. I saw it in the handwriting of some of them. I say: Sheikh Ibrahim al-Madari al-Halabi mentioned similar in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar from his teacher the researcher Sayyid Ali al-Darir, then said: it is sound, because one who intended residence in a place for half a month then left it without intending travel, then returned intending travel and passed by it, he performs full prayer even though he initiated travel after taking this place as a residence. So it is established that initiating travel does not nullify the homeland of residence unless he initiates travel from it. Let the homeland of residence be likewise.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key ruling regarding the conditions for establishing a watan al-iqama (residence that changes a traveler's status to resident). The author, Ibn Nujaym, is commenting on a statement from the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) that 'made it absolute' regarding the requirement of preceding travel. He clarifies that for watan al-asli (original homeland), there is no condition of preceding travel by consensus. However, for watan al-iqama, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to the zahir al-riwayah (the six major books of Imam Muhammad), preceding travel is NOT a condition. But in a riwaya from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, it IS a condition that travel precedes and that there is a travel distance (musafat al-qasr, approximately 48 miles or three days' journey) between the starting point and the residence. The passage then provides detailed examples with a Cairene traveling to Bilbays and al-Salihiyya to illustrate when the watan al-iqama is nullified. The discussion includes a critical refinement from al-Ramli and others regarding whether initiating travel after leaving a residence nullifies the watan al-iqama. The core point: the ruling depends on whether the travel was initiated from the residence itself or from elsewhere.

Key Terms
وطن الإقامة (watan al-iqama): A place where one intends to reside for 15 days or more, which changes the ruling of prayer from shortening to full, and nullifies a previous travel status.
تقديم السفر (taqdim al-safar): The condition that a travel (journey) precedes the establishment of a residence, specifically for watan al-iqama in Muhammad's riwaya.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known narration; the six core books of Imam Muhammad are considered the most authoritative within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, is preceding travel required to establish a watan al-iqama?
A) Yes, travel must precede the intention to reside.
B) No, preceding travel is not required.
C) It depends on the length of stay.
D) Only if the stay is less than 15 days.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is that a watan al-iqama is established by the intention to reside for 15 days, regardless of prior travel.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Make-Up Prayers: Travel vs. Residence
Ruling on how to make up prayers missed during travel and residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for making up prayers missed during travel versus residence and explain the principle 'al-qada bihasab al-ada'.

Core Idea
Make-up prayers mirror the state they were missed in – travel means 2, residence means 4.

Knowing how to make up a missed prayer depends on when it was missed, not when you make it up. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position through the rule 'al-qada bihasab al-ada'. A traveler who misses Zuhr must pray 2 rak'ahs, even if he later returns home.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on making up (qada) prayers missed during travel (safar) and residence (hadar). The ruling: missed travel prayers are made up as 2 rak'ahs; missed residence prayers as 4 rak'ahs (for Zuhr, Asr, Isha). Fajr and Maghrib are unchanged.
This covers the default: one rak'ah count difference.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the principle 'al-qada bihasab al-ada' (the make-up follows the performance). This is derived from qiyas on the Prophet's practice of shortening prayers during travel and the hadith 'Pray as you see me praying.'
The text mentions no explicit hadith but implies the qiyas.
3
Understand the principle
'Qada bihasab al-ada' means the form of the make-up prayer is determined by the state at the time the prayer was missed. If you missed it while traveling, you make it up as a traveler's prayer (shortened). If you missed it while resident, you make it up as a full prayer.
This is a Hanafi consensus; other schools may differ (e.g., Shafi'i makes it depend on the place of qada).
4
Note the exception (incomplete text)
The text ends with 'bikhilaf ma law fatahu fi...' indicating an exception: if the prayer was missed in a different state, etc. The complete commentary likely clarifies that if one misses a prayer while traveling but becomes resident before making it up, the travel form still applies.
The exception underscores the principle: the state at the time of the original obligation governs.
5
Apply the ruling
Apply to a concrete case: A traveler misses Zuhr. He must make it up as 2 rak'ahs regardless of when or where he later prays it. A resident who misses Zuhr makes it up as 4 rak'ahs.
No compensation (sajdah sahw) is needed for the change in rak'ahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا صلى وفائتة السفر والحضر تقضى ركعتين وأربعاً والمعتبر فيه آخر الوقت والعاصي قوله : (وفائتة السفر والحضر تقضى ركعتين وأربعاً لف ونشر مرتب أي فائتة السفر تقضى ركعتين وفائتة الحضر تقضى أربعاً لأن القضاء بحسب الأداء بخلاف ما لو فاتته في
And otherwise he prays, and the missed prayer of travel and residence are made up as two rak'ahs and four rak'ahs, and the consideration is the end of the time and the disobedient. His saying: (And the missed prayer of travel and residence are made up as two rak'ahs and four rak'ahs is a twisted and arranged form, i.e., the missed prayer of travel is made up as two rak'ahs and the missed prayer of residence is made up as four rak'ahs because the make-up is according to the performance, contrary to if it were missed in
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage provides a concise ruling on how to make up (qada) prayers that were missed during a specific time. The matn states: 'The missed prayer of travel and residence are made up as two rak'ahs and four rak'ahs.' The commentator explains that the phrase uses a literary device (laf wa nashr murattab) meaning that the missed prayer of travel is made up as two rak'ahs, and the missed prayer of residence as four rak'ahs. The proof given is 'because the make-up is according to the performance' (al-qada bihasab al-ada') – meaning the missed prayer must be prayed in the same form as it would have been performed at its proper time. So if one missed a prayer while traveling, it is made up as a shortened prayer (2 rak'ah for Zuhr, Asr, Isha; Maghrib and Fajr are unchanged). If one missed it while a resident, it is made up in full (4 rak'ah for Zuhr, Asr, Isha). The text also mentions 'the consideration is the end of the time' (al-mu'tabar fihi akhir al-waqt) which refers to another ruling about prayer of a traveler who enters residence during the time, etc. The incomplete fragment at the end likely contrasts the case of missing in travel versus residence.

Key Terms
فائتة السفر (fai'ta al-safar): A prayer that was missed (not performed) during the state of travel.
قضاء بحسب الأداء (qada bihasab al-ada): The principle that the make-up prayer must correspond to the form of the prayer at the time it was missed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What legal principle does the text use to justify that a missed travel prayer is made up as 2 rak'ahs?
A) Al-qada bihasab al-ada
B) Al-qada bihasab al-waqt
C) Al-umur bi-maqasidiha
D) Al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that make-up prayers are performed exactly as they would have been at their prescribed time: travel prayers are shortened, residence prayers are full.
